Biography of Imam al-Quduri: The Hanafi Jurist and His Students
Biographical entry on Imam al-Quduri with students

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts about Imam al-Quduri and identify his major students and their contributions.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri was a towering Hanafi jurist, likened to Abu Yusuf, and a teacher of great scholars.

This lesson introduces you to Imam al-Quduri, the author of the renowned Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. The passage also highlights two of his distinguished students, giving you a glimpse into the scholarly chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar and His Lineage
Read the first paragraph to determine who Imam al-Quduri is and what era he lived in.
Pay attention to his death year (478 AH).
2
Extract His Scholarly Attributes
Note the qualities mentioned and the comparison to Abu Yusuf.
The comparison emphasizes his dignity, intellect, and leadership.
3
List His Works
Identify the work mentioned by the author.
Only one work is explicitly named: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Hakim.
4
Examine the Students Mentioned
Read about Abu al-Harith al-Sarakhsi and al-Mufaddal al-Tanukhi, noting their achievements and what al-Quduri said about them.
Al-Sarakhsi was praised as the most knowledgeable from Khorasan; al-Tanukhi was a judge and grammarian.
5
Summarize the Scholarly Impact
Reflect on the significance of this biography for understanding the Hanafi madhhab's transmission.
The chain from al-Quduri to his students shows the continuity of Hanafi learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري

شيخ ابن عقيل الحنبلي، الإمام المشهور. وكان وافر العقل، كامل الفضل، سديد الرأي، عفيفاً نزيهاً، وكان يُنظّر بأبي يوسف القاضي حشمة وجاهاً وسؤدداً وعقلاً. ومن مصنفاته: شرح مختصر الحاكم في الفقه الحنفي، توفي رحمه الله سنة ٤٧٨هـ.

٦ ـ أبو الحارث محمد بن أبي الفضل محمد السرخسي، الإمام الفقيه الكبير، روي أنه ذكر عند شيخه الإمام القدوري، فقال عنه : «ما جاء من خراسان وعبر النهر أفقه منه». وهو من طبقة الدامغاني، ولم تذكر سنة وفاته.

المفضل بن مسعود بن محمد يحيى التنوخي القاضي الفقيه النحوي، تفقه على القدوري، وله عدة مصنفات، منها: أخبار النحويين، ورسالة في وجوب غسل الرّجلين، توفي سنة ٤٢٣هـ.
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri

Teacher of Ibn Aqeel al-Hanbali, the famous Imam. He was abundant in intellect, perfect in virtue, sound in opinion, chaste and honorable, and was likened to Abu Yusuf al-Qadi in dignity, prestige, leadership, and intellect. Among his works: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Hakim in Hanafi fiqh. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 478 AH.

6 – Abu al-Harith Muhammad ibn Abi al-Fadl Muhammad al-Sarakhsi, the great jurist. It is reported that he was mentioned before his teacher Imam al-Quduri, who said about him: 'No one has come from Khorasan and Transoxiana who is more learned in fiqh than him.' He is of the same class as al-Damghani, and his year of death is not mentioned.

Al-Mufaddal ibn Mas'ud ibn Muhammad Yahya al-Tanukhi, the judge, jurist, and grammarian. He studied fiqh under al-Quduri, and authored several works, including: Akhbar al-Nahwiyyin, and a treatise on the obligation of washing the feet. He died in the year 423 AH.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section introducing Imam al-Quduri, the author of the matn being commented upon. It highlights his intellectual virtues and compares him to Abu Yusuf, the famous student of Abu Hanifa. Al-Quduri's most notable work mentioned is 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Hakim' in Hanafi fiqh. He died in 478 AH. The passage then lists two of his prominent students: Abu al-Harith al-Sarakhsi, whom al-Quduri praised as the most knowledgeable from Khorasan and Transoxiana, and al-Mufaddal al-Tanukhi, a judge and grammarian who wrote on grammar and the obligation of washing the feet (a detail relevant to Hanafi fiqh on wudu).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which student of Imam al-Quduri wrote a treatise on the obligation of washing the feet?
A) Abu al-Harith al-Sarakhsi
B) Al-Mufaddal al-Tanukhi
C) Ibn Aqeel
D) Al-Damghani

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri was a pivotal Hanafi scholar, and his students continued his legacy of fiqh and grammar.

Understanding Scholarly Praise: Al-Quduri's 'Saduq'
Compilation of scholarly acclaim with clarification of terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's use of 'saduq' for al-Quduri is not a downgrade but a praise, and identify the importance of distinguishing technical hadith terminology from ordinary usage in biographical evaluations.

Core Idea
Scholars praised al-Quduri as 'saduq' — the intensive form of truthfulness, not the technical hadith grade.

This passage collects the unanimous acclaim for Imam al-Quduri and clarifies a key point about a word that could be misunderstood. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, a renowned hadith scholar and historian, called al-Quduri 'saduq'. Without context, a student of hadith might think this indicates a flaw, but the author explains that al-Khatib meant the intensive 'very truthful', not the technical rank. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly reading classical biographies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Claim
The passage begins by asserting that all biographers agree on al-Quduri's leadership of the Hanafis and their unanimous praise of him. Recognize this consensus as the foundation for the discussion.
Consensus (ijma) here is not a legal one but a historical agreement among scholars.
2
Locate the Quoted Testimony
Find the direct quote from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. He says: 'He only narrated a little, and I wrote from him. He was extremely truthful, and he was among those who excelled in fiqh due to his intelligence...' Note the key phrase 'saduqan'.
Al-Khatib himself wrote from al-Quduri, which shows he trusted his transmissions.
3
Analyze the Critical Term
Examine the term 'saduq'. In hadith criticism (jarh wa ta'dil), 'saduq' means 'truthful' but below 'thiqah'. However, the author argues that al-Khatib used it as an intensive form (صيغة المبالغة) meaning 'very truthful', not the technical grade. Why does the author say this? Look at the context: al-Khatib praises al-Quduri's excellence in fiqh and his high status, which suggests he is not downgrading him.
The author also parallels Ibn Abi Hatim's description of Imam al-Shafi'i as 'saduq' in a similar non-technical sense.
4
Compare with Another Example
The author compares al-Khatib's usage with Ibn Abi Hatim's description of Imam al-Shafi'i: 'فقيه البدن، صدوق'. Both are founders of schools (madhhab), and both are called 'saduq' by major hadith critics. This parallel reinforces that the word is used to emphasize truthfulness, not to grade their hadith.
Al-Shafi'i was not primarily a hadith transmitter, so the technical term would be inappropriate.
5
Synthesize the Significance
Understand why this distinction matters: if we misinterpret 'saduq' as a technical downgrade, we might wrongly doubt al-Quduri's reliability as a narrator and scholar. The author's clarification protects his reputation and teaches a methodological lesson: always consider context and intention when reading technical terms in biographical literature.
This is a lesson in usul al-hadith methodology applied to fiqh history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثاني
مكانة القدوري العلمية وثناء العلماء عليه

اتفق كل من ترجم للإمام القدوري على أنه كان شيخ الحنفية، ورئيساً لهم في زمانه، كما أجمعوا على الثناء عليه، وأنه كان ثقة صدوقاً، بل كلهم نَقَلَ في ترجمته كلمة تلميذه الخطيب البغدادي (ت٤٦٣ هـ) فيه، حيث أثنى عليه بقوله :

لم يحدث إلا بشيء يسير، وقد كتبتُ عنه، وكان صدوقاً، وكان ممن أنجب في الفقه لذكائه، وانتهت إليه بالعراق رئاسة أصحاب أبي حنيفة، وعظم عندهم قَدْرُه ، وارتفع جاهه (۱).

وأراد الخطيب البغدادي بقوله : (صدوقاً): أراد صيغة المبالغة، ولم يُرد المعنى الاصطلاحي عند علماء الجرح والتعديل، مـن أنـه أدنى من الثقة، وأن حديثه حَسَن ، وهذا كما وصف ابن أبي حاتم
الإمام الشافعي صاحب المذهب ، بقوله: «فقيه البدن، صدوق».
Second Section: Al-Quduri's Scholarly Status and Scholars' Praise of Him

All who have written a biography of Imam al-Quduri agree that he was the shaykh of the Hanafis and their leader in his time. They also unanimously praise him, stating that he was trustworthy and extremely truthful. Indeed, they all transmit in his biography the words of his student al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (d. 463 AH) about him, who praised him saying:

'He only narrated a little, and I wrote from him. He was extremely truthful, and he was among those who excelled in fiqh due to his intelligence. The leadership of the followers of Abu Hanifa in Iraq ended with him, and he was greatly esteemed and honored among them.'

By his saying 'extremely truthful' (saduqan), al-Khatib al-Baghdadi intended the intensive form, not the technical meaning according to the scholars of jarh wa ta'dil (that he is below 'trustworthy' and his hadith is hasan). This is similar to how Ibn Abi Hatim described Imam al-Shafi'i, the founder of the school, saying: 'He was a jurist in his constitution, extremely truthful.'
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section that compiles the unanimous praise of Imam al-Quduri by later scholars. It emphasizes that he was the undisputed head of the Hanafi school in Iraq. The author quotes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, a famous hadith scholar and historian, who called al-Quduri 'saduq' (extremely truthful). The author then clarifies that al-Khatib used 'saduq' in its literal intensive sense ('very truthful'), not in the technical hadith criticism sense where 'saduq' indicates a level below 'thiqah' (trustworthy). He draws a parallel with Ibn Abi Hatim's description of Imam al-Shafi'i as 'saduq', which similarly was not meant to downgrade his reliability but to praise his truthfulness. This clarification is important to prevent misunderstanding about al-Quduri's status as a narrator.

Key Terms
صدوق (saduq): In this text, the term is used in its literal intensive sense meaning 'very truthful', not the technical hadith criticism term meaning 'below thiqah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author clarify about al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's use of the word 'saduqan' for al-Quduri?
A) That it means al-Quduri was not fully trustworthy
B) That it is the technical hadith term meaning 'acceptable'
C) That it is the intensive form meaning 'very truthful', not the technical term
D) That it implies al-Quduri narrated only a little

Key Takeaway
The term 'saduq' in classical biographical notes can be used as an intensive praise, not necessarily the technical hadith grade; context is crucial.

The Scholarly Status of Imam al-Quduri: Consensus and Praise
Biographical eulogy with linguistic clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of Imam al-Quduri's scholarly status and explain why the term 'sadduq' in his biography is not a technical hadith classification.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri was the undisputed leader of the Hanafi school in Iraq, praised by all as a 'roaring sea in fiqh'.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri presents the unanimous praise of scholars for Imam al-Quduri. It also clarifies an important linguistic point: when al-Khatib al-Baghdadi called him 'sadduq', he meant 'very truthful' in a general sense, not a technical assessment of his hadith narration. Understanding this distinction protects against misinterpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus
Read the opening statement: all biographers agree that al-Quduri was the foremost Hanafi scholar (Shaykh al-Hanafiyya) and his time's leader. This establishes his authority.
2
Examine al-Khatib's testimony
Focus on the quote from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. Note the description 'sadduq' (truthful) and the mention of his intelligence and leadership.
3
Distinguish lexical from technical meaning
The author explicitly clarifies that al-Khatib used 'sadduq' as an intensive form (صيغة المبالغة) meaning 'very truthful', not the technical jarh wa ta'dil term. Compare with how Ibn Abi Hatim described Imam al-Shafi'i similarly.
4
Analyze later scholars' praises
Read the quotes from al-Itqani (bahr zakhkhar), al-Qurashi (eloquence, Quran recitation), and Ibn Kathir (eminent imam, reliable debater). Extract the qualities they highlight.
5
Synthesize the portrait
Combine all praises: leadership, intelligence, vast fiqh knowledge, hadith expertise, eloquence, piety, and authorship of the Mukhtasar.
This biography shows why al-Quduri's works, especially al-Mukhtasar, carry great authority.

الفصل الأول: ترجمة الإمام القدوري
المبحث الثاني
مكانة القدوري العلمية وثناء العلماء عليه

اتفق كل من ترجم للإمام القدوري على أنه كان شيخ الحنفية، ورئيساً لهم في زمانه، كما أجمعوا على الثناء عليه، وأنه كان ثقة صدوقاً، بل كلهم نَقَلَ في ترجمته كلمة تلميذه الخطيب البغدادي (ت٤٦٣ هـ) فيه، حيث أثنى عليه بقوله :
لم يحدث إلا بشيء يسير، وقد كتبتُ عنه، وكان صدوقاً، وكان ممن أنجب في الفقه لذكائه، وانتهت إليه بالعراق رئاسة أصحاب أبي حنيفة، وعظم عندهم قَدْرُه ، وارتفع جاهه (۱).
وأراد الخطيب البغدادي بقوله : (صدوقاً): أراد صيغة المبالغة، ولم يُرد المعنى الاصطلاحي عند علماء الجرح والتعديل، مـن أنـه أدنى من الثقة، وأن حديثه حَسَن ، وهذا كما وصف ابن أبي حاتم (۲) الإمام الشافعي صاحب المذهب ، بقوله: «فقيه البدن، صدوق»،

(۲) مناقب الشافعي لابن أبي حاتم . ص ۸۹، بتحقيق عبد الغني عبد الخالق،

وقال الإمام أمير كاتب الإتقاني الأترازي (ت٧٥١هـ)،
صاحب غاية البيان شرح الهداية(۱):

First Chapter: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Second Section: The Scholarly Status of al-Quduri and the Praise of Scholars for Him

Everyone who wrote a biography of Imam al-Quduri agreed that he was the foremost Hanafi scholar and their leader in his time, and they unanimously praised him, stating that he was trustworthy (thiqa) and truthful (sadduq). Indeed, all of them transmitted in his biography the words of his student al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (d. 463 AH) concerning him, where he praised him saying: 'He only narrated a few things, and I wrote from him, and he was truthful (sadduq). He was among those who excelled in fiqh due to his intelligence, and the leadership of the followers of Abu Hanifa in Iraq came to him, and his status became great among them, and his honor elevated.' (1)
And al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, by his saying 'sadduq', intended the intensive form, and did not intend the technical meaning according to the scholars of jarh wa ta'dil [criticism and validation], that it is less than trustworthy (thiqa) and that his hadith is hasan. This is similar to how Ibn Abi Hatim (2) described Imam al-Shafi'i, the founder of the [Shafi'i] school, saying: 'He was a jurist of sound body, truthful (sadduq).'
(1) Tarikh Baghdad 4/377, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 17/575, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 1/248; see also al-Nujum al-Zahira by Ibn Taghribirdi 5/27, and the severe remarks made against al-Khatib al-Baghdadi.
(2) Manaqib al-Shafi'i by Ibn Abi Hatim, p. 89, edited by 'Abd al-Ghani 'Abd al-Khaliq.

First Chapter: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
And he did not intend the technical meaning of the muhaddithun.
And Imam Amir Katib al-Itqani al-Atrazi (d. 751 AH), author of Ghayat al-Bayan Sharh al-Hidaya, said:
'And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, is a roaring sea in fiqh, and a pouring rain in hadith. Sufficient as evidence of the abundance of his knowledge is his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, may Allah have mercy on him. If you read it, you will know that his rank in fiqh was at the star Capella, which the hand of everyone cannot reach, and the eye of the beholder turns back from his station due to exhaustion and eye-sore.' End quote.
(2)
In
And Imam al-Qurashi (d. 775 AH) said in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya (3): 'Al-Quduri was eloquent in speech in discussion, fluent in tongue, and constantly reciting the Quran.' End quote.
(E).
And Imam Ibn Kathir (d. 774 AH) said in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya (4): 'He was an eminent imam, a scholar, a reliable debater, and he is the author of the Mukhtasar.'
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, presenting the unanimous praise of biographers for Imam al-Quduri's leadership in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that all scholars who wrote his biography agree he was the leading Hanafi scholar of his time and a trustworthy person. The passage then quotes his student al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who emphasizes that al-Quduri was 'truthful' (sadduq) and intelligent, and that he became the head of Abu Hanifa's followers in Iraq. The author clarifies that al-Khatib used 'sadduq' in its lexical intensive sense (صيغة المبالغة), not as a technical term of hadith criticism where 'sadduq' ranks below 'thiqa'. This is analogous to how Ibn Abi Hatim described Imam al-Shafi'i as 'sadduq'. The passage then cites further praises: al-Itqani (al-Atrazi) compares al-Quduri to a 'roaring sea in fiqh' and a 'pouring rain in hadith', pointing to his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi as proof of his vast knowledge. Al-Qurashi (in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya) notes his eloquence and constant Quran recitation. Finally, Ibn Kathir calls him an eminent imam, scholar, and reliable debater, and identifies him as the author of the famous Mukhtasar (al-Quduri).

Key Terms
شيخ الحنفية (Shaykh al-Hanafiyya): The foremost authority and leader of the Hanafi school.
صدوق (sadduq): Used here in its intensive lexical sense meaning 'very truthful', not the technical hadith term meaning a reliable narrator below the level of thiqa.
ثقة (thiqa): Trustworthy; a higher level of reliability in hadith narration.
بحر زخار (bahr zakhkhar): Metaphor for immense knowledge, like a roaring sea.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Khatib al-Baghdadi mean by describing Imam al-Quduri as 'sadduq'?
A) That he was a hadith narrator of the 'hasan' level according to jarh wa ta'dil
B) That he was very truthful, using the intensive form of the word
C) That he was a companion of the Prophet
D) That he was a weak narrator

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's biography confirms his unparalleled authority in Hanafi fiqh, and his praise as 'sadduq' was a lexical intensifier, not a technical hadith rating.

Imam al-Quduri: Scholar and Debater
Biographical introduction with scholarly encomiums

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam al-Quduri and explain why his scholarly credentials in both fiqh and hadith lend authority to his Mukhtasar.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri was not only a Hanafi jurist but also a hadith master and skilled debater.

In this lesson, we explore the life and scholarly stature of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, the author of one of the most widely studied Hanafi texts. Understanding his biography helps us appreciate the weight of his rulings and the confidence later scholars placed in his work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the figure
Who is Imam al-Quduri? Note his full name, era (362-428 AH), and his major work Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
He is a central figure in the Hanafi madhhab.
2
Recognize the praise
Read the comments by al-Itqani, al-Qurashi, Ibn Kathir, and Ibn Taghridi. What aspects do they highlight?
Focus on fiqh mastery, hadith knowledge, eloquence, and debates.
3
Understand his hadith activity
While he sought hadith extensively, he narrated only a little. This shows his caution in transmission.
Al-Dhahabi counted him among the hadith memorizers (huffaz).
4
Appreciate the debate culture
The passage mentions his scholarly debates with contemporaries, conducted with mutual respect. This reflects the Hanafi tradition of rigorous yet ethical discourse.
Such debates were part of the process of legal reasoning.

الفصل الأول: ترجمة الإمام القدوري
ولم يُرد المعنى الاصطلاحي عند المحدثين.
وقال الإمام أمير كاتب الإتقاني الأترازي (ت٧٥١هـ)، صاحب غاية البيان شرح الهداية:
والشيخ أبو الحسن القدوري رحمه الله هو بحر زخار في الفقه، وغَيْث مدرار في الحديث، وناهيك من الدلالة على غزارة علمه: شرحه لمختصر الكرخي رحمه الله ، فإذا طالعته عرفت أن محله الفقه كان عند العيوق () ، لا تناله يد كل أحد، ويرجع طـرف الـنـاظر إلى منزله من كَلالِ ورَمَد». اهـ
وقال الإمام القرشي (ت ٧٧٥هـ) في الجواهر المضية: كان القدوري حَسَن العبارة في النظر، جري اللسان، مديماً لتلاوة القرآن». اهـ
وقال الإمام ابن كثير (ت) ٧٧٤هـ) في البداية والنهاية: كان إماماً بارعاً عالماً ، وثَبْتاً مناظراً ، ... وهو صاحب المختصر الذي يُحفظ». اهـ
وقال الإمام يوسف بن تغري بردي (ت ٨٧٤هـ): هو الإمام العلامة .... وإن شأن هذا الإمام قد تجاوز الحد في العلم والزهد». اهـ
وكان للقدوري اهتمام بالغ بطلب الحديث وسماعه، لكنه لم يحدث إلا بشيء يسير، وقد روى عنه الحديث تلامذته، مثـل الخطيب البغدادي، وغيره، وقد عده الذهبي مـن حفاظ الحديث، فترجم له في تذكرة الحفاظ.
وعن مروياته يقول الإمام القرشي: «ووقع لي جزء من حديثه، رواية قاضي القضاة أبي عبد الله الدامغاني، أخبرنا بجميعه المسندان المعمران الإمامان...». اهـ، وساق السند.
مناظرات القدوري مع علماء عصره :
كانت للإمام القدوري مجالس علمية عامرة تجري فيها مناظرات علمية بارزة بينه وبين بعض أئمة عصره، كل يُبدي فيها حُجَجه وأدلته على قوله الذي توصل إليه وتبنّاه مع كل محبة واحترام وأدب بين الطرفين.
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. He did not intend the technical meaning according to the hadith scholars. Imam Amir Katib al-Itqani al-Atrazi (d. 751 AH), author of Ghayat al-Bayan Sharh al-Hidayah, said: 'Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, is an overflowing sea in fiqh, a pouring rain in hadith, and sufficient proof of the abundance of his knowledge is his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. If you examine it, you will know that his station in fiqh was at the [height of] Capella, unattainable by just anyone, and the eye of the beholder turns back from his station in exhaustion and soreness.' Imam al-Qurashi (d. 775 AH) said in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya: 'Al-Quduri was excellent in expression in discussion, fluent in tongue, and constant in reciting the Qur'an.' Imam Ibn Kathir (d. 774 AH) said in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya: 'He was a distinguished, knowledgeable imam, a reliable debater... and he is the author of al-Mukhtasar that is memorized.' Imam Yusuf ibn Taghridi (d. 874 AH) said: 'He is the imam, the scholar... and indeed the station of this imam has exceeded the limits in knowledge and asceticism.' Al-Quduri had great interest in seeking and listening to hadith, but he only narrated a little. His students, such as al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and others, narrated hadith from him. Al-Dhahabi counted him among the hadith memorizers and included his biography in Tadhkirat al-Huffaz. Regarding his narrated texts, Imam al-Qurashi said: 'I obtained a portion of his hadith, narrated by the Chief Judge Abu Abd Allah al-Damaghani; we were informed of all of it by the two reliable, long-lived imams...' and he traced the chain. Debates of al-Quduri with the scholars of his time: Imam al-Quduri had flourishing scholarly gatherings in which notable debates took place between him and some scholars of his time, each presenting his proofs and evidence for his conclusion and adopted view, with mutual love, respect, and etiquette between the parties.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, the author of the celebrated Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri (also known as al-Mukhtasar). The passage begins by clarifying that al-Quduri's biography is presented here not in the technical sense of the hadith scholars but as an introduction. Several prominent scholars praise al-Quduri's profound knowledge in both fiqh and hadith. Amir Katib al-Itqani describes him as an 'overflowing sea in fiqh' and a 'pouring rain in hadith,' emphasizing his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi as a testament to his mastery. Al-Qurashi highlights his eloquence and frequent recitation of the Qur'an. Ibn Kathir calls him a distinguished imam and reliable debater, noting that his Mukhtasar is widely memorized. Ibn Taghridi exalts his knowledge and asceticism. The passage also underscores al-Quduri's dedication to hadith acquisition, though he narrated little; his students transmitted from him, and al-Dhahabi regarded him as a hadith memorizer. Finally, it mentions his dynamic scholarly debates conducted with mutual respect, reflecting the ethical scholarly tradition. This introduction establishes the authority of the author whose work is being commented upon.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (362-428 AH), a leading Hanafi jurist and author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مناظرات (munazarat): Scholarly debates where each party presents proofs and evidence for their positions, conducted with etiquette and respect.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's dual expertise in fiqh and hadith, combined with his ethical debating practice, establishes his authority as a foundational Hanafi scholar.

Imam al-Quduri: The Hanafi Jurist and His Scholarly Debates
Biographical sketch with introduction to scholarly debates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly stature of Imam al-Quduri and identify the nature of his debates with Shafi'i scholars.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri combined Hanafi jurisprudence with hadith scholarship and engaged in respectful inter-madhhab debate.

This lesson introduces you to Imam al-Quduri, the author of the Mukhtasar that forms the basis of this commentary. Beyond his juristic work, he was a hadith scholar and an active participant in scholarly debates with imams of other schools, particularly the Shafi'is. This biographical background helps us appreciate the authority and scholarly environment from which the Mukhtasar emerged.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Quduri's full name and death date
From the passage, note that al-Quduri is Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, who died in 428 AH. This places him in the 5th century of hijra.
2
Recognize his dual competence: fiqh and hadith
The passage notes that al-Quduri sought and heard hadith, though he narrated little. He was considered a hadith preserver by al-Dhahabi. This shows he was not only a jurist but also a muhaddith.
3
Understand the nature of his debates
The debates were conducted with mutual love, respect, and decorum. Each scholar presented proofs for his position. This reflects the adab of ikhtilaf in classical scholarship.
The passage gives an example: a debate with Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari on whether a woman divorced by khul' can be affected by subsequent divorce during her iddah.
4
Identify the Shafi'i opponents
The two Shafi'i imams mentioned are Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari and Abu Hamid al-Isfrayini. Note that Abu Hamid was highly regarded by al-Quduri.

هو الإمام العلامة .... وإن شأن هذا الإمام قد تجاوز الحد في العلم والزهد». اهـ
وكان للقدوري اهتمام بالغ بطلب الحديث وسماعه، لكنه لم يحدث إلا بشيء يسير، وقد روى عنه الحديث تلامذته، مثـل الخطيب البغدادي، وغيره، وقد عده الذهبي مـن حفاظ الحديث، فترجم له في تذكرة الحفاظ (٢).
وعن مروياته يقول الإمام القرشي(۳): «ووقع لي جزء من حديثه، رواية قاضي القضاة أبي عبد الله الدامغاني، أخبرنا بجميعه المسندان المعمران الإمامان...». اهـ، وساق السند.

كانت للإمام القدوري مجالس علمية عامرة تجري فيها مناظرات علمية بارزة بينه وبين بعض أئمة عصره، كل يُبدي فيها حُجَجه وأدلته على قوله الذي توصل إليه وتبنّاه مع كل محبة واحترام وأدب بين الطرفين.
ومن تلك المجالس المنوّرة بالعلم، المزيَّنة بالأدب، مناظرات كانت تُعقد بين الإمام القدوري والإمامين أبي الطيب الطبري الشافعي وأبي حامد الإسفراييني الشافعي وكانت لأبي حامد مكانة كبيرة عند القدوري وقد ذكر الإمام السبكي في طبقاته (۲)، في ترجمة القاضي أبي الطيب الطبري، نص مناظرة كانت بين الإمام القدوري الحنفي والإمام أبي الطيب الشافعي في مسألة : هل يلحق المختلعة حال عدتها الطلاق أم لا؟ فالقدوري يدلل على أنه يلحقها، وأبو الطيـب يـدلل علـى عـدم لحوقها، وقد جاء نص المناظرة في عشر صفحات باستعراض شافعي.
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. 'He who memorizes...' end quote. Imam Yusuf ibn Taghribirdi (d. 874 AH) said: 'He is the Imam, the scholar... and indeed the status of this Imam has exceeded the limit in knowledge and asceticism.' End quote. Al-Quduri had great interest in seeking and hearing hadith, but he narrated only a little. His students narrated hadith from him, such as al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and others. Al-Dhahabi counted him among the preservers of hadith and wrote his biography in Tadhkirat al-Huffaz. Regarding his narrations, Imam al-Qurashi said: 'A part of his hadith came to me, transmitted by the chief judge Abu Abdullah al-Damaghani, informed to us by the two trustworthy senior imams...' end quote, and he narrated the chain. Debates of al-Quduri with the scholars of his time: Imam al-Quduri had flourishing scholarly gatherings in which prominent scholarly debates took place between him and some of the imams of his time, each presenting his proofs and evidence for the opinion he had reached and adopted, with mutual love, respect, and decorum. Among those gatherings illuminated by knowledge and adorned with etiquette were debates held between Imam al-Quduri and the two imams Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari al-Shafi'i and Abu Hamid al-Isfrayini al-Shafi'i. Abu Hamid held a great status in al-Quduri's view. Imam al-Subki mentioned in his Tabaqat, in the biography of Judge Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, the text of a debate between Imam al-Quduri al-Hanafi and Imam Abu al-Tayyib al-Shafi'i on the issue: 'Does divorce affect a woman who has been divorced by khul' during her waiting period or not?' Al-Quduri argued that it does affect her, while Abu al-Tayyib argued that it does not. The text of the debate, presenting the Shafi'i view, spans ten pages.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the Mukhtasar (the matn being commented upon by al-Maydani in al-Lubab). It highlights his high status as a Hanafi jurist and hadith scholar, despite his limited hadith narration. It also introduces his famous debates with Shafi'i scholars, specifically one on whether a divorced woman (by khul') is subject to divorce during her waiting period. This biographical information sets the stage for the commentary, showing the scholarly context of the author.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the Hanafi jurist and author of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
المناظرات (al-munazarat): Scholarly debates where each party presents proofs for their positions, conducted with mutual respect.
المختلعة (al-mukhtali'ah): A woman who obtains a divorce by khul' (redemption), i.e., she pays compensation to her husband to secure her release.

Imam al-Quduri and His Scholarly Legacy
Biographical and bibliographic introduction to Imam al-Quduri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and structure of Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and identify its place in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar: 12,000 rulings without proofs — a master key to Hanafi fiqh.

Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) was a towering Hanafi jurist. He is best known for his concise work, al-Mukhtasar, which encapsulates the core rulings of the Hanafi school. This lesson explores his life, his scholarly debates, and the pedagogical genius behind his writings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key works
Locate in the passage the names of al-Quduri's major books: al-Mukhtasar and al-Tajrid. Note their distinct purposes – one for quick reference, the other for detailed evidence.
Al-Mukhtasar contains 12,000 issues; al-Tajrid covers differences between Hanafis and Shafi'is in 12 volumes.
2
Understand the Mukhtasar's function
The passage explains that al-Mukhtasar is for those who want to act on rulings without delving into proofs. It states it contains 'the essence and fruit of Hanafi fiqh' and is 'devoid of evidences'.
This makes it a practical primer, not a theoretical treatise.
3
Contrast with al-Tajrid
The passage notes that al-Tajrid is a large work specifically for those who want 'elaboration and aspects of evidence' on the branches of fiqh. It deals with khilaf (disagreements) between schools.
Al-Tajrid thus serves a different audience – advanced students and scholars.
4
Appreciate the debate context
The passage mentions a debate between al-Quduri and Shafi'i scholars on whether talaq can affect a mukhalla'a during her 'iddah. This illustrates the interactive nature of fiqh discourse and al-Quduri's role as a defender of Hanafi positions.
The debate is recorded in ten pages in al-Subki's Tabaqat.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري
ومن تلك المجالس المنوّرة بالعلم، المزيَّنة بالأدب، مناظرات كانت تُعقد بين الإمام القدوري والإمامين أبي الطيب الطبري الشافعي وأبي حامد الإسفراييني الشافعي وكانت لأبي حامد مكانة كبيرة عند القدوري وقد ذكر الإمام السبكي في طبقاته (۲)، في ترجمة القاضي أبي الطيب الطبري، نص مناظرة كانت بين الإمام القدوري الحنفي والإمام أبي الطيب الشافعي في مسألة : هل يلحق المختلعة حال عدتها الطلاق أم لا؟ فالقدوري يدلل على أنه يلحقها، وأبو الطيـب يـدلل علـى عـدم لحوقها، وقد جاء نص المناظرة في عشر صفحات باستعراض شافعي.

المبحث الثالث
مصنفات الإمام القدوري
لقد بارك الله تعالى في جهود الإمام القدوري، وأعماله العلمية، حيث صنف عدة كتب كبار في خلاف الفقهاء وأدلتهم، تدل على إمامته وبراعته في علم الفقه والحديث وغيرهما.
كما أنه ألف مختصره المشهور في الفقه الحنفي، الذي وضع فيـه زبدة الفقه الحنفي وثمرته، وغالب رؤوس مسائله الفقهية، خالياً مـن الأدلة، فمن أراد العمل، ومعرفة الحكم دون الخوض في الأدلة والمناقشات، فعليه بالمختصر، ففيه غُنية عظمى، وكفاية كبرى، إذ حوى هذا المختصر اثنتا عشرة ألف مسألة فقهية، ومن أراد بسط ووجوه الدلالة على تلك الفروع والمسائل، فعليه بكتبه الأدلة، الكبيرة التي خصها لذلك.
بقوله :
وفيما يلي أذكر ما وقفتُ عليه من كتبه، مع بيان حالها ومزاياها:
١ - التجريد في مسائل الخلاف بين الحنفية والشافعية : وهو مطبوع محقق في (۱۲) مجلداً، وقد وصفه الإمام القرشي
والتجريد في سبعة أسفار اشتمل على مسائل الخلاف بين
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. Among those assemblies illuminated by knowledge, adorned with literature, were debates held between Imam al-Quduri and the two Imams Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari al-Shafi'i and Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini al-Shafi'i. Abu Hamid had a great status with al-Quduri. Imam al-Subki mentioned in his Tabaqat (2), in the biography of Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, the text of a debate between Imam al-Quduri al-Hanafi and Imam Abu al-Tayyib al-Shafi'i on the issue: Does divorce (talaq) affect the mukhalla'a (woman who obtained khul') during her 'iddah or not? Al-Quduri argued that it does affect her, and Abu al-Tayyib argued that it does not. The text of the debate appears in ten pages with a Shafi'i review.

Third Section: Works of Imam al-Quduri. Allah Almighty blessed the efforts of Imam al-Quduri and his scholarly works. He authored several major books on the differences among jurists and their evidences, indicating his imamate and skill in fiqh, hadith, and other sciences.
He also authored his famous Mukhtasar in Hanafi fiqh, in which he placed the essence and fruit of Hanafi fiqh, and most of its principal issues, devoid of evidences. So whoever desires action and knowledge of the ruling without delving into evidences and discussions, he should refer to the Mukhtasar, for it contains great sufficiency and large capability. Indeed, this Mukhtasar contains twelve thousand fiqh issues. And whoever desires elaboration and aspects of evidence on those branches and issues, he should refer to his large books of evidences that he dedicated for that.
He said: In the following I mention what I have come across of his books, with explanation of their condition and merits:
1. Al-Tajrid fi Masa'il al-Khilaf bayna al-Hanafiyyah wa al-Shafi'iyyah: It is printed and edited in (12) volumes. Imam al-Qurashi described it as: "Al-Tajrid in seven volumes containing issues of disagreement between"
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction from 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. It first discusses Imam al-Quduri's scholarly engagements, highlighting a famous debate with the Shafi'i scholar Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari on whether a divorced woman who obtains khul' (mukhalla'a) can be affected by another divorce during her 'iddah period. Al-Quduri held that it does attach, while Abu al-Tayyib disagreed. This shows the interactive nature of Hanafi-Shafi'i discourse. Then the passage details al-Quduri's major works, especially his concise Mukhtasar, which is a foundational text in the Hanafi school containing 12,000 issues without evidences, and his detailed work 'Al-Tajrid' which covers differences between Hanafis and Shafi'is. This structure - a concise primer and a detailed comparative work - reflects the pedagogical approach of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المختلعة (al-mukhalla'ah): A woman who obtains khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation).
الطلاق (al-talaq): Divorce. A husband's pronouncement ending the marriage. In this context, whether it can be validly issued to a mukhalla'a during her waiting period.
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying. For a divorced woman, three menstrual cycles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 12

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh, providing a concise summary of 12,000 rulings for practical application, while his al-Tajrid details the proofs and disagreements.

Imam al-Quduri's Works: Al-Mukhtasar and Al-Tajrid
Biographical overview of al-Quduri's writings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main works of Imam al-Quduri, describe their distinct purposes and contents, and identify the appropriate work for a given scholarly need.

Core Idea
Al-Mukhtasar gives twelve thousand rulings without proof; al-Tajrid argues Hanafi positions against Shafi'i objections.

Imam al-Quduri authored works that serve different levels of fiqh study. His Mukhtasar is a concise reference for daily practice, while al-Tajrid is a scholarly work of dispute (khilaf) providing evidence and preference. Knowing which work to use is essential for effective learning and research in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Works
Read the passage and note the two books named: al-Mukhtasar and al-Tajrid. Translate each into Arabic (المختصر and التجريد).
2
Describe the Purpose of Each
Al-Mukhtasar summarizes core Hanafi rulings in 12,000 issues without evidences, meant for practitioners. Al-Tajrid presents disputed issues between Hanafis and Shafi'is with tarjih (preference), suitable for advanced study of khilaf.
Contrast the target audience: 'whoever wants to practice' vs. 'whoever wants elaboration and aspects of indication'.
3
Recognize Scholarly Praise
The passage quotes al-Qurashi, Ibn Taghribirdi, Kashf al-Zunun, and al-Kawthari. Ibn Taghribirdi highlights al-Quduri's memory of al-Daraqutni's hadiths. Kashf al-Zunun notes the concise style and inclusion of tarjih.
These citations establish the authority and utility of al-Tajrid.
4
Note the Date and Origins
Al-Quduri began dictating al-Tajrid on 23 Dhu al-Qa'dah 405 AH. The introduction includes a supplication. This historical detail helps contextualize the work.
5
Apply the Knowledge
Given a scenario (e.g., a beginner wanting to know prayer rulings, or a researcher comparing Hanafi/Shafi'i views on sale), choose the appropriate work and justify.
Example: Mukhtasar for daily fiqh; Tajrid for khilaf analysis.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري
٢٩٥
المبحث الثالث
مصنفات الإمام القدوري
لقد بارك الله تعالى في جهود الإمام القدوري، وأعماله العلمية، حيث صنف عدة كتب كبار في خلاف الفقهاء وأدلتهم، تدل على إمامته وبراعته في علم الفقه والحديث وغيرهما.
كما أنه ألف مختصره المشهور في الفقه الحنفي، الذي وضع فيـه زبدة الفقه الحنفي وثمرته، وغالب رؤوس مسائله الفقهية، خالياً مـن الأدلة، فمن أراد العمل، ومعرفة الحكم دون الخوض في الأدلة والمناقشات، فعليه بالمختصر، ففيه غُنية عظمى، وكفاية كبرى، إذ حوى هذا المختصر اثنتا عشرة ألف مسألة فقهية، ومن أراد بسط ووجوه الدلالة على تلك الفروع والمسائل، فعليه بكتبه الأدلة، الكبيرة التي خصها لذلك.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
295
Third Section: The Writings of Imam al-Quduri
Allah the Exalted has blessed the efforts of Imam al-Quduri and his scholarly works. He authored several major books on the differences among jurists and their evidences, indicating his imamate and brilliance in the knowledge of fiqh, hadith, and other fields.
He also wrote his famous Mukhtasar (abridgement) in Hanafi fiqh, in which he placed the essence of Hanafi fiqh and its fruit, and most of its major legal issues, free from evidences. So whoever wants to practice and know the ruling without delving into evidences and discussions should rely on this Mukhtasar, for it is a great sufficiency and a large enough coverage. Indeed, this Mukhtasar contains twelve thousand fiqh issues. And whoever wants elaboration and aspects of indication on those branches and issues should refer to his books on evidences, the large ones which he dedicated for that.
He said:
Below I mention what I have come across of his books, along with explaining their status and merits:
1 - Al-Tajrid on issues of dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is: It is printed and verified in 12 volumes. Imam al-Qurashi described it: "Al-Tajrid in seven volumes contains the issues of dispute between our colleagues and the Shafi'is. He began dictating it in the year 405 AH." End quote. Imam Ibn Taghribirdi (d. 874 AH) said in praise of al-Tajrid:
"He dictated al-Tajrid on the matters of difference, and in it he demonstrated his memory of what al-Daraqutni had of hadiths on rulings and their defects." End quote.
The author of Kashf al-Zunun said about it: "Al-Tajrid by Imam al-Quduri in one large volume. In it he singled out the issues in which al-Shafi'i differed, with concise wording, and he mentioned the preponderance, so that the beginner and intermediate may both understand it." End quote.
Allamah Shaykh Muhammad Zahid al-Kawthari (d. 1371 AH) said: "His al-Tajrid indicates his breadth in fiqh." And in the author's introduction it says:
Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Baghdadi al-Quduri, may Allah be pleased with him, began dictating on Sunday, the 23rd of Dhul-Qa'dah, in the year 405 AH, and said:
"O Allah, protect us from error, grant us success in word and deed, make us obedient to You, adhering to what pleases You, and desiring what is with You."
(1) Al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 1/248.
(2) 1/346.
(3) Al-Tahrir al-Wajiz p.108, in his license to his student Ahmad Khayri.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch presenting the scholarly output of Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the famous Hanafi jurist. It highlights two primary works: his Mukhtasar, which is a concise compendium of Hanafi fiqh containing twelve thousand legal rulings without proofs, intended for those who seek practical knowledge without delving into evidence; and his larger work Al-Tajrid, which systematically presents the disputed issues between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, including the preferred position (tarjih). The passage cites several authorities (al-Qurashi, Ibn Taghribirdi, Kashf al-Zunun, al-Kawthari) praising Al-Tajrid for its comprehensive coverage of hadiths on rulings and its clarity for students at various levels. The author notes that the dictation of Al-Tajrid began on 23 Dhul-Qa'dah 405 AH, as recorded in the book's introduction, which includes a supplication by al-Quduri.

Key Terms
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): The famous concise work by Imam al-Quduri summing up Hanafi fiqh rulings without evidence.
التجريد (al-Tajrid): A book by al-Quduri detailing the points of legal disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is, with preponderance.
مسائل الخلاف (masa'il al-khilaf): Issues of disagreement between schools of law; here specifically between Hanafis and Shafi'is.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar provides 12,000 Hanafi rulings for practice, while his Tajrid presents evidence and tarjih for disputes with the Shafi'i school.

The Scholarly Authority of Imam al-Quduri and His Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi
Biographical introduction with scholarly praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the significance of Imam al-Quduri's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi and explain how it reflects his expertise in fiqh and hadith.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi is a monumental work demonstrating his mastery of both fiqh and hadith.

This passage introduces you to the life and works of Imam al-Quduri, focusing on his extensive commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. Understanding his scholarly stature is key to appreciating the authority of his opinions in later Hanafi texts. The praise from Imam al-Itqani and the description of the commentary's size reveal why this work is considered a cornerstone of Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text and its authors
First, note that Mukhtasar al-Karkhi was authored by Imam al-Karkhi, and its commentary was written by Imam al-Quduri. This relationship is central to the passage.
Al-Karkhi died 340 AH, al-Quduri died 428 AH.
2
Extract the evidence of al-Quduri's knowledge
Focus on the quote from Imam al-Itqani. He says the commentary itself is sufficient proof of al-Quduri's vast knowledge, comparing him to a 'vast sea' in fiqh and 'plentiful rain' in hadith.
The metaphor 'al-ʿAyyūq' (a star) indicates a height that few can reach.
3
Assess the physical scope of the commentary
The passage notes the commentary runs into several volumes, with about two thousand folios in one copy. This indicates the breadth and depth of al-Quduri's work.
This large size suggests thorough treatment of evidence and disputes.

وممن شرح هذا المختصر الإمام القدوري، ولم يوقف على اسم لهذا الشرح، وقد بَسَط القدوري في شرحه هذا بسطاً واسعاً، مع سوق الأدلة، وذكر الخلاف والمناقشات.

The esteemed legal schools, and that the four legal schools are like one cohesive family connected by the bond of Islam and knowledge, leading to true affection and love among the followers of these esteemed legal schools. The book was published in a critical edition by a team of nearly twenty [scholars], and the book was published in 12 volumes. The supervisors of the critical edition were Prof. Dr. Muhammad Ahmad Siraj and Prof. Dr. Ali Jum'a Muhammad, and the edition was published by Dar al-Salam for Printing and Publishing in Cairo, in the year 1425 AH. (1) The editors relied on several handwritten manuscripts, and there are other copies mentioned by the authors of the Comprehensive Index, which the editors did not mention. Overall, the edition is largely acceptable, but it is not free from oversights and errors that occurred in the text. 2- Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi: Mukhtasar al-Karkhi is authored by Imam Abu al-Hasan 'Ubayd Allah ibn al-Husayn al-Karkhi, who attained the leadership of the Hanafis in his time, died in Baghdad in the year 340 AH. (2) It appears from the transmitted texts about him that al-Karkhi did not omit the mention of evidence, like the rest of the abridgments, and he also cites the hadith used as evidence with its continuous chain. ... And among those who commented on this abridgment is Imam al-Quduri, and no specific name for this commentary has been found. Al-Quduri expanded greatly in this commentary, presenting evidence and discussing differences and debates. Imam Amir Katib al-Itqani (d. 751 AH), author of Ghayat al-Bayan Sharh al-Hidaya, praised this commentary, saying: 'Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, is a vast sea in fiqh and a plentiful rain in hadith. Sufficient proof of the abundance of his knowledge is his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, may Allah have mercy on him. If you examine it, you will know that his station in fiqh is at the star Capella, which not everyone can reach, and the eye of the observer returns from his position with fatigue and blindness.' End quote. This commentary consists of several large volumes, and there are numerous copies in Turkey and elsewhere. A copy from the Wali Allah Library in Istanbul is in five volumes, with approximately two thousand folios, and the remaining copies are also around five volumes.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Qudūrī): Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, a leading Hanafi jurist (d. 428 AH), author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and this commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi.
مختصر الكرخي (Mukhtaṣar al-Karkhī): A concise legal manual by Imam al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH), a prominent Hanafi scholar. It is a matn that presents rulings with evidence.
العيوق (al-ʿAyyūq): A bright red star (Capella) in the constellation Auriga, used metaphorically to denote something lofty and unreachable.

Imam al-Quduri and His Expansive Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi
Imam al-Quduri's biographical details and his extensive commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the significance of al-Quduri's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi and identify key biographical details about its composition and reception.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi is a colossal scholarly work that demonstrates his mastery in both fiqh and hadith.

This passage introduces Imam al-Quduri and his extensive commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. It highlights the praise this work received from later scholars, the sheer volume of the work, and the contrast with his famous concise Mukhtasar. Understanding this biography helps us appreciate the depth of Hanafi scholarship and the authority of al-Quduri's writings.

الفصل الأول: ترجمة الإمام القدوري

وممن شرح هذا المختصر الإمام القدوري، ولم يوقف على اسم لهذا الشرح، وقد بَسَط القدوري في شرحه هذا بسطاً واسعاً، سوق الأدلة، وذكر الخلاف والمناقشات.

وقد أثنى على هذا الشرح الإمام أمير كاتب الإتقاني (ت ٧٥١هـ)، صاحب غاية البيان شرح الهداية، حيث قال: والشيخ أبو الحسن القدوري رحمه الله بحر زخـار في الفقه، وغيث مدرار في الحديث، وناهيك من الدليل علـى غــزارة علمـه : شرحه لمختصر الكرخي رحمه الله ، فإذا طالعته عرفت أن محله في الفقه عند العيُّوق (٢) ، لا تناله يد كل أحد ، ويرجع طـرف الناظر إلى منزله من كلال ورمد». اهـ

هذا ويقع الشرح في عدة مجلدات كبار، ومنه نسخ عديدة في تركيا وغيرها)، وقد جاءت نسخة مكتبة ولي الله باسطنبول في خمس مجلدات يبلغ عدد أوراقها ألفي ورقة تقريباً، وكذلك بقية النسخ تقع في نحو خمس مجلدات

وهكذا سبحان من ألهم القدوري أن يكتب هذا الشرح بهذا البسط الكبير، وأن يكتب أيضاً ذلك المختصر المشهور مختصر القدوري بذلك الحجم اللطيف مع ما حواه من علم غزير.

والكتاب يُحقق في معهد القضاء في الرياض، مـن قبـل طـلاب الدراسات العليا، ويعمل على إخراجه أيضاً أحد الأساتذة الكرام. اختصر شرح القدوري على الكرخي: الإمام أبو المعالي عبد الرب بن منصور الغزنوي، المتوفى في حدود سنة ٥٠٠هـ، كما جاء في مقدمة الغزنوي نفسه لشرحه على مختصر القدوري المسمى: (ملتمس الإخوان)، حيث قال: (إني لما وفقني الله تعالى بفضله ورحمته ومنه ورأفته أن لخصت شرح مختصر الكرخي ، المصنف من جهة الشيخ أبي الحسين أحمد بن محمد القدوري... وأنفقت أكثر عمري على تلخيصه وتنقيحه، وأرقـت مـا شـيبني في ترصيفه وتوشيحه، واستحسن مجهودي كل من وقف عليه من الفقهاء والمحققين المميزين... التمس إخواني... أن أشرح لهم مختصر الشيخ القـدوري...، وسميت هذا الكتاب من بين سائر الأسماء: ملتمس الإخوان ومبتغى الأحباب والخلان ..»
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri

Among those who commented on this compendium is Imam al-Quduri, and no name for this commentary has been found. Al-Quduri expanded greatly in this commentary, adducing evidence and mentioning disagreement and discussions.

Imam Amir Katib al-Itqani (d. 751 AH), author of Ghayat al-Bayan Sharh al-Hidayah, praised this commentary, saying: “Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, is a vast sea in fiqh and a copious rain in hadith. Sufficient evidence of his abundant knowledge is his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. When you peruse it, you will know that his station in fiqh is as high as the star Capella, not attainable by everyone. The viewer’s gaze returns from his level with weariness and eye strain.”

This commentary runs to several large volumes. There are numerous copies in Turkey and elsewhere. The copy in the Wali Allah Library in Istanbul comprises five volumes, about two thousand folios, and the other copies are also around five volumes.

Thus, glory be to the One who inspired al-Quduri to write this commentary with such great expansion, and also to write the famous compendium Mukhtasar al-Quduri in that concise size, despite encompassing abundant knowledge.

The book is being edited at the Institute of the Judiciary in Riyadh by graduate students, and one esteemed professor is also working on its publication. An abridgement of al-Quduri's commentary on al-Karkhi was made by Imam Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Rabb ibn Mansur al-Ghaznawi, who died around 500 AH. In his introduction to his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, titled Multamis al-Ikhwan, al-Ghaznawi said: “When Allah, by His grace and mercy, enabled me to summarize the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi authored by Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri… and I spent most of my life on its summary and revision, staying awake until my hair turned grey in arranging and adorning it, and every scholar and precise investigator who saw it praised my effort… my brothers requested that I write a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri… and I named this book, among all other names, Multamis al-Ikhwan wa Mubtagha al-Ahbab wa al-Khillan.”
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction about Imam al-Quduri and his extensive commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. It begins by stating that al-Quduri wrote a commentary on the compendium (likely Mukhtasar al-Karkhi) but the title is unknown. The author notes that al-Quduri's commentary is detailed, including evidence and discussions of disagreement. Then, a quotation from Imam Amir Katib al-Itqani praises al-Quduri's knowledge, comparing his commentary to a testament of his vast learning, and using a poetic simile about the star Capella to emphasize his high rank. The passage then describes the physical size of the commentary—multiple large volumes, with copies in Turkey, especially one Istanbul library holding five volumes of about 2000 folios. The author marvels at how al-Quduri could produce both this massive commentary and his concise Mukhtasar (the well-known primer). Finally, it mentions that the commentary is being edited in Riyadh, and that an abridgement was made by al-Ghaznawi, who in his introduction (quoted) states that he summarized al-Quduri's work and then wrote his own commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, naming it Multamis al-Ikhwan. The passage provides biographical and bibliographic information, emphasizing the prestige of al-Quduri's scholarship.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The famous concise Hanafi fiqh compendium by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
شرح مختصر الكرخي (Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi): Al-Quduri's commentary on the earlier compendium by al-Karkhi, which is the subject of this biographical passage.
العيُّوق (al-'Ayyuq): The star Capella, used as a metaphor for high rank, difficult to reach.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Imam al-Quduri and His Scholarly Legacy
Biographical introduction to Imam al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major works of Imam al-Quduri and explain their significance in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri authored the foundational Mukhtasar and two works on ikhtilaf, inspiring centuries of scholarly commentary.

This lesson introduces you to Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the author of the iconic Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a text that has shaped Hanafi fiqh study for nearly a millennium. Understanding his biography and the works he produced will help you appreciate the textual hierarchy of the school and the scholarly efforts that built upon his concise manual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his main contribution
Recognize that Imam al-Quduri is the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise yet comprehensive manual of Hanafi fiqh. This matn is a foundational text in the school.
The commentator praises al-Quduri for balancing brevity with abundant knowledge.
2
List his major works mentioned in the passage
From the text, extract: (1) Mukhtasar al-Quduri, (2) al-Taqrib al-Awwal (without proofs), (3) al-Taqrib al-Thani (with proofs), and (4) a hadith collection of 23 narrations.
Note the distinction between the two Taqrib works: one without adillah, one with.
3
Trace the transmission and commentary tradition
Observe that al-Ghaznawi wrote a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri called Multamas al-Ikhwan, and that the present commentary (al-Lubab) is itself a sharh of al-Quduri's work. This shows a chain of scholarly engagement.
The passage also mentions that the book is being critically edited at the Institute of Judiciary in Riyadh.
4
Appreciate the significance of the hadith collection
The text notes a small hadith collection (23 ahadith) transmitted by al-Quduri from his teacher. It was passed orally until the ninth century, highlighting the importance of isnad even in fiqh-focused works.
Modern scholars have verified and published it.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Thus glory be to the One who inspired al-Quduri to write this commentary with such great expansion, and also to write that famous summary, the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri, in that elegant size with what it contains of abundant knowledge.
The book is being verified at the Institute of Judiciary in Riyadh by graduate students, and one of the honorable professors is also working on its publication. The one who shortened al-Quduri's commentary on al-Karkhi: Imam Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Rabb ibn Mansur al-Ghaznawi, who died around the year 500 AH, as mentioned in al-Ghaznawi's own introduction to his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri called (Multamas al-Ikhwan), where he said: (When Allah, may He be exalted, granted me success by His grace, mercy, favor, and kindness to summarize the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, composed by the Sheikh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri... and I spent most of my life summarizing and refining it, and spent my youthful vigor in its arrangement and adornment, and everyone who saw it from the jurists and investigating discerning scholars praised my effort... my brothers asked... that I comment on the Mukhtasar of Sheikh al-Quduri... and I named this book among all other names: Multamas al-Ikhwan wa Mubtagha al-Ahbab wa al-Khillan.) End quote.
(1) As was written to me about that from Istanbul, thank you, the noble brother Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya, for he inspected the manuscript himself and quoted this introduction from it. Mention of his commentary will come in the third chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Allah willing.
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
Al-Taqrib fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah bayn al-Imam Abi Hanifah wa Ashabihi: It is devoid of evidence and comprises one volume. The authors of the Comprehensive Index (1) mentioned a copy of it in Istanbul, comprising 279 folios, and its copying date is 480 AH.
4- Al-Taqrib al-Thani fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah bayn Abi Hanifah wa Ashabihi (with evidence): He incorporated the first Taqrib into it, then added the evidence of each group, and it comprises several volumes (2).
A hadith section from the narrations of Imam al-Quduri from his teacher Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Mu'addib, narrated from al-Quduri by his student al-Damaghani, mentioned by Imam al-Qurashi (3), who mentioned his chain to it and quoted a hadith from it.
(4)
The authors of the Comprehensive Index mentioned several copies of it, each copy comprising (4) folios, and it contains only 23 hadiths. It was verified and its hadiths were authenticated by Professor Yasin Kok Kuz in Konya, Turkey, and it came in 130 pages.
The hadith scholars transmitted it by listening among themselves until the ninth century.
(1) 2/671
(2) He named it with this name: al-Taqrib al-Awwal and al-Taqrib al-Thani. Ibn Taghribardi in al-Nujum al-Zahirah 5/27, and see Taj al-Tarajim p. 99, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 31.
(3) al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah 1/249.
(4) 3/123
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This is the opening of the first chapter of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, which provides a biography of Imam al-Quduri (Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, d. 428 AH), the author of the famous Mukhtasar in Hanafi fiqh. The commentator (Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, d. 1298 AH) begins by praising Allah for inspiring al-Quduri to produce both this expansive commentary (i.e., the present work) and the concise Mukhtasar that contains a wealth of knowledge. He then notes that the book is being critically edited at the Institute of Judiciary in Riyadh. The author mentions that al-Ghaznawi (d. ca. 500 AH) abridged al-Quduri's commentary on al-Karkhi's Mukhtasar and wrote his own commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri titled &quot;Multamas al-Ikhwan.&quot; He quotes al-Ghaznawi's introduction explaining his motivation and effort. The biography then lists works of al-Quduri: (1) al-Taqrib fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah (concerning differences between Abu Hanifa and his students, without proofs, in one volume, with a manuscript in Istanbul from 480 AH); (2) al-Taqrib al-Thani (the same but with proofs, in several volumes); and (3) a hadith collection containing 23 narrations from his teacher, verified by a modern scholar. The author notes that hadith scholars transmitted this collection orally until the ninth century. The passage also includes footnotes citing references from Ibn Taghribardi, Taj al-Tarajim, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah, and al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah. This section serves as an introduction for students to appreciate the scholarly legacy of al-Quduri and the foundational texts of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The famous concise manual of Hanafi fiqh authored by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a foundational text for the school.
التقريب في المسائل الخلافية (al-Taqrib fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah): A work by al-Quduri on the disputed issues within the Hanafi school (between Abu Hanifa and his students), first without evidence, then with evidence.
ملتمس الإخوان (Multamas al-Ikhwan): Al-Ghaznawi's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, written at the request of fellow scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The first is in one volume, the second is also in one volume

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh study, and his other works like al-Taqrib and his hadith collection show his breadth as a scholar.

Biography of Imam al-Quduri and His Works
Biography listing al-Quduri's major works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major works of Imam al-Quduri and identify their significance in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri authored seven books, including the foundational Mukhtasar, a comparative work on khilaf, and a hadith collection.

Imam al-Quduri is a towering figure in the Hanafi school, best known for his Mukhtasar. But his scholarly output extended beyond that single text. This passage from Lubab al-Lubab maps out his full bibliography, including works on legal disagreements (khilaf) and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and Context
Note that Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) is the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. This passage lists his other works.
2
List Each Work Mentioned
Go through the text and extract each work: al-Taqrib (first without proofs), al-Taqrib (second with proofs), a hadith collection, Adab al-Qadi, and al-Mukhtasar. Note there are seven total, but only five are named explicitly; the others may be lost.
3
Note Distinguishing Features
Observe that the first Taqrib is devoid of proofs, while the second includes proofs. The hadith collection contains only 23 hadiths but was transmitted orally for centuries.
4
Recognize Total and Possible Lost Works
The text states the total is seven books, but only five are detailed. The author hints at additional works not found, as mentioned by Hadiyat al-'Arifin.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري
التقريب في المسائل الخلافية بين الإمام أبي حنيفة وأصحابه : وهو مجرد من الأدلة، ويقع في مجلد، وقد ذكر أصحاب الفهرس الشامل نسخة منه في اسطنبول، تقع في (۲۷۹) ورقة، و تاريخ نسخها ٤٨٠هـ.
٤- التقريب الثاني في المسائل الخلافية بين أبي حنيفة وأصحابه (مع الأدلة) : وقد ضمن فيه التقريب الأول، ثم زاد فيه أدلة كل فريق، ويقع في عدة مجلدات.
ه- جزء في الحديث من مرويات الإمام القدوري عن شيخه أبي بكر محمد بن علي المؤدب، رواه عن القدوري تلميذه الدامغاني، ذكره الإمام القرشي، وذكر سنده إليه، وأورد حديثاً منه.

وكان المحدثون يتناقلونه بالسماع فيما بينهم حتى القرن التاسع وما بعده، كما في الدرر الكامنة، والضوء اللامع.
بل قال العلامة الشيخ الكوثري رحمه الله : «وللقدوري جزء حديثي معروف، مروي في أثبات المشايخ على توالي القرون، وهو مروي في المعجم المؤسس، للحافظ ابن حجر، وإني أرويه بالسند إلى ...» . اهـ
٦- أدب القاضي على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة.
المختصر (مختصر القدوري) في فروع المذهب الحنفي : وقد أفردت عنه دراسة خاصة موسعة مع ذكر ما وقفت عليه من شروحه، والأعمال العلمية التي قامت عليه، والتي بلغت بمجموعها (۱۲۳)، وستأتي قريباً إن شاء الله تعالى.
وهكذا، فجملة ما ذكر للقدوري من مؤلفات: سبعة كتب، ومع هذا فإن صاحب هدية العارفين لما ترجم للقدوري، وذكر كتبه السابقة الذكر ما عدا جزءه الحديثي، قال: «وغير ذلك». اهـ. وعليه فيحتمل أن تكون له كتب أخرى لم نقف عليها. وأذكر فيما يلي أسماء كتبه مجملةً مرتبة على حروف المعجم:
Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. Al-Taqrib concerning the issues of disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions: it is devoid of proofs, and consists of one volume. The authors of al-Fihris al-Shamil mentioned a copy of it in Istanbul, consisting of 279 folios, and its copying date is 480 AH. 4- The second al-Taqrib concerning the issues of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his companions (with proofs): he included in it the first al-Taqrib, then added the proofs of each group, and it consists of several volumes. 5- A Hadith collection from the narrations of Imam al-Quduri from his teacher Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ali al-Mu'addib, narrated from al-Quduri by his student al-Damaghani. Imam al-Qurashi mentioned it and mentioned his chain to it, and cited a hadith from it. The authors of al-Fihris al-Shamil mentioned several copies of it, each copy consisting of 4 folios, containing only 23 hadiths. It was edited and its hadiths were authenticated by Professor Yasin Kuk Kuz in Konya, Turkey, and it came in 130 pages. The hadith scholars used to transmit it orally among themselves until the 9th century and beyond, as mentioned in al-Durar al-Kaminah and al-Daw' al-Lami'. Rather, the scholar Shaykh al-Kawthari said: 'Al-Quduri has a known Hadith collection, transmitted in the proofs of the shaykhs across successive centuries, and it is transmitted in al-Mu'jam al-Mu'assis by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, and I narrate it with chain to...' end. 6- Adab al-Qadi according to the school of Imam Abu Hanifa. The abridgment (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) on the branches of the Hanafi school: I have devoted a separate extensive study to it, mentioning the commentaries I came across and the academic works done on it, which total 123, and it will come soon, God willing. Thus, the total works mentioned for al-Quduri are seven books. Yet, the author of Hadiyat al-'Arifin, when he translated al-Quduri and mentioned his previous books except his Hadith collection, said: 'And other than that.' So it is possible that he has other works we have not come across. I will list below the names of his books summarized in alphabetical order:
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Quduri, the author of the famous Mukhtasar al-Quduri in Hanafi fiqh. The text lists his known works: (1) al-Taqrib on comparative issues between Abu Hanifa and his students without proofs, (2) the second al-Taqrib with proofs, (3) a Hadith collection of 23 hadiths, (4) Adab al-Qadi (the judge's etiquette), and (5) his renowned Mukhtasar. The total is seven books, though some may be lost. The passage emphasizes the scholarly importance of al-Quduri's contributions, especially the Mukhtasar which received extensive commentaries.

Key Terms
التقريب (al-Taqrib): A work by al-Quduri on issues of disagreement (khilaf) between Abu Hanifa and his students, first without proofs, then expanded with proofs.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): Al-Quduri's famous abridgment of Hanafi fiqh, a foundational text for the school.
أدب القاضي (Adab al-Qadi): A work by al-Quduri on the etiquette and procedures for judges according to the Hanafi school.

Imam al-Quduri's Scholarly Legacy: His Works and Contributions
List and description of al-Quduri's seven works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven known works of Imam al-Quduri and explain the significance of al-Mukhtasar in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri authored seven works, but his Mukhtasar is the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh study.

Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) is a towering figure in the Hanafi madhhab. While his Mukhtasar is famous worldwide, he authored several other important works covering khilaf, hadith, and judicial ethics. This passage from Lubab al-Quduri lists all seven, showing the breadth of his scholarship and reinforcing why his legacy endures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full name
Recognize that al-Quduri is Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, a Hanafi jurist from Baghdad. Note his death year (428 AH).
2
Count the works mentioned
The passage states the total is seven books. Scan the list: Adab al-Qadi, al-Tajrid, al-Taqrib al-Awwal, al-Taqrib al-Thani, a hadith collection, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, and al-Mukhtasar.
The hadith collection is sometimes omitted in other sources; this passage includes it.
3
Categorize each work by genre
Fiqh: al-Mukhtasar. Khilaf (disputes): al-Tajrid (between Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i) and al-Taqribs (between Abu Hanifa and his students). Hadith: the hadith collection. Judicial ethics: Adab al-Qadi. Commentary: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi.
This shows al-Quduri's expertise in multiple disciplines.
4
Recognize the centrality of al-Mukhtasar
The passage notes 123 commentaries and studies on al-Mukhtasar. Understand that this work became the standard textbook for Hanafi fiqh for centuries.
Memorize that al-Mukhtasar is also called Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
5
Reflect on the possibility of additional works
The author cites Hadiyat al-Arifin suggesting 'and other than that', indicating al-Quduri may have authored more works not listed.
Historical research may uncover more.

وما بعده، كما في الدرر الكامنة ) ، والضوء اللامع

٦ـ أدب القاضي على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة (٤).

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
And what follows, as in al-Durar al-Kamina and al-Daw' al-Lami'. In fact, al-Allamah al-Shaykh al-Kawthari (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Al-Quduri has a well-known hadith collection, narrated in the registries of the shaykhs across successive centuries, and it is narrated in al-Mu'jam al-Mu'assis by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, and I narrate it with the chain to ...' End quote. 6- Adab al-Qadi according to the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. The Mukhtasar (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) in the branches of the Hanafi madhhab: A separate extensive study has been devoted to it, mentioning the commentaries I have come across, and the academic works based upon it, which amount to a total of (123), and it will come soon, Allah willing. Thus, the total works mentioned for al-Quduri are seven books. Moreover, the author of Hadiyat al-'Arifin, when he translated al-Quduri and mentioned his books (except his hadith collection), said: 'and other than that.' End quote. Hence it is possible that he had other works we have not encountered. Below I will list the names of his books in summary, arranged alphabetically: 1. Adab al-Qadi. 2. al-Tajrid fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah bayn Abi Hanifah wa al-Shafi'i. 3. al-Taqrib al-Awwal fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah bayn al-Imam Abi Hanifah wa Ashabih. 4. al-Taqrib al-Thani, including the first Taqrib (with evidence). 5. A hadith collection from the narrations of al-Quduri. 6. Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. 7. al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This is a biographical passage about Imam al-Quduri, the renowned Hanafi jurist. It begins by referencing his biography found in other works, then quotes Shaykh al-Kawthari confirming al-Quduri's hadith collection. The passage lists al-Quduri's work 'Adab al-Qadi' and then focuses on his famous 'Mukhtasar' (al-Mukhtasar), which is the foundational text for Hanafi fiqh. It notes that 123 commentaries and studies have been written on this Mukhtasar. The passage then states that al-Quduri authored seven books in total, and even the author of 'Hadiyat al-'Arifin' indicates there may be more. The remainder of the passage lists the seven works alphabetically: (1) Adab al-Qadi (a judge's etiquette), (2) al-Tajrid (a work on points of difference between Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i), (3) al-Taqrib al-Awwal (on differences between Abu Hanifa and his students), (4) al-Taqrib al-Thani (including the first with evidence), (5) a hadith collection, (6) Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi (a commentary on al-Karkhi's Mukhtasar), and (7) al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh (the well-known abridgement of Hanafi fiqh). This list shows the breadth of al-Quduri's scholarship in fiqh, usul, hadith, and judicial ethics.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a prominent Hanafi jurist and author of al-Mukhtasar.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): The abridged work on Hanafi fiqh by al-Quduri, also known as 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'.
التجريد (al-Tajrid): A book by al-Quduri on points of legal difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i.
التقريب (al-Taqrib): Two works by al-Quduri on differences between Abu Hanifa and his students, the second including evidence.
أدب القاضي (Adab al-Qadi): A work by al-Quduri on the ethics and conduct of a judge according to the Hanafi school.
شرح مختصر الكرخي (Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi): Al-Quduri's commentary on the Mukhtasar of al-Karkhi, an earlier Hanafi text.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri authored seven known works, spanning fiqh, khilaf, hadith, and judicial ethics, with al-Mukhtasar being the most influential.

Imam al-Quduri and His Scholarly Legacy
Listing the works of Imam al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major works of Imam al-Quduri and explain the significance of his Mukhtasar for Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is the foundational Hanafi matn, but he also wrote on khilaf, hadith, and judicial ethics.

This passage opens a window into the scholarly output of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the Mukhtasar that forms the basis of al-Lubab. While his Mukhtasar is his most famous work, al-Quduri was a prolific author who contributed to multiple areas of Hanafi knowledge. Understanding his full bibliography helps us appreciate the depth of his scholarship and the breadth of the tradition we are studying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the range of topics
Scan the list and note the different subjects: fiqh (Mukhtasar), khilaf (Tajrid, Taqrib works), hadith (Juz'), and judicial ethics (Adab al-Qadi).
This shows al-Quduri was not only a faqih but also a muhaddith and a specialist in judicial conduct.
2
Distinguish the Taqrib works
The two Taqrib works both deal with khilaf (disputed issues). The first Taqrib is a compilation of differences between Abu Hanifa and his companions; the second incorporates those and adds evidence (dalil).
This demonstrates the progressive refinement of scholarly works, moving from mere listing to proof-based analysis.
3
Recognize the chain of commentary
Al-Quduri wrote a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, showing that he was part of a tradition of building on earlier works. Later, al-Lubab comments on his Mukhtasar.
This highlights the interconnected nature of Hanafi scholarship: each generation builds upon the previous.
4
Appreciate the Mukhtasar's centrality
The Mukhtasar is listed separately at the end, indicating its primacy as the core text of al-Lubab's commentary.
It remains one of the most widely memorized and taught texts in the Hanafi madhhab.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
1. Adab al-Qadi (The Etiquette of the Judge).
2. Al-Tajrid fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah bayna Abi Hanifah wa al-Shafi'i (The Abstract in Controversial Issues between Abu Hanifah and al-Shafi'i).
3. Al-Taqrib al-Awwal fi al-Masa'il al-Khilafiyyah bayna al-Imam Abi Hanifah wa Ashabih (The First Approximation in Controversial Issues between Imam Abu Hanifah and His Companions).
4. Al-Taqrib al-Thani, Mudamminan fihi al-Taqrib al-Awwal (with proofs) (The Second Approximation, Containing the First Approximation with Evidence).
5. Juz' fi al-Hadith min Marwiyyat al-Quduri (A Section of Hadith from al-Quduri's Narrations).
6. Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi (Commentary on the Abridged Work of al-Karkhi).
- Al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh (The Abridged Work in Fiqh).
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of the major works of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the renowned Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which is the foundational text (matn) for the Hanafi school that the commentary 'al-Lubab' explains. The passage enumerates six (actually seven) key writings by al-Quduri. The first, 'Adab al-Qadi,' deals with the ethics and conduct of a judge. The second, 'Al-Tajrid,' is a compilation of points of difference between Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i. The third and fourth are 'Taqrib' works focusing on differences among Hanafi imams, with the fourth incorporating evidence. The fifth is a collection of hadith narrations. The sixth is a commentary on another Hanafi abridgment by al-Karkhi. Finally, the famous 'Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh' is listed separately, which is the core text upon which 'al-Lubab' comments. This biography establishes the scholarly pedigree of the text being studied.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) is the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
المختصر في الفقه (al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh): Al-Quduri's abridged work on Hanafi fiqh, also known as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, is the basis for the commentary al-Lubab.
التجريد (al-Tajrid): Al-Quduri's work on controversial issues between Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i.
التقريب (al-Taqrib): Two works (al-Awwal and al-Thani) on controversial issues among Hanafi imams, the second including evidence.
أدب القاضي (Adab al-Qadi): A work on the ethics and conduct of a judge in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri was a prolific Hanafi scholar whose works spanned fiqh, khilaf, hadith, and judicial ethics, with his Mukhtasar serving as the foundational text for Hanafi studies.
