The Blessedness of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Narrating the story of barakah and scholarly consensus on the book's blessing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical account of the barakah of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and identify the scholars who attested to it.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri prayed for barakah at the Kaaba; scholars have unanimously recognised his book as blessed for over a millennium.

This passage from al-Maydani's introduction to al-Lubab presents the extraordinary story of how Mukhtasar al-Quduri received divine blessing. It calls our attention to the spiritual dimension of fiqh texts and the sincere intention behind their composition. Understanding this narrative deepens appreciation for the Hanafi canon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core story
Locate the account of al-Quduri hanging his book on the Kaaba curtains and supplicating for blessing. Note the key action and the result.
The story is narrated from a manuscript note, indicating it was widely transmitted.
2
Confirm the textual witnesses
The author reports seeing this report in multiple manuscripts and an old print. Verify the consistency of the transmission.
Multiple witnesses across centuries strengthen the reliability of the account.
3
Note the early commentator's testimony
Imam Ahmad al-Razi (d. 500 AH) in his introduction to 'Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri' explicitly praises the book's brevity and barakah. Extract his words.
Al-Razi's statement shows that the barakah was recognised within a century of the author's death.
4
Observe the consensus among scholars
Al-Maydani states that scholars of the madhhab and others agreed that the Mukhtasar is blessed, to the point of it becoming 'necessary knowledge' (al-'ilm al-daruri).
Consensus (ijma) among Hanafi scholars, even if not a legal ruling, affirms the spiritual status of the text.
5
Reflect on practical implications
Consider the report from 'Miftah al-Sa'adah' that scholars would recite the Mukhtasar during calamities. How does barakah influence the approach to studying this text?
This reinforces the idea that barakah is not merely symbolic but has tangible effects.

Chapter Two: Study on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Second Section
The Blessing (Yumn) and Blessedness (Barakah) of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
I saw on the first page of a manuscript copy of the book 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by al-Hadadi, deposited in the Mahmudiyyah Library in Medina, number 1036, copied in the ninth century, I saw written on it the following text:
'When al-Quduri authored this book, he proceeded to the Sacred House of Allah, and hung it on the curtains of the Kaaba, and asked Allah Almighty to bless it, and his prayer was answered, and He made it blessed. The number of its issues is twelve thousand and five hundred.' End.
And I saw this same report at the end of another manuscript copy of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, deposited in the Qarah Bash Library, within the King Abdul Aziz Library in Medina, number 231 in 225 folios, copied in the year 1033 AH.
6
Also, this report is mentioned on the first page of an old printed edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, printed in 1309 AH in the Ottoman Press in Istanbul, during the reign of Sultan Abdul Hamid.
And one of the early commentators of al-Quduri clearly stated its blessing and grace – he is Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muzaffar al-Razi, died 500 AH, in the introduction of his book: 'Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri', for he said in his praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, as mentioned: '... what is in it of good brevity... and it being blessed for its students, auspicious for its readers and memorizers, and people are too intelligent to praise something unless they see signs of beneficence.' End.
And thus the consensus of the scholars of the madhhab and others agreed that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a blessed book, and that its blessing has become widespread until it became like necessary knowledge. End.
And the author of Miftah al-Sa'adah said:
'Know that this Mukhtasar is such that scholars have sought blessings from it, even to the extent that they would practice reading it during times of hardship and days of plague.' End.
And the author of Kashf al-Zunun quoted from the author of 'Misbah Anwar al-Ad'iyyah' that he said: ...
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is biographical and devotional in nature, discussing the blessedness (barakah) of the famous Hanafi primer, Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). The author, 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of al-Lubab, opens this section by narrating a widely reported story: when al-Quduri completed his book, he traveled to Makkah, hung it on the curtains of the Kaaba, and prayed to Allah to bless it. Allah answered his prayer, making the book a source of blessing for countless students. The number of masā'il (legal issues) in the book is said to be 12,500. Al-Maydani confirms that he saw this note in multiple manuscripts and even an old printed edition, indicating the consistent transmission of this account. He then quotes Imam Ahmad al-Razi (d. 500 AH), an early commentator, who in his introduction to 'Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri' praised the book for its concise style and affirmed that it is 'blessed for its students, auspicious for its readers and memorizers.' Al-Razi adds that people are too intelligent to praise something without witnessing its beneficial effects. Al-Maydani then states that there is general consensus (ittifaq) among scholars of the Hanafi madhhab and others that the Mukhtasar is a blessed book, and that its blessing has become so widespread it is considered necessary knowledge (al-'ilm al-daruri). He further quotes Tashkubri Zada from 'Miftah al-Sa'adah' noting that scholars would seek blessings by reciting this book during calamities and plagues. Finally, he references Kashf al-Zunun by Hajji Khalifa, who quoted from 'Misbah Anwar al-Ad'iyyah' by 'Abd al-Rahman al-Bistami (d. 852 AH) regarding the barakah of the Mukhtasar. The passage emphasizes the spiritual dimension of religious texts in the Hanafi tradition and the belief that a book can be a means of divine blessing beyond its legal content. It also serves to motivate students to value and engage sincerely with the Mukhtasar.

Key Terms
بركة (barakah): Spiritual blessing and divine favor that increases goodness and benefit; here attributed to the book Mukhtasar al-Quduri through the supplication of its author.
يمن (yumn): Blessing, auspiciousness; synonym for barakah in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Quduri do with his book after authoring it to seek Allah's blessing?
A) He read it to scholars in Baghdad.
B) He hung it on the curtains of the Kaaba and supplicated.
C) He distributed copies to all mosques.
D) He performed ijtihad and prayed for acceptance.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a blessed book, as testified by its author's du'a, early commentators, and a consensus of scholars over centuries.

The Tradition of Memorizing Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Historical account of the memorization of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the historical practice of memorizing Mukhtasar al-Quduri among Hanafi scholars and identify at least three scholars who memorized it.

Core Idea
Memorization of Mukhtasar al-Quduri was a hallmark of Hanafi legal training for centuries.

This passage offers a fascinating glimpse into the educational culture of the Hanafi madhhab. It documents how scholars, fathers, and students valued the memorization of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, often with incentives and rewards. Understanding this helps us appreciate the role of foundational texts in preserving and transmitting Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and its context
Recognize that the passage is from a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, providing historical background on the text's memorization.
The text is from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri by al-Maydani.
2
Locate the key claim about Hanafis' attachment
Al-Shihab al-Marjani states that Hanafis were passionate about memorizing and narrating Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
This sets the tone for the entire passage.
3
List the scholars mentioned who memorized it
Identify each scholar: al-Qurashi, his father, his brother, al-Abbasi, al-Maraghi, and more than forty others counted by al-Sakhawi.
These demonstrate the widespread practice.
4
Examine the incentives for memorization
Note the story of Kamal al-Din, whose father promised rewards for memorizing al-Luma' and then Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
This shows how families encouraged memorization.
5
Reflect on the significance of memorizing a single text
Consider why memorization of this specific matn was so central to Hanafi education—it ensured uniformity and mastery of foundational rulings.
This practice continues in traditional Hanafi seminaries today.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري

بل قال الشهاب المرجاني حين ذكر مختصر القدوري، واهتمام الحنفية به قال:
أولعوا فيه حفظاً، ورواية...» (۱). اهـ

*
وممن كان يحفظه : ما ذكره الإمام القرشي صاحب الجواهر المضية (٢) أن والده كان يحفظ هذا المختصر، وكذلك كان يحفظه أخوه الشقيق، وكان يحفظه هو.

كما كان يحفظه الإمام شهاب الدين أحمد بن محمد العباسي، المتوفى سنة ٨٩٠هـ، كما صرح هو في مقدمة كتابه: «العقـود المفصلة في الجمع بين القدوري والتكملة»(4).

بل عد السخاوي في كتابه الضوء اللامع أكثر من أربعين مترجمـاً كان يحفظ مختصر القدوري.

العطاء
وهكذا كان الآباء يشجعون أبناءهم على حفظه، ويكثرون لهم والهدايا في مقابل ذلك.

فقد جاء في معجم الأدباء لياقوت الحموي (٥) ، في ترجمة مؤرّخ مدينة حلب الشهباء المحدّث كمال الدين ابن العديم عمر بن أحمد ابن هبة الله ، المتوفى سنة ٦٦٠هـ، قال ياقوت :
حدثني كمال الدين - أدام الله معاليه ـ قال : قال لي والدي : احفظ اللمَع) (۱) حتى أعطيك كذا وكذا ، فحفظته، وقرأته على شيخ حلب يومئذ، وهو الضياء بن دهن العصا.
ثم قال لي: احفظ : «القدوري»، حتى أهـب لـك كذا وكذا مـن الدراهم، كثيرة أيضاً، فحفظته في مدة يسيرة». اهـ

وأعظم من هذا ما ذكره القرشي في ترجمة محمد بن يحيى ابن مسلم القاضي المَرَاغي، المتوفى سنة ٥٦٣ هـ، أنه كان يحفظ شرح مختصر القدوري للأقطع

ومثل هذا الخبر أيضاً ما جاء (۳) في ترجمة محمد بن الحسن الحلبي، أحد فقهاء الحنفية في القرن الثامن الهجري، ولم يذكر سنة وفاته، أنه حفظ كتاب الهداية للمرغيناني في صغره، وعرضه على العلامة ابن الوردي الفقيه الشافعي، فاختبره بـه، فأعجب به، وكتب له إجازة جيدة سنة ٧٤٤هـ.

وكذلك ذكر السخاوي في ترجمة عبد الرحمن بن العلامة

(۱) للإمام الشيرازي إبراهيم بن علي (ت ٤٧٦ هـ) ، مختصر في علـم أصـول الفقه للسادة الشافعية.
(۲) الجواهر المضية ٣٩٧/٣.
(۳) الجواهر المضية ١٣٧/٣.
(٤) الضوء اللامع ٩١/٤.
Chapter Two: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Al-Shihab al-Marjani said when mentioning Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Hanafis' interest in it: 'They were passionate about memorizing it and narrating it...' end. * And among those who memorized it: what Imam al-Qurashi, author of al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, mentioned: that his father memorized this Mukhtasar, and likewise his full brother memorized it, and he himself memorized it. Also, Imam Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Abbasi, died 890 AH, memorized it, as he stated in the introduction to his book: 'al-Uqud al-Mufassala fi al-Jam bayn al-Quduri wa al-Takmila'. Rather, al-Sakhawi in his book al-Daw' al-Lami' counted more than forty translators who memorized Mukhtasar al-Quduri. And thus fathers encouraged their sons to memorize it and gave them abundant gifts in return. It is mentioned in Mu'jam al-Udaba' by Yaqut al-Hamawi, in the biography of the historian of Aleppo, the muhaddith Kamal al-Din ibn al-Adim Umar ibn Ahmad ibn Hibbat Allah, died 660 AH: Yaqut said: Kamal al-Din narrated to me: My father said to me: Memorize al-Luma' so that I give you such and such, so I memorized it and recited it to the shaykh of Aleppo at that time, al-Diya' ibn Dahn al-Asa. Then he said to me: Memorize al-Quduri, so that I give you such and such dirhams, also many, so I memorized it in a short time. End. And greater than this is what al-Qurashi mentioned in the biography of Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Muslim al-Qadi al-Maraghi, died 563 AH: that he memorized the commentary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Aqta. And similar news also came in the biography of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Halabi, one of the Hanafi jurists of the eighth century AH (death date not mentioned): that he memorized the book al-Hidaya by al-Marghinani in his youth, and presented it to the scholar Ibn al-Wardi, the Shafi'i jurist, who examined him on it and was impressed, and wrote him a good ijaza in 744 AH. Likewise, al-Sakhawi mentioned in the biography of Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Alama... (footnotes follow).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It demonstrates the immense importance placed on memorizing this foundational Hanafi text. The author lists several notable scholars and their efforts to memorize the Mukhtasar, including al-Marjani's statement about the Hanafis' passion for it. The anecdote about Kamal al-Din ibn al-Adim shows how fathers incentivized their sons with rewards. The passage also highlights that even commentaries on the Mukhtasar were memorized, as seen with al-Maraghi memorizing al-Aqta's commentary. This reflects the centrality of al-Quduri's work in Hanafi legal education.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri, widely memorized and studied in the Hanafi school.

The Absence of an Introduction in Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Textual criticism of the Mukhtasar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence that al-Quduri did not write an introduction to his Mukhtasar and identify the implications for studying the text.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri’s Mukhtasar has no introduction; manuscripts begin directly with the Book of Purification.

When studying a foundational fiqh text like Mukhtasar al-Quduri, knowing its textual history is crucial. This passage investigates whether al-Quduri wrote an introduction. The findings affect how we understand his methodology and source reliance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The author states that it is strongly believed (yaghlibu ʿala al-ẓann) that al-Quduri did not write an introduction.
2
Examine the evidence
Dozens of manuscripts and printed copies were surveyed; all begin after the Basmalah with Kitab al-Taharah without any preface.
This empirical evidence undercuts later claims of an introduction.
3
Analyze counter-claims
Kashf al-Zunun records an opening praise, but the author suggests it may be an editor's addition. Similarly, a quote attributed to al-Quduri is actually from al-Razi.
Careful attribution is needed: the quote 'This book compiles...' is from al-Razi's commentary on the Takmila.
4
Draw the conclusion
No authentic introduction exists; any appearance of one is a later interpolation.
Thus, al-Quduri's methodology must be inferred from the text itself.

المبحث الثالث
منهج الإمام القدوري وأسلوبه في مختصره
بيان أن القدوري لم يكتب مقدمة لمختصره :
يغلب على الظن أن الإمام القدوري رحمه الله لم يكتب مقدمـةً لمختصره في الفقه، والتي كان يمكن من خلالها التعرف على خطة عمله فيه، ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، والمصادر التي استقى منها معلومات هذا الكتاب ونحو هذا مما يذكره المؤلفون عادة في مقدمات كتبهم. ومن هنا لم نستطع التعرف على شيءٍ من ذلك إلا عن طريق الدراسة، وما يلمحه الباحث المتأمل فيه.
وإن عدم وجود مقدمة لهذا المختصر مما أجمعت عليه نُسَخ هذا المختصر المخطوطة والمطبوعة، وذلك حسب استقرائي لعشرات النسخ منه، ولعشرات من شروحه التي ضمت هذا المختصر. وهكذا، فالنسخ كلها تبدأ بعد البسملة، وبعـد عنـوان: (كتـاب الطهارة، تبدأ بآية الوضوء التي افتتح بها القدوري مختصره، ثم يأتي ذكر فرائض الوضوء، وهكذا إلى تمام نهاية المختصر، دون أن تُذكر له أي مقدمة.
في حين أن صاحب كشف الظنون (1) ذكر أن أول المختصر يبدأ بقوله : «الحمد لله رب العالمين، والعاقبة للمتقين، والصلاة على رسوله محمد وآله أجمعين ...». اهـ. هكذا.
قلت: ولعل ذلك من تصرفات الناخ.
ومع هذا، يبقى الاحتمال قائماً أن تكون هذه الافتتاحية هـي مـن كلام القدوري نفسه، والله أعلم.
* وأيضاً : ففي المطبوع من كشف الظنون، عند ذكره لمختصر القدوري وشروحه، جاء فيه نص يفيد ظاهره أن القدوري كتب مقدمةً لمختصره، والصواب أنها ليست من كلام القدوري.
فبعد أن ذكر صاحب كشف الظنون (2) أن الإمام حسام الدين الرازي علي بن أحمد مكي، (ت 598هـ) ، قد عمل تكملة لمختصر القدوري، وأنه شرحها ، نَقَلَ عن مقدمة شرحه للتكملة قوله : (3) قال القدوري : هذا كتاب يجمع من فروع الفقه ما لم يجمعه غيره.
(3) هكذا في كشف الظنون، والصواب والله أعلم : (قال الرازي)، لأن الكلام السابق لهذا الذي ذكره صاحب كشف الظنون هو من كلام الرازي حسام الدين وهو عن تكملة القدوري وشرحه لها، وأنه جمع في التكملة ما شد من المختصر من المسائل المنشورة في المختصرات كالجامع الصغير، ومختصر الطحاوي، والإرشاد، وموجز الفرغاني، فقال : هذا كتاب يجمع من فروع الفقـه مـا لـم يجمع غيره». اهـ
Chapter Two: Study on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Third Section: Methodology of Imam al-Quduri and his style in his Mukhtasar
Statement that al-Quduri did not write an introduction to his Mukhtasar:
It is strongly believed that Imam al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, did not write an introduction to his Mukhtasar in fiqh, through which one could know his plan of work, the methodology he followed, the sources from which he derived the information of this book, and the like that authors usually mention in the introductions of their books. Hence we could not know anything of that except through study and what the careful researcher may glimpse.
The absence of an introduction to this Mukhtasar is something unanimously agreed upon by the manuscripts and printed copies of this Mukhtasar, according to my survey of dozens of its copies and dozens of its commentaries that include this Mukhtasar. Thus, all copies begin after the Basmalah and after the title: (Book of Purification), beginning with the verse of wudu with which al-Quduri opened his Mukhtasar, then mentioning the obligatory acts of wudu, and so on to the end of the Mukhtasar, without any introduction being mentioned for it.
Whereas the author of Kashf al-Zunun (1) mentioned that the beginning of the Mukhtasar starts with his saying: 'Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and the end is for the righteous, and blessings upon His Messenger Muhammad and all his family...' end. Like that.
I say: Perhaps that is due to the editor's interference.
Nevertheless, the possibility remains that this opening is from al-Quduri's own words, and Allah knows best.
*Also: In the printed copy of Kashf al-Zunun, when mentioning al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and its commentaries, a text appears that implies that al-Quduri wrote an introduction to his Mukhtasar, but the correct view is that it is not from al-Quduri's words.
After the author of Kashf al-Zunun (2) mentioned that Imam Husam al-Din al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad Makki (d. 598 AH) produced a supplement (Takmila) to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and wrote a commentary on it, he quoted from the introduction of his commentary on the Takmila his statement: (3) 'Al-Quduri said: This book compiles from the branches of fiqh what no other has compiled.'
(3) Thus in Kashf al-Zunun, but the correct view, and Allah knows best, is: (al-Razi said), because the previous words to this which the author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned are from al-Razi Husam al-Din's words about al-Quduri's Takmila and his commentary on it, and that he compiled in the Takmila what was missing from the Mukhtasar of the issues scattered in the abridgments such as al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Irshad, and Mujaz al-Farghani, so he said: 'This book compiles from the branches of fiqh what no other has compiled.' end.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a textual investigation into whether Imam al-Quduri wrote an introduction to his famous Mukhtasar. The author argues that based on examining dozens of manuscripts and printed editions, no introduction exists. All copies begin directly with the Basmalah and the title 'Kitab al-Taharah' and then the verse of wudu. The author rebuts the claim in Kashf al-Zunun that there is an opening praise, suggesting it may be an editor's addition. He also clarifies that a quote attributed to al-Quduri in Kashf al-Zunun is actually from al-Razi's commentary on the Takmila. This passage is important for understanding the textual history of the Mukhtasar and its transmission.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): Abridgment of Hanafi fiqh by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied as a foundational text in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Authenticity of Mukhtasar al-Quduri's Preface and Misattributed Praise
Critical discussion on preface authenticity and misattribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the misattribution of a famous praise statement to Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain the evidence that it actually refers to al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Core Idea
The praise 'Whoever memorizes this book…' belongs to al-Jami' al-Saghir, not Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

This lesson examines a common historical error in Hanafi textual studies. The introduction of Mukhtasar al-Quduri has been subject to debate: some sources claim al-Quduri wrote a preface, while others attribute laudatory remarks to early shaykhs. We will untangle the evidence to see why the famous phrase about memorization actually refers to Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir, and what this teaches us about source criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed claim in Kashf al-Zunun
Note that Kashf al-Zunun mentions that Mukhtasar al-Quduri opens with a specific phrase and implies that al-Quduri wrote an introduction. The author of the lesson questions this, suspecting scribal alteration.
Kashf al-Zunun is a reference work, not a primary source; its information must be verified.
2
Analyze the chronological problem
The praise 'Whoever memorizes this book…' is attributed to Abu Ali al-Shashi, who died before al-Quduri was born. Therefore, al-Shashi could not have praised a book written after his death.
Al-Shashi died in 344 AH; al-Quduri was born in 362 AH.
3
Trace the praise to its original source
Kashf al-Zunun itself records the same praise for al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad, and notes that early shaykhs tested judges on its memorization. The phrasing matches exactly.
The author of Kashf al-Zunun also mentions Husam al-Din al-Razi saying it about al-Jami' al-Saghir in his commentary.
4
Understand the implication for Hanafi textual history
The misattribution likely arose because later scholars confused the two works or because scribes inserted marginal notes into the introduction. This teaches us to verify quotations across multiple sources.
This is a cautionary tale in Hanafi scholarship about the importance of isnad even for textual attestations.

(۱) ترجم صاحب الجواهر المضية ٢٦٢/١ لأحمد بن محمد أبي علي الشاشي تلميذ الكرخي وأنه توفي سنة ٣٤٤هـ ، وقد ولد القدوري سنة ٣٦٢هـ، وعلى هذا فقد ولد بعد وفاة الشاشي هذا بنحو ١٨ سنة، وعليه يبعد تماماً أن يقـول الرازي هذا ما تقدم من الثناء على مختصر القدوري. وقد جعل كثيرون خطأ هذه المقولة في الثناء على مختصر القدوري، مع أن الشاشي المذكور هو قبل القدوري.
ومما يؤكد أن هذه المقولة ليست في مختصر القدوري، أن صاحب كشف الظنون ٥٦١/١ حين ذكر كتاب «الجامع الصغير»، للإمام محمد بن الحسن، ذكرهـا الثناء عليه، فقال: «وكان علي الرازي يقول : من فهم هذا الكتاب : فهو أفهـم أصحابنا، ومن حفظه : كان أحفظ أصحابنا، وأن المتقدمين من مشايخنا كانوا لا يقلدون أحداً القضاء حتى يمتحنوه، فإن حفظه : قلدوه، وإلا أمروه بالحفظ. اهـ. ويظهر أن حسام الدين الرازي قال هذا الثناء أيضاً في شرحه على الجامع الصغير كما قالها الشاشي، وزاد عليها ، وفي الأعلام ٢٥٦/٤ أن لعلي الرازي هذا شرحاً على الجامع الصغير، وأن منه جزءاً أو قطعة في شستربتي (٣٣١٦).
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri (Page 325) While the author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned that the beginning of the Mukhtasar starts with his words: 'Praise be to Allah, Lord of the Worlds, and the good end is for the righteous, and blessings upon His Messenger Muhammad and his family all together...' End quote. Like this. I say: Perhaps this is from the scribe's alterations. Nevertheless, the possibility remains that this opening is from al-Quduri himself, and Allah knows best. Also: In the printed edition of Kashf al-Zunun, when mentioning Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its commentaries, there is a text whose apparent meaning is that al-Quduri wrote an introduction to his Mukhtasar, but the correct view is that it is not from al-Quduri. (Y). So after the author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned that Imam Husam al-Din al-Razi Ali ibn Ahmad Makki (d. 598 AH) produced a supplement to Mukhtasar al-Quduri and commented on it, he quoted from the introduction of his commentary on the supplement his saying: (3) 'Al-Quduri said: This book gathers from the branches of fiqh what no other has gathered.' ... (1:1631/2; 2:1633/2) He is speaking. (3) Thus in Kashf al-Zunun, but the correct view, and Allah knows best, is: 'al-Razi said', because the previous words mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun are from al-Razi Husam al-Din and concern his supplement to al-Quduri and his commentary on it, and that he gathered in the supplement what was missing from the Mukhtasar from the issues spread in the abridgements like al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Irshad, and Mujaz al-Farghani, so he said: 'This book gathers from the branches of fiqh what no other has gathered.' End quote. [Page 326] Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri (Page 326) And Abu Ali al-Shashi used to say: 'Whoever memorizes this book is the most memorizing among our companions, and whoever understands it is the most understanding among our companions.' And it is a book of varying arrangement; because he began it to be a small book, then added to it after the acts of worship, so when he passed (al-Rahn), he expanded it in a comprehensive manner. And he intended (I) to dictate a comprehensive book in its commentary, relying in it on the clarification of branches and narrations, and introducing in it from the issues of disagreement what achieves independence. This error is what made some say that al-Quduri wrote an introduction to his Mukhtasar, including this sentence praising the Mukhtasar. (1) The author of al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya (1:262) translated Ahmad ibn Muhammad Abu Ali al-Shashi, a student of al-Karkhi, and that he died in 344 AH, while al-Quduri was born in 362 AH. So he was born about 18 years after the death of this al-Shashi. Therefore, it is very remote that al-Razi said this previous praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Many have mistakenly attributed this saying to praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, while the aforementioned al-Shashi came before al-Quduri. What confirms that this saying is not in Mukhtasar al-Quduri is that the author of Kashf al-Zunun (1:561), when mentioning the book 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, mentioned this praise for it, saying: 'Ali al-Razi used to say: Whoever understands this book is the most understanding among our companions, and whoever memorizes it is the most memorizing among our companions, and that the early shaykhs among us would not appoint anyone as judge until they tested him; if he memorized it, they appointed him; otherwise they ordered him to memorize.' End quote. It appears that Husam al-Din al-Razi also said this praise in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir as al-Shashi said it, and added to it. In al-A'lam (4:256) that this Ali al-Razi has a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir, and that a part or fragment of it is in Chester Beatty (3316).
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a historical-critical analysis of the preface of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author discusses whether the opening words attributed to al-Quduri are genuine or later scribal additions. He cites Kashf al-Zunun, which claims al-Quduri wrote an introduction, but the author argues this is a mistake. The praise often quoted about memorizing the book—'Whoever memorizes this book is the most memorizing among our companions'—was actually said by Abu Ali al-Shashi about al-Jami' al-Saghir, not Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author provides evidence: Abu Ali al-Shashi died before al-Quduri was born, so he could not have praised al-Quduri's work. Additionally, the same praise is recorded in Kashf al-Zunun for al-Jami' al-Saghir. This lesson clarifies a common misattribution in Hanafi textual history, emphasizing the importance of accurate transmission.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A famous abridgement of Hanafi fiqh by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a foundational text for memorization.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A collection of hadith by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing legal hadith and sayings of the Hanafi imams.
كشف الظنون (Kashf al-Zunun): A bibliographic encyclopedia of Islamic books and authors by Mustafa ibn Abdallah Katib Chelebi (Hajji Khalifa), used to reference works and their introductions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Imam Muhammad said it about al-Jami' al-Saghir

Key Takeaway
Always verify the chain of attribution for textual praises; chronological and cross-referencing checks prevent historical errors in Hanafi studies.

The Global Reach of Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Publications and Translations
Biographical and publication history of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the publication history and linguistic spread of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain why it became a globally studied text in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri spread across continents through editions, commentaries, and translations, becoming a cornerstone of Hanafi learning.

This passage gives us a glimpse into the remarkable journey of Imam al-Quduri's concise manual. Beyond being a mere primer, the Mukhtasar has been printed in countless editions, spawned major commentaries, and even crossed linguistic borders into Persian, Turkish, German, and French. Understanding this reach helps you appreciate the authority and centrality of this text in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core subject
Recognize that this passage is about the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text, and note the context: it is from a commentary (al-Lubab) discussing the text's history.
This is not a fiqh ruling but a front matter introduction.
2
Note the publication pattern
Observe that editions number in the thousands and pages range 120-130, indicating a concise but densely packed work.
3
Identify the commentary tradition
The Mukhtasar is printed both independently and within commentaries like al-Lubab and al-Jawharah, showing its role as a matn with sharh.
These commentaries are key references in the Hanafi curriculum.
4
Map the linguistic reach
List the translations: Persian (Bombay, 1307 AH), Turkish commentary (Istanbul, 1281 AH), partial German (Nikah, 1832) and French (Jihad, 1829).
This early European translation indicates Orientalist interest and the text's global relevance.
5
Reflect on significance
Consider why the text gained such widespread use: brevity, authority, and being a standard curriculum text in the Indian subcontinent and beyond.

The Second Chapter: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Mustafa al-Babi, year 1377 AH. Page 357. Thus editions continued here and there, and it is still being printed, and every edition is no less than thousands of copies. * Its number of pages in previous editions was between 120 medium-sized pages, densely packed in its words and lines, up to approximately 130 pages. All this, along with its other editions printed within commentaries of al-Quduri such as al-Lubab, al-Jawharah, and other numerous glosses spread in the lands of India, Sindh, and Pakistan. Also, it has been printed translated into several languages, including an edition translated into Persian in Bombay, India, in 1307 AH, and printed with a commentary in Turkish in Istanbul in 1281 AH, done by Amin Fahmi Pasha. Commentary
This passage is a biographical and historical account of Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. The author discusses the widespread publication of the Mukhtasar, noting that each edition runs into thousands of copies. He mentions that earlier editions ranged from 120 to 130 pages, with dense text. The work has been printed not only independently but also as part of major commentaries and super-commentaries (hawashi) such as al-Lubab and al-Jawharah, which are used extensively in the Indian subcontinent. Furthermore, the Mukhtasar has been translated into several languages: a Persian translation from Bombay (1307 AH), a Turkish commentary (1281 AH) by Amin Fahmi Pasha, and partial translations of the Nikah and Jihad sections into German (1832 CE) and French (1829 CE) respectively. The passage ends with praise to Allah for the widespread benefit of this work. This section serves as a front matter introduction, highlighting the global impact and enduring legacy of al-Quduri's concise manual.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). It is one of the most widely studied primers in the Hanafi madhhab.
اللباب (al-Lubab): A famous commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH). It is one of the key explanations used in the Hanafi curriculum.

Two Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: al-Aqta' and Ibn Qutlubugha
Biographical and bibliographical account of two commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two major Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and state their authors and subjects.

Core Idea
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri generated a rich commentary tradition, with al-Aqta's al-Muqni' and Ibn Qutlubugha's Taqrib al-Gharib serving distinct purposes.

This lesson introduces two important works within the Hanafi commentary tradition on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Understanding these works gives you insight into how scholars built upon foundational fiqh texts, focusing on concise explanation and hadith clarification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. Its small size and great benefit attracted many commentators.
Al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) authored the Mukhtasar, which became a core text in Hanafi curricula.
2
Meet al-Aqta' and his al-Muqni'
Al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), a student of al-Quduri, wrote al-Muqni' as a concise commentary (sharh saghir) highlighting subtle points (nukat latifa) in each issue.
This commentary is known as al-Sharh al-Saghir, contrasting with larger commentaries.
3
Understand Taqrib al-Gharib's role
Ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH) compiled Taqrib al-Gharib to explain the rare (gharib) hadiths that appear in al-Aqta's commentary, facilitating hadith comprehension within fiqh study.
This work is a specialized hadith commentary tied directly to a fiqh commentary.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري

المقنع شرح مختصر القدوري (الشرح الصغير). للأقطع: أحمد بن محمد تلميذ القدوري، المتوفى سنة ٤٧٤هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. وقد وجد عنوان هذا الشرح بهذا الاسم: (المقنع): على صفحة العنوان في النسخ الخطية له. ومن هذا الشرح المختصر نسخة في مركز البحث العلمي بمكة المكرمة، برقم ٢٦٣ ، في (۱۷۳) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (٢١) سطراً، وتاريخ نسخها سنة ٩٦٦هـ ، مصوّرة عن النسخة الأزهرية بالقاهرة، برقم ٢١٤٧. وقد جاء في مقدمة مؤلفه ما يلي: «الحمد لله حق حمده، فقد كثُرت رغبة المتعلمين في معرفة هذا المختصر في الفقه الذي جَمَعـه أبو الحسين القدوري، لصغر حجمه، وعظم فائدته، فأشرتُ في كل مسألة إلى نكتة لطيفة ...... الخ

تقريب الغريب، وهو شرح لغريب أحاديث شرح الأقطع. للإمام العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا المتوفى سنة ٨٧٩هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.

نسبه له السخاوي في ترجمته في الضوء اللامع، وصاحب كشف الظنون. ومنه نسخة في مكتبة لا له لي [؟] (۸۳۹) [؟]، في (۹۷) ورقة من القطع الصغير، بخط المؤلف ، جاء على طرتها بخط المؤلف : كتاب تقريب الغريب صنعة كاتبه العبد الفقير إلى الله تعالى قاسم بن قطلوبغا الحنفي. . اهـ

وقال في مقدمته ... وبعد : فيقول فقير رحمة ربه الغني قاسم بن قطلوبغا الحنفي : هذا كتاب ذكرتُ فيه غريب الأحاديث المذكورة في شرح مختصر القدوري، للشيخ الإمام أبي نصر أحمد بن محمد البغدادي، الشهير بالأقطع رحمه الله تعالى، على حسب مقتضى الحال، وأسأل الله سبحانه تحقيق الأماني في الحال والمآل». اهـ ويَنْبَهُ هنا أن ابن العماد ذكر في شذرات الذهب نقلاً عن البقاعي في كتابه : عنوان الزمان، أن للإمام العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا كتاباً في تخريج أحاديث شرح القدوري للأقطع، في مجلد لطيف. اهـ
The third chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Al-Muqni' Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the small commentary). By al-Aqta': Ahmad ibn Muhammad, student of al-Quduri, died 474 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And the title of this commentary was found with this name: (al-Muqni') on the title page in its manuscript copies. And of this concise commentary there is a copy in the Center for Scientific Research in Mecca, number 263, in 173 folios, each page 21 lines, its copying date 966 AH, photographed from the Azhar copy in Cairo, number 2147. And in its author's introduction came the following: "Praise be to Allah as He deserves, for the desire of learners has increased to know this concise work in fiqh compiled by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, due to its small size and great benefit, so I pointed out in each issue a subtle point... etc." Taqrib al-Gharib, which is a commentary on the strange hadiths of Sharh al-Aqta'. By the Imam, the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, died 879 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Sakhawi attributed it to him in his biography in al-Daw' al-Lami', and so did the author of Kashf al-Zunun. And there is a copy of it in the library of... (839?), in 97 folios of small size, in the author's handwriting, on its cover in the author's handwriting: "Kitab Taqrib al-Gharib, work of its writer, the poor servant in need of Allah Almighty, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi." ... and he said in his introduction: "... After: the poor one of the mercy of his Rich Lord, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi, says: This is a book in which I mentioned the strange hadiths mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by the Shaykh Imam Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, known as al-Aqta', may Allah have mercy on him, according to the requirement of the situation, and I ask Allah Almighty to fulfill hopes in the present and the future." ... And it is noted here that Ibn al-Imad mentioned in Shadharat al-Dhahab, quoting from al-Biqa'i in his book 'Unwan al-Zaman, that the Imam, the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha had a book on the takhrij of the hadiths of Sharh al-Quduri of al-Aqta', in a slim volume.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographical account from the book al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, which is itself a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author, al-Maydani, is listing commentaries written on the Mukhtasar. Here he discusses two works: First, al-Muqni' by al-Aqta' (Ahmad ibn Muhammad), a student of al-Quduri who died in 474 AH. This is a concise commentary (شرح صغير) that points out subtle points in each issue. A manuscript copy exists in Mecca. Second, Taqrib al-Gharib by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), which explains the rare hadiths found in al-Aqta's commentary. Ibn Qutlubugha's work focuses on gharib al-hadith (unusual words in hadith texts) as they appear in al-Aqta's commentary. The passage notes that a manuscript of Taqrib al-Gharib in the author's own hand exists in a library (possibly 'Lah Lah' or similar). The text also cites later historians al-Sakhawi, Kashf al-Zunun, and Ibn al-Imad, confirming the attribution and mentioning another work by Ibn Qutlubugha on takhrij (source verification) of hadiths in al-Aqta's commentary. As a Hanafi biographical note, this shows the scholarly tradition of commenting on the foundational text of al-Quduri and the importance of hadith explanation in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الأقطع (al-Aqta'): The nickname of Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, a Hanafi jurist and student of al-Quduri, author of al-Muqni' commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
تقريب الغريب (Taqrib al-Gharib): A work by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha explaining rare (gharib) hadiths that appear in al-Aqta's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) A biography of al-Quduri

Key Takeaway
Al-Aqta's al-Muqni' provides concise fiqh commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, while Ibn Qutlubugha's Taqrib al-Gharib clarifies the rare hadiths within that commentary.

Three Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Listing and describing three commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and distinguish between works of gharib al-hadith and takhrij.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri inspired multiple commentaries; knowing them deepens your grasp of Hanafi legal transmission.

In the Hanafi tradition, the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri is a foundational text that has generated a rich body of commentary. This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri introduces three important commentaries, highlighting their authors, content, and manuscript variations. Understanding these works not only aids in locating source material but also reflects the scholarly care in preserving and explaining the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
List the three commentaries
Identify each commentary mentioned in the passage: Taqrib al-Gharib by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri (also called Fawa'id al-Quduri) by Khawahrizade, and another Sharh by al-Sabbāghī al-Madini.
The first is not a direct commentary but a work on gharib hadith.
2
Identify authors and their backgrounds
Note the full names and death dates: Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), Khawahrizade (d. 483 AH), and al-Sabbāghī (d. after 540 AH). Recognise that al-Sabbāghī studied under Abu al-Yusr al-Bazudi.
These dates help place the commentaries in Hanafi history.
3
Distinguish gharib from takhrij
Understand the difference: gharib works explain unusual hadith terms; takhrij traces the original sources. The author clarifies that Qutlubugha's work is gharib, not takhrij, based on the introduction.
This precision is crucial for scholarly referencing.
4
Note manuscript evidence and naming variations
Observe that Khawahrizade's commentary is sometimes titled 'Fawa'id al-Quduri' in certain manuscripts. Recognise that such variations can affect identification.
Bibliographical awareness prevents confusion.

(۲) كما كتب إلي بذلك الأخ العزيز الأستاذ محمد فاتح قايا من اسطنبول، جزاه الله خيراً، وينظر الفهرس الشامل ٤٦٠/٥ ، ومعجم المخطوطات الموجودة في مكتبات اسطنبول والأناطولي (۳۸۷۸).
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. (1) 367: Al-Sakhawi attributed it to him in his biography in al-Daw' al-Lami', and the author of Kashf al-Zunun. And there is a copy in the library of Laleli [?], (839), in (97) folios of small size, in the author's handwriting. On its cover in the author's handwriting: 'Kitab Taqrib al-Gharib, the work of its writer, the poor servant of Allah, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi.' And he said in his introduction: '... After: The poor in need of his Lord's mercy, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi, says: This is a book in which I have mentioned the gharib (unusual) hadiths mentioned in the Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Shaykh Imam Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, known as al-Aqta', may Allah have mercy on him, according to the requirement of the situation, and I ask Allah Almighty to fulfill hopes in the present and the future.' And it is noted here that Ibn al-Imad mentioned in Shadharat al-Dhahab, quoting from al-Biqa'i in his book 'Unwan al-Zaman, that Imam al-Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha had a book on the takhrij of hadiths of Sharh al-Quduri by al-Aqta', in a slim volume. I say: The correct view is that it is on the gharib hadiths of Sharh al-Aqta', not on its takhrij, as stated earlier from the author's words in his introduction to the book. 4- Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Khawahrizade Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Bukhari, known as Bakr Khawahrizadeh, died in 483 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Thus the name of this commentary is mentioned as 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' in most copies of the book. And it appears as 'Fawa'id al-Quduri' in the copy of Hasan Husni Pasha (421) in Istanbul, in (164) folios, and similarly in the copy of Nafiz Pasha in Istanbul (274), in (136) folios. And Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbāghī al-Madini, Abu al-Makarim Abd al-Karim ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ali, who studied under Abu al-Yusr al-Bazudi Muhammad ibn Muhammad. (1) His biography is in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 3/141, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p.163, Taj al-Tarajim p.259, but they did not mention this book in his biography; Hadiyat al-Arifin 2/76, and it mentions that among his works is Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri. (2) As written to me by the dear brother, Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya from Istanbul, may Allah reward him, and see al-Fihris al-Shamil 5/460, and Mu'jam al-Makhtutat al-Mawjuda fi Maktabat Istanbul wa al-Anaduli (3878).
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage from Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri is a biographical and bibliographical survey listing three important Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The first is Taqrib al-Gharib by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), which focuses on explaining unusual hadiths found in al-Aqta's commentary. The author clarifies that this work is a gharib al-hadith compilation, not a takhrij as some claimed. The second is by Khawahrizade Abu Bakr al-Bukhari (d. 483 AH), also known as Bakr Khawahrizadeh, whose commentary is sometimes titled Fawa'id al-Quduri. The third is by Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbāghī al-Madini (d. after 540 AH), who studied under Abu al-Yusr al-Bazudi. The passage provides manuscript details and references to verify the works, reflecting the scholarly care in preserving the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
شروح مختصر القدوري (shurūḥ mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): Commentaries on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational text of Hanafi fiqh.
تقريب الغريب (taqrīb al-gharīb): A work by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha explaining unusual (gharib) hadiths found in a specific commentary.
تخريج (takhrij): The process of tracing and citing the original sources of hadiths; distinguished from gharib work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Knowing the commentators and their works on Mukhtasar al-Quduri enriches your understanding of Hanafi fiqh transmission and textual history.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, title variants, and manuscript significance of Khwahrizadah's Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Khwahrizadah's commentary is a foundational Hanafi text, also known as Fawa'id al-Quduri.

This lesson introduces you to a key early commentary on the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, one of the most important texts in the Hanafi school. Understanding its author, alternate titles, and manuscript tradition helps you appreciate the chain of transmission and commentary that shaped Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Find the full name of the commentator and his death date. This gives the historical context of the commentary.
The author is Khwahrizadah, a Hanafi scholar from Bukhara who died in 483 AH.
2
Note the title variants
The text is primarily called Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri, but some manuscripts refer to it as Fawa'id al-Quduri. Understand why variant titles occur (sometimes scribal or regional preferences).
Knowing the alternative title helps in cataloguing and identifying the work in different libraries.
3
Examine manuscript evidence
The passage mentions two manuscript copies with their locations and folio counts. This shows how the text has been preserved and transmitted.
Manuscript details provide clues about the work's circulation and popularity.
4
Assess the commentary's importance
Reflect on why this commentary was written and its role in the Hanafi curriculum. Early commentaries like this shape later understanding.
Khwahrizadah's work is a link between the matn of al-Quduri and later supercommentaries.

Al-Sabbāghī's Sharh al-Quduri: Significance and Transmission
Biographical entry for al-Sabbāghī's Sharh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, teacher, and scholarly significance of al-Sabbāghī's Sharh al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Sabbāghī's commentary contains unique benefits not found elsewhere.

This biographical entry introduces the Hanafi scholar al-Sabbāghī and his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. His teacher was Abū al-Yusr al-Bazdawī, a prominent jurist who died in 493 AH. The commentary is cited by later authorities like Qāsim in Tāj al-Tarājim and praised by al-Zāhidī for containing great benefits not found elsewhere. Understanding the chain of transmission and scholarly assessment helps us appreciate the work's place in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and His Lineage
Extract the full name and honorific of al-Sabbāghī from the text: Rukn al-A'immah al-Sabbāghī al-Madīnī, Abu al-Makārim 'Abd al-Karīm ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Alī.
The honorific 'Rukn al-A'immah' indicates his high rank among Hanafi scholars.
2
Identify His Teacher and the Death Date
The text states he studied under Abū al-Yusr al-Bazdawī (Muhammad ibn Muhammad), who died in 493 AH. This establishes the scholarly chain.
Abū al-Yusr al-Bazdawī is a well-known Hanafi jurist.
3
Determine the Scholarly Assessment
The text quotes al-Zāhidī saying the commentary contains 'great benefits not found in others'. This indicates its unique value.
Such praise from a later scholar suggests the work is a key reference.
4
Note the Sources Mentioning This Commentary
The commentary is mentioned by al-Allāmah Qāsim in Tāj al-Tarājim and Taṣḥīḥ al-Quduri, and also in Kashf al-Ẓunūn with a marginal note.
These are major bibliographic works, confirming the commentary's circulation.

A quotation from al-Zāhidī in al-Mujtabā, reported by Walī al-Dīn, praises the commentary for containing unique and great benefits. This indicates the work's high scholarly value.

Examining a Biographical Note: Al-Rāzī and His Hall Mushkilāt
Biographical entry with a textual discrepancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the work Hall Mushkilāt Mushkil al-Quduri and state the scholarly discrepancy regarding its author's death date.

Core Idea
Verify author identities – a single name can hide multiple scholars.

This lesson introduces a short biographical note about a Hanafi commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The passage highlights a factual discrepancy between sources regarding the author's name and death year. Such variations are common in classical works and require careful verification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work
Read the Arabic title: حل مشكلات مشكل القدوري. Note that it is a commentary resolving difficult points in al-Quduri's text.
The title may appear as 'Mushkilāt' or 'Mushkil'.
2
Note the author's name
The work is attributed to al-Rāzī, with full name: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muzaffar al-Rāzī.
3
Spot the discrepancy
al-Baghdādī and Qāsim give his death as 500 AH, but Kashf al-Ẓunūn gives 642 AH and adds 'Shams al-A’immah al-Kardarī'. This suggests there may be two different scholars or an error.
4
Understand the implication
When citing classical works, one must verify the author's biography to avoid conflating different individuals. This ensures accurate attribution in fiqh references.

Verifying Authorship: The Case of Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri
Resolving confusion over the identity of a commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply chronological verification to identify the correct author of a classical Hanafi text.

Core Idea
Chronological impossibility disproves a famous attribution – dates are decisive in textual criticism.

A text widely attributed to Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi is actually by Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi. The key evidence is simple: Abu al-Layth died too early to have commented on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. This lesson trains you to use biographical data as a critical tool in Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested attribution
Note the text and the author it is commonly attributed to: Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri attributed to Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
Abu al-Layth is a well-known Hanafi scholar, but not the commentator here.
2
Extract the death and birth dates
Record the death date of Abu al-Layth (around 383 AH) and the birth date of al-Quduri (362 AH).
Dates may vary; the author gives multiple possibilities: 375, 383, 393 AH.
3
Assess chronological plausibility
Calculate the age of al-Quduri when he wrote his Mukhtasar. He was born in 362 AH, so by 383 AH he would be only 21 years old. It is very unlikely he authored a mature legal compendium before age 20.
The argument does not require exact dates, only the reasonable inference.
4
Conclude the correct author
Since Abu al-Layth died before al-Quduri could have written the Mukhtasar, the commentary must be by another scholar with a similar name: Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi (d. 552 AH).
This is confirmed by manuscript evidence (Zahiriyya Library).

أعلام النبلاء ٣٢٢/١٦، الجواهر المضية
٥٤٤/٣ ، كشف الظنون ١٢٢٠/٢.
(۳) فهرس مخطوطات الظاهرية (الفقه الحنفي) ٤٤٢/١.
10. Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri. By Muhammad bin Ahmad al-Samarqandi, may Allah have mercy on him, died in the year 552 AH. It is stated in Kashf al-Zunun: 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri, by the Imam Abu al-Layth Nasr bin Muhammad al-Samarqandi, and it is a brief commentary. So it is said. But perhaps it is the commentary of Abu Bakr 'Ala' al-Din Muhammad bin Ahmad al-Samarqandi, the exegete and author of Mizan al-Usul, who died in 552 AH.' End quote from Kashf al-Zunun. I (the author) say: The death of Abu al-Layth Nasr bin Muhammad was in 383 AH, or 375 AH, or 393 AH, while the birth of Imam al-Quduri was in 362 AH. It is very unlikely that al-Quduri compiled his Mukhtasar before the age of twenty, and that Abu al-Layth commented on it. Therefore, this commentary is by Muhammad bin Ahmad al-Samarqandi, who died in 552 AH. A copy of this commentary exists in al-Zahiriyya Library, number 9183, consisting of ...
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is a biographical clarification regarding the authorship of Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri. The text begins by citing Kashf al-Zunun, which attributes the work to Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (d. 383/375/393 AH). However, the author of al-Lubab (likely 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani) refutes this by pointing out the chronological impossibility: Quduri was born in 362 AH, so he would have written his Mukhtasar before age 20 for Abu al-Layth to have commented on it, which is highly improbable. The correct author is Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi (d. 552 AH), a known commentator and author of Mizan al-Usul. The passage also notes that a manuscript of this commentary exists in the al-Zahiriyya Library in Damascus (number 9183). This illustrates careful historical verification in Hanafi scholarship.

Key Terms
شرح مشكلات القدوري (Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri): A commentary on difficult passages of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, originally attributed to Abu al-Layth but correctly assigned to Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi.
أبو الليث السمرقندي (Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi): A famous Hanafi scholar (d. 383/375/393 AH), author of many works, but not the commentator of Mushkilat al-Quduri.
كشف الظنون (Kashf al-Zunun): A famous bibliographic encyclopedia by Hajji Khalifa, which contains the disputed attribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the commentary Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri not by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi?
A) Abu al-Layth lived after al-Quduri
B) Abu al-Layth died before al-Quduri could have written his Mukhtasar
C) Abu al-Layth was a Shafi'i
D) Al-Quduri did not write a Mukhtasar

Key Takeaway
Chronological consistency is a fundamental tool for verifying authorship of classical texts.

Al-Lubab: A Medium Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describing al-Yazdi's commentary Al-Lubab and its manuscripts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose, author, and relationship of Al-Lubab to Al-Tahdhib, and identify the level of detail in Al-Lubab as a commentary.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a concise commentary that points to each issue without elaboration, relying on Al-Tahdhib for full details.

In this lesson, we examine the biographical and textual background of al-Yazdi's Al-Lubab, a medium-length commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding its place helps you navigate the layers of Hanafi commentaries, from concise matn to exhaustive sharh. You will learn how al-Yazdi himself described his work and why it remains a valuable teaching text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full title.
Find the author's name, lineage, and honorifics as given in the passage. Note his title: al-Yazdi, and his kunya: Abu Sa'd al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn.
Al-Yazdi is a Hanafi scholar and commentator.
2
Note his death date and the completion date of his earlier work Al-Tahdhib.
The passage does not give a death date but places it after 559 AH, based on the completion date of Al-Tahdhib. Record this for historical context.
Al-Tahdhib is a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Understand the purpose of Al-Lubab as stated in its introduction.
Al-Yazdi explicitly says that Al-Lubab points to each issue of Mukhtasar al-Quduri without elongation. It is a concise guide.
He invites those wanting more to refer to Al-Tahdhib.
4
Recognize the relationship to Al-Tahdhib.
Al-Lubab is not a standalone exhaustive work; it is a concise derivative that refers to the comprehensive commentary Al-Tahdhib for complete explanations.
Thus, the two works are complementary, not independent.
5
Appreciate the manuscript evidence and its significance.
The passage lists several manuscripts with dates, indicating the work's circulation and preservation. This shows its importance in the Hanafi tradition.
The oldest copies date from the 6th century AH.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
١١ - اللباب في شرح الكتاب (شرح مختصر القدوري). لليزدي الإمام شيخ الإسلام قاضي القضاة جمال الدين (جـلال الدين أبي سعد المطهر بن الحسين (الحسن) بـن سـعـد اليزدي (٢)، ولم يُحدد مترجموه سنة وفاته، لكنها كانت بعد سنة ٥٥٩هـ. فقد ذكر صاحب كشف الظنون (۳) أن للمطهر هذا شرحاً على الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن سماه التهذيب، في مجلدين، فرغ من تأليفه سنة ٥٥٩هـ. وقد ذكر اليزدي في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري (اللباب) أنـه يشير إشارة لكل مسألة من مسائل مختصر القدوري بدون إطالة، ومن أراد الزيادة فليراجع التهذيب شرح الجامع الصغير، ففيه غنى، حيث علل فيه للمسائل والأحكام باستيفاء. وعلى هذا، فشرح اللباب شرح متوسط، يذكر فيه بعض الأدلة، دون استيفاء. وللكتاب عدة نُسخ، تنظر في الفهرس الشامل، ومن أقدمها نسخة بتاريخ سنة ٥٧١هـ، ونسخة أخرى بتاريخ ٥٧٦هـ، في المكتبة الوطنية في جوروم (۱۵۲۸)، ونسخة في داماد زاده (۹۰۲)، نُسخت سنة ٦٦٤هـ، كما ذكر هذا الأخ الكريم الشيخ محمد فاتح قايا، فيما كتبه إلى مشكوراً من اسطنبول، جزاه الله خيراً. وقد يسر الله لي تصوير نسخة دار الكتب الوطنية بتونس، المصوّرة في الجامعة الإسلامية بالمدينة المنورة. وتقع هذه النسخة في (۲۳٥) ورقة وفي كل صفحة (۲۱) سطراً، وفيها طمس في مقدمة المؤلف، وهي بخط مغربي بتاريخ سنة ١١٤٨ هـ، نسخها أحمد بن علي الرشيد. وقد ذكر القرشي في الجواهر المضية في ترجمة الإمام منصور بن أبي بكر بن منصور الصديقي السنجاري الناهشي، أنه كان يحفظ اللباب في شرح القدوري، لليزدي، ولم يذكر القرشي سنة وفاته.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 11 - Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri). By al-Yazdi, the Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, Qadi al-Qudat, Jamal al-Din (Jalal al-Din) Abu Sa'd al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn (al-Hasan) ibn Sa'd al-Yazdi. His biographers did not specify his year of death, but it was after 559 AH. The author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned that al-Mutahhar had a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan called al-Tahdhib, in two volumes, completed in 559 AH. Al-Yazdi mentioned in the introduction to his commentary on al-Quduri (Al-Lubab) that he points to each issue of Mukhtasar al-Quduri without elaboration, and whoever wants more should refer to al-Tahdhib, the commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir, for it is sufficient, as he explained the issues and rulings thoroughly. Therefore, Al-Lubab is a medium commentary, mentioning some proofs without completeness. The book has several manuscripts, see al-Fihris al-Shamil. Among the oldest is a copy dated 571 AH, another dated 576 AH in the National Library in Chorom (1528), and a copy in Damad Zada (902) copied in 664 AH, as mentioned by the noble brother Shaykh Muhammad Fatih Qaya in his letter to me from Istanbul, may Allah reward him. Allah facilitated for me to photograph a copy from the National Library in Tunis, which is microfilmed at the Islamic University in Medina. This copy consists of 235 folios, each page has 21 lines, with some obliteration in the author's introduction, written in Maghribi script dated 1148 AH, copied by Ahmad ibn Ali al-Rashid. Al-Qurashi mentioned in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya in the biography of Imam Mansur ibn Abi Bakr ibn Mansur al-Siddiqi al-Sanjari al-Nahishi that he memorized Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri by al-Yazdi, but al-Qurashi did not mention his death date.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory section of the book, presenting a biographical and bibliographical overview of the commentary 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' by al-Yazdi. The author first identifies the work as a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and provides the full name of its author: al-Yazdi, whose full lineage and titles are given. His death is not precisely known but is placed after 559 AH based on the completion date of his earlier work 'al-Tahdhib'. Al-Yazdi himself explains the nature of his commentary in his introduction: 'Al-Lubab' is a concise guide, pointing out each issue without lengthy discussion, directing those who desire deeper elaboration to his earlier comprehensive commentary 'al-Tahdhib' on al-Jami' al-Saghir. Thus, 'Al-Lubab' is a medium-length commentary, mentioning some proofs but not exhaustively. The passage then lists multiple manuscripts of 'Al-Lubab', citing specific library locations and dates, demonstrating the scholarly effort to trace and preserve the text. It concludes with a note that Imam al-Qurashi recorded in 'al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya' that someone memorized 'Al-Lubab', which attests to its value and circulation among Hanafi scholars. This information is crucial for understanding the place of 'Al-Lubab' in the Hanafi tradition: it is a middle-level commentary, bridging the concise matn and the extensive sharh, and serves as a teaching text for students who want more than just the matn but not the full length of 'al-Tahdhib'.

Key Terms
اللباب في شرح الكتاب (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab): A medium-length commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Yazdi, summarizing rulings with some proofs but without exhaustive detail.
اليزدي (al-Yazdi): Abu Sa'd al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn al-Yazdi, a Hanafi scholar and commentator, author of Al-Lubab and Al-Tahdhib.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied and commented upon.
التهذيب (al-Tahdhib): Al-Yazdi's earlier comprehensive commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, completed in 559 AH.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between Al-Lubab and Al-Tahdhib according to al-Yazdi?
A) Al-Lubab is a summary of Al-Tahdhib, referring readers to it for more detail.
B) Al-Tahdhib is a summary of Al-Lubab.
C) They are two completely unrelated works.
D) Al-Lubab is a commentary on Al-Tahdhib.

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a concise medium commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, directing readers to al-Yazdi's exhaustive work Al-Tahdhib for deeper study.

Al-Kirmani and His Commentary Al-Musta‘dhab
Biographical note on a Hanafi commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Kirmani as the author of al-Musta‘dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri and explain the significance of his commentary in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Musta‘dhab is a Hanafi commentary by al-Kirmani on al-Quduri's pivotal Mukhtasar.

This lesson introduces you to a key figure in the Hanafi textual tradition: Muhammad ibn Mukarram ibn Shu‘ban, known as al-Kirmani. His commentary al-Musta‘dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri is one of many works written to explain and expand upon Imam al-Quduri's foundational summary of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding the authors and their chains helps you assess the authority of the rulings you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his credentials
In the passage, find the name of the author (al-Kirmani) and his full name, title (imam, faqih), and death date (593 AH). Note that he is explicitly labeled a Hanafi jurist.
The date is given as 593 AH with a note that other years are also mentioned, but this is the primary.
2
Identify the work under discussion
Locate the title of the commentary: al-Musta‘dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri. Recognize that this is a sharh (commentary) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, which is a core Hanafi matn.
The title means 'The Pleasing in Explanation of al-Quduri'.
3
Note the evidence for attribution
The passage gives two sources: (1) al-Kirmani himself mentions his commentary in his other work al-Masalik fi al-Manasik, and (2) al-Baghdadi cites it in Hadiyat al-‘Arifin. This establishes the work's authenticity and its recognition in biographical literature.
These cross-references help in verifying the chain of transmission of the text.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi tradition
Reflect on the importance of such commentaries: they are not mere repetitions but analyses that clarify rulings, resolve apparent contradictions, and sometimes present preferred positions. Al-Kirmani's work is one link in a long chain of scholarship on al-Quduri.
Knowing the author and his other works (like al-Masalik fi al-Manasik on Hajj) gives you a fuller picture of his expertise.

Source Text

١٧ ـ المستعذب في شرح القدوري . للكرماني محمد بن مكرم بن شعبان الإمام الفقيه الحنفي صاحب : «المسالك في المناسك، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٣هـ، وقيل غير ذلك، رحمه الله تعالى. وقد ذكر هذا الشرح المؤلف نفسه في كتابه المسالك (۱). كما ذكره البغدادي في هدية العارفين (۲).
17. Al-Musta‘dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri. By al-Kirmani, Muhammad ibn Mukarram ibn Shu‘ban, the imam, the Hanafi jurist, author of 'al-Masalik fi al-Manasik', who died in 593 AH, and it is also said other than that, may Allah have mercy on him. He mentioned this commentary himself in his book al-Masalik (1). And al-Baghdadi mentioned it in Hadiyat al-‘Arifin (2).
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for a Hanafi scholar and his work. Al-Kirmani (d. 593 AH) was a Hanafi jurist who authored a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri titled 'al-Musta‘dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri'. He is also known for his work on Hajj rituals, 'al-Masalik fi al-Manasik'. The entry notes that al-Kirmani himself referenced this commentary in his other work, and it was also listed by al-Baghdadi in his biographical dictionary 'Hadiyat al-‘Arifin'. This commentary is among the many written on al-Quduri's foundational Hanafi text.

Key Terms
المستعذب في شرح القدوري (al-Musta‘dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri): Title of al-Kirmani's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
الكرماني (al-Kirmani): Nisba referring to the scholar Muhammad ibn Mukarram ibn Shu‘ban, a Hanafi jurist.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).

The 'Al-Qadi' Commentary: A Hanafi Biographical Note
Biographical entry for a Hanafi commentator from Yemen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name of al-Qadi al-‘Awfi and recall that his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri is known among Hanafis as 'al-Qadi'.

Core Idea
A Yemeni Hanafi judge's commentary became known simply as 'al-Qadi'.

This brief entry introduces us to a Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri authored by Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi ‘Awf, known as al-Qadi. The passage highlights how later Hanafi scholars referred to this work and provides clues about the author's death date through transmission evidence. Understanding such biographical notes helps us appreciate the chain of commentary tradition in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Locate the full name of the scholar: Abu al-‘Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi ‘Awf. Note his title 'al-Qadi' (the judge).
2
Recognize the commentary's popular name
Understand that among Hanafis, this commentary is simply called 'al-Qadi', after the author's title.
3
Establish the death date range
Since al-Kirmani (died 597 AH) quoted this commentary, the author must have died before 597 AH.
4
Connect to the broader tradition
Realize that such commentaries form a chain, with later scholars like al-Kirmani relying on earlier works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۸ - شرح مختصر القدوري. لأبي العباس أحمد بن الحسن بن أبي عوف، الإمام الفقيه المعروف بالقاضي، من علماء اليمن ذكر هذا الشرح علي القاري في طبقاته، وقال: هو الشرح المعروف عند الحنفية بـ: (القاضي) ولم يذكر سنة وفاته، وهي قبل سنة ٥٩٧هـ. وقد وجدت الكرماني صاحب المسالك في المناسك قد نقل عنه مراراً، وسماه : شرح القدوري للعوفي (٤)، ووفاة الكرماني مختلف فيها، والمرجح أنها كانت سنة ٥٩٧هـ، وعليه تكون وفاة صاحب هذا الشرح قبل ٥٩٧هـ، والله أعلم.
18. Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Abu al-‘Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi ‘Awf, the imam, the jurist known as al-Qadi, from the scholars of Yemen. ‘Ali al-Qari mentioned this commentary in his Tabaqat and said: 'It is the commentary known among the Hanafis as al-Qadi.' He did not mention his date of death, which is before 597 AH. And I found that al-Kirmani, author of al-Masalik fi al-Manasik, transmitted from it repeatedly and called it Sharh al-Quduri li al-‘Awfi (4). The death of al-Kirmani is disputed, and the preferred view is that it was 597 AH, and accordingly the author of this commentary died before 597 AH. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This entry introduces another Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri written by Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi ‘Awf, known as al-Qadi (the judge), a scholar from Yemen. The commentary is famously referred to among Hanafis as 'al-Qadi'. The text notes that although the exact date of his death is not recorded, it was before 597 AH, as al-Kirmani (who died in 597 AH) frequently quoted from it. This shows the transmission and reliance on this commentary by later Hanafi scholars. The entry also demonstrates the practice of naming commentaries after their authors, as in 'al-Qadi'.

Key Terms
القاضي (al-Qadi): Common name for the commentary by al-‘Awfi, referring to his title 'the judge'.
أبو العباس أحمد بن الحسن بن أبي عوف (Abu al-‘Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi ‘Awf): Full name of the scholar known as al-Qadi al-‘Awfi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-‘Awfi is known as 'al-Qadi', and its author likely died before 597 AH.

Al-Razi and His Concise Hanafi Commentary
Biographical entry for a Hanafi commentator and his concise work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, title, and scholarly significance of Khulasat al-Dala’il fi Tanqih al-Masa’il within the Hanafi commentary tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's Khulasat al-Dala’il is a concise yet comprehensive Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

This lesson introduces the final entry in the list of commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri – the Khulasat al-Dala’il fi Tanqih al-Masa’il by Husam al-Din al-Razi. Recognized as both useful and concise, this work reflects the rich tradition of Hanafi scholarship that sought to distill legal proofs into a compact form. By studying this entry, you will learn about the author, his scholarly profile, and how later scholars valued his contribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Work and Author
Locate the title 'Khulasat al-Dala’il fi Tanqih al-Masa’il' and note that it is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Identify the author as Husam al-Din ‘Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki al-Razi.
2
Note the Author's Scholarly Profile
Read the biographical details: al-Razi lived in Aleppo and Damascus, taught in both cities, and died in Damascus around 593 or 598 AH. This shows he was a prominent Hanafi scholar of the 6th century AH.
3
Understand the Praise from Later Scholars
Examine the quotations: Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari calls it a 'precious book', and Kashf al-Zunun describes it as 'useful, concise, and beneficial'. These endorsements indicate the work's high standing among Hanafi scholars.
The praise emphasizes both conciseness and benefit – key features for a commentary meant for memorization and quick reference.
4
Recognize Its Place in Hanafi Literature
Place this work among the many commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Its concise presentation of proofs (dala’il) distinguishes it from longer works like the Kifayah of al-‘Awfi. This shows how different commentaries served different pedagogical needs.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۹ - خلاصة الدلائل في تنقيح المسائل (شرح مختصر القدوري). للإمام حسام الدين علي بن أحمد بن مكي الرازي، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٨هـ، وقيل : ٥٩٣هـ، وكان قد سكن حلب ودمشق، ودرس فيهما، وتوفي رحمه الله بدمشق. قال اللكنوي: «قال ملا علي القاري: وَضَعَ الرازي كتاباً نفيساً على مختصر القدوري، وسماه خلاصة الدلائل». اهـ وقال صاحب كشف الظنون: «وهو شرح مفيد مختصر نافع». اهـ
19. Khulasat al-Dala’il fi Tanqih al-Masa’il (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri). By Imam Husam al-Din ‘Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki al-Razi, who died in 598 AH, and it is said: 593 AH. He lived in Aleppo and Damascus and taught in both, and he died, may Allah have mercy on him, in Damascus. Al-Lakhnawi said: 'Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari said: Al-Razi produced a precious book on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and named it Khulasat al-Dala’il.' And the author of Kashf al-Zunun said: 'It is a useful, concise, and beneficial commentary.'
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This final entry introduces al-Razi's commentary, 'Khulasat al-Dala’il fi Tanqih al-Masa’il' (The Summary of Evidences in Refining the Issues), which is a concise yet comprehensive commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author, Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 or 593 AH), was a Hanafi scholar who taught in Aleppo and Damascus. The entry praises the work through quotations: Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari calls it a 'precious book', and the bibliographer Hajji Khalifa (in Kashf al-Zunun) describes it as 'useful, concise, and beneficial'. This commentary is another example of the rich tradition of Hanafi scholarship on al-Quduri's text.

Key Terms
خلاصة الدلائل في تنقيح المسائل (Khulasat al-Dala’il fi Tanqih al-Masa’il): Title of al-Razi's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
حسام الدين الرازي (Husam al-Din al-Razi): Honorific name of the author ‘Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki al-Razi.

Analyzing a Hanafi Biographical Entry: Husam al-Din al-Razi's Khulasat al-Dala'il
Biographical and bibliographic entry about a Hanafi commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a Hanafi biographical entry (tarjama) and explain the significance of a commentary like Khulasat al-Dala'il within the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
A concise commentary can still be rich in evidence and inter-madhhab comparison.

This passage introduces a commentary on the foundational Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author, Husam al-Din al-Razi, produced a concise yet evidence-based work that also notes disagreements among madhhab imams. By analyzing this biographical entry, we learn how to extract information about author, work, and scholarly methodology from classical sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his biographical details.
From the passage, note the full name of the author: Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki al-Razi, known as Husam al-Din. Note his death year (around 597 or 598 AH), his teaching locations (Aleppo and Damascus), and place of death (Damascus).
Biographical details help establish the scholar's context and authority.
2
Identify the work and its relation to the base text.
Find the title of the commentary: Khulasat al-Dala'il fi Tanqih al-Masa'il. Recognize that it is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a standard Hanafi text.
Understanding the genre (sharh) and base text is key to assessing the work's scope.
3
Extract scholarly assessments of the work.
The passage cites Mulla Ali al-Qari, the author of Kashf al-Zunun, and al-Kawthari praising the commentary as 'beneficial', 'concise', and 'the best of the abridged commentaries'. Note these assessments.
Later scholars' evaluations indicate the work's acceptance and utility.
4
Analyze the author's methodology from his introduction.
Read the excerpt from the author's introduction. He explains that he wrote the commentary in response to complaints about other commentaries being too long or too short, aiming for a balanced approach that includes evidence and avoids tedium.
The author's own words reveal his scholarly goals.
5
Recognize the work's utility: includes evidence and inter-madhhab differences.
The passage explicitly states that despite its conciseness, the work includes evidence (adilla) and mentions disagreements among Hanafi imams, and occasionally with Malik and al-Shafi'i.
This feature makes it valuable for advanced beginners seeking deeper understanding.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
And the scholar al-Kawthari said: “The best of the abridged commentaries is: Khulasat
al-Dala'il.” End quote.
And despite it being a concise commentary, its author did not leave it devoid of some evidence, with brevity, and also addressed disagreement among the imams of the madhhab, and mentions the disagreement of Malik and al-Shafi'i occasionally.

... Afterwards: Hearts and natures have not ceased inclining to storing good remembrance, and souls and ambitions aspire to acquiring immense treasure, and in the direction of these two goals, and towards these two merits, I have favored with assistance and aid, and I have permitted kindness and support to one who complained about the length of some commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and their tediousness, and the brevity of some and their deficiency, and by refining a book consistent in wording and meaning with eloquence, similar in beginning and end in brevity and length.
This, along with my admission of scantiness of skill, and lack of advancement in the craft, but rather pure audacity, and ignorance and advancement (and pretentiousness?) purely, and undertaking to correct
the attribution of the father, and confirming the word of the Lord in His saying: “And man bore it; indeed, he was unjust and ignorant” (Quran 33:72). So whoever walks on the example of his father, and swims on the path of his brother: he has not committed a sin.
