Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry from the chapter on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It introduces the commentary 'Khulasat al-Dala'il fi Tanqih al-Masa'il' by Imam Husam al-Din Ali ibn Ahmad al-Razi. The text notes the uncertainty of his death year, suggesting 597 AH or 598 AH, and that he died in Damascus after teaching in Aleppo and Damascus. It cites authorities like Mulla Ali al-Qari and al-Kawthari praising the work for being beneficial and concise yet containing evidence and occasional mention of disagreements with Malik and al-Shafi'i. The passage then quotes from the author's introduction, where al-Razi explains his motivation to produce a commentary that avoids excessive length or excessive brevity, responding to complaints about other commentaries. He acknowledges his own shortcomings but proceeds with the task, citing Quran 33:72 about man's capacity. This establishes the scholarly utility and methodology of the work within the Hanafi tradition.

حسام الدين الرازي (Husam al-Din al-Razi): Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki al-Razi, a Hanafi jurist and author of Khulasat al-Dala'il, died around 598 AH.

The Three Glosses of Ibn al-Turkmani on Khulasat al-Dala'il
Bibliographic listing of glosses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of glosses written by Ibn al-Turkmani on al-Razi's Khulasat al-Dala'il and explain their purposes in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Turkmani's three glosses cover difficulties, omissions, and hadith criticism.

This passage introduces us to a key figure in Hanafi scholarship, Ibn al-Turkmani, and his three complementary glosses on al-Razi's commentary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding the purpose of each gloss reveals how later Hanafi scholars systematically built upon earlier works to refine and complete the school's legal corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and its commentary
The base text is Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise manual of Hanafi fiqh. Al-Razi wrote a commentary on it titled Khulasat al-Dala'il.
2
Recognize the author of the glosses
Ibn al-Turkmani (d. 744/745 AH) is a Hanafi scholar known for his work al-Jawhar al-Naqi. He wrote three glosses on al-Razi's commentary.
3
List the three glosses and their purposes
First gloss: solves difficulties and clarifies expressions. Second gloss: fills in issues omitted from al-Hidaya. Third gloss: discusses the hadiths cited in the commentary.
4
Understand the scholarly context
These glosses are super-commentaries that supplement the original commentary, demonstrating the layered nature of Hanafi legal literature.
Such glosses were common in later scholarship to expand and critique earlier works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Al-'Allama Qasim said: Ibn al-Turkmani has three glosses on al-Razi's Khulasat al-Dala'il: The first: in solving its difficulties, clarifying its perplexities, explaining its expressions, and interpreting its meanings for its memorizers. The second: in mentioning what he omitted from the issues of al-Hidaya. The third: in mentioning its hadiths and discussing them. End.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic entry from Chapter Three of a work on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It first mentions a note by al-Qurashi about seeing a manuscript of al-Khulasa (which is al-Razi's commentary) dated 545 AH. Then it lists the commentary of Ibn al-Turkmani, giving his full name, his famous work al-Jawhar al-Naqi, and his death date with a discrepancy. It quotes al-'Allama Qasim enumerating three distinct glosses (ta'aliq) written by Ibn al-Turkmani on al-Razi's Khulasat al-Dala'il. Each gloss serves a specific purpose: the first explains difficult points and clarifies expressions, the second fills in missing issues from al-Hidaya, and the third discusses the hadiths cited. This demonstrates the scholarly practice of writing comprehensive super-commentaries.

Key Terms
خلاصة الدلائل (Khulasat al-Dala'il): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by the Hanafi scholar Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A renowned concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri.
تعليقة (ta'liqa): A gloss or super-commentary that explains and expands upon a base text.

Al-Qurashi's Incomplete Commentary on Khulasat al-Dala'il
Bibliographic note identifying a commentary and its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, the work commented upon, and the extent of al-Qurashi's commentary on Khulasat al-Dala'il.

Core Idea
Not all commentaries are complete; al-Qurashi's work reaches only the Book of Partnership.

This lesson introduces a specific commentary on a key Hanafi text. Understanding the scope and authorship of such works is crucial for navigating the Hanafi scholarly tradition. We will parse a brief biographical note to extract essential details about al-Qurashi's commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work being commented on
Determine what the commentary is explaining. The passage states that Khulasat al-Dala'il is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Razi.
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi matn.
2
Identify the commentator
Name the author of the commentary. It is Imam Muhyi al-Din 'Abd al-Qadir ibn Muhammad al-Qurashi, who died in 775 AH.
Al-Qurashi is also known for his biographical work al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya.
3
Determine the extent of the commentary
Find out how far the commentary proceeds. The passage says it reached the Book of Partnership (Kitab al-Shirka).
This indicates the work is incomplete, as it does not cover the entire Mukhtasar.
4
Note the author's own cross-reference
Recognize that al-Qurashi himself confirmed his authorship in another work, al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il fi Takhrij Ahadith Khulasat al-Dala'il.
This cross-reference helps verify authorship and links related works.
5
Summarize the physical form
The surviving portion is contained in two volumes (mujalladayn).
Provides a concrete sense of the work's size.

Al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il: A Hadith Companion to Khulasat al-Dala'il
Biographical entry listing a hadith companion to Khulasat al-Dala'il

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of al-Qurashi's al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il in verifying hadiths within Khulasat al-Dala'il.

Core Idea
Al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il traces hadiths to their sources, strengthening Hanafi proof-texts.

This lesson introduces a specialized work by the Hanafi scholar al-Qurashi, designed to complement the famous Khulasat al-Dala'il of al-Razi. Understanding its role helps you appreciate how later Hanafis systematically verified the hadith evidence underpinning their school's rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and author
Note the full title 'al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il ila Ma'rifat Ahadith Khulasat al-Dala'il' and the author al-Qurashi. The title itself reveals the book's function.
2
Parse the title's components
Break down the title: 'al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il' (the paths and means), 'ila Ma'rifat Ahadith' (to knowing the hadiths), 'Khulasat al-Dala'il' (of the abridgment of evidences). This is a methodological tool for hadith verification.
3
Connect to the base text
Khulasat al-Dala'il is a Hanafi Fiqh work that adduces proofs. al-Qurashi's work extracts and contextualizes the hadiths cited there, providing chains and references.
This shows the tradition of supplementing Fiqh works with hadith verification.
4
Recognize the scholarly gap filled
Khulasat al-Dala'il often cites hadiths without full chains or explicit references. al-Turuq wa al-Wasa'il fills this gap, making the evidence more accessible to muhaqqiqin (verifiers).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٢ - الطرق والوسائل إلى معرفة أحاديث خلاصة الدلائل (4).
للإمام محيي الدين عبد القادر بن محمد القرشي، المتوفى سنة ...

Two Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical listing of two Hanafi textual works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri introduced in this passage and explain their respective purposes.

Core Idea
Two essential Hanafi reference works: one biographical dictionary of scholars, one completion of al-Quduri's matn.

This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri lists two important works that build upon the foundational Mukhtasar of al-Quduri. Understanding these works helps you navigate the Hanafi literary tradition and appreciate the scholarly efforts to preserve and expand upon the school's core texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first work and its author
Locate the title 'Tahdhib al-Asma' al-Waqi'a fi al-Hidaya wa al-Khulasa' and its author, Muhyi al-Din al-Qurashi (d. 775 AH). Note the date and the author's full name.
2
Determine its purpose and content
Read the description: it is a biographical dictionary that identifies notable figures mentioned in al-Hidaya and Khulasat al-Dala'il. Compare it to Imam al-Nawawi's Tahdhib al-Asma' wa al-Lughat.
This is not a fiqh commentary but a tool for identifying scholars.
3
Identify the second work and its author
Find 'Takmilat al-Quduri' by Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 AH). Note that he also authored the commentary Khulasat al-Dala'il.
The word 'takmila' means supplement or completion.
4
Understand the relationship between the two works
Observe that al-Razi's Takmila completes or adds to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, while al-Qurashi's work is a reference for names in al-Hidaya and Khulasat al-Dala'il (al-Razi's commentary). They serve different but complementary purposes.
Both works support the study of the same matn.
5
Grasp the significance of such commentaries
Recognize that these works demonstrate the vitality of the Hanafi tradition through textual expansion, biographical clarification, and scholarly transmission. They are essential for advanced study.
They also show the interconnectedness of Hanafi texts.

للإمام محيي الدين عبد القادر بن محمد القرشي، المتوفى سنة ٧٧٥هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Tahdhib al-Asma' al-Waqi'a fi al-Hidaya wa al-Khulasa (i.e., Khulasat al-Dala'il Sharh al-Quduri li al-Razi).
By Imam Muhyi al-Din 'Abd al-Qadir ibn Muhammad al-Qurashi, died 775 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
It is a very useful book in refining the biographies of the notable figures mentioned in these two books, al-Hidaya and Khulasat al-Dala'il, and it resembles Imam al-Nawawi's book 'Tahdhib al-Asma' wa al-Lughat'.
The book has been printed in a slim volume (232 pages) in Beirut, at Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyya, edition 1419/1 AH, edited by Ayman Salih Sha'ban. It was also edited as a doctoral thesis at the University of Algiers, Faculty of Usul al-Din, by Dr. Ahmad ibn Fadilat al-Shaykh Muhammad Nimr al-Khatib in two large volumes with extensive comments, but has not yet been printed.

24 - Takmilat al-Quduri.
By Husam al-Din al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki, died 598 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, and he is the author of the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri called 'Khulasat al-Dala'il fi Tanqih al-Masa'il'.
It is mentioned in the author's introduction:
'... To proceed: the highest rank of the successor, if unable to reach the level of the predecessor, is to follow in his footsteps or gaze upon his traces. The Shaykh Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him, composed a summary that excelled in its composition, excelled in its arrangement and structuring, and sufficed despite its conciseness of wording and richness of meaning, with many issues and allusion to proofs.
Where the beginner has no need to study and read it, and the advanced has no escape from reviewing and studying it. Whoever aspires to produce something like it is more ambitious than...'
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri presents a biographical listing of two important commentaries written on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The first is 'Tahdhib al-Asma al-Waqi'a fi al-Hidaya wa al-Khulasa' by al-Qurashi (d. 775 AH). This work is a biographical dictionary that identifies the notable figures (a'lam) mentioned in al-Hidaya (by al-Marghinani) and Khulasat al-Dala'il (by al-Razi). It is described as very useful and compared to Imam al-Nawawi's similar work. The author provides publication details, showing the book has been printed and also edited as a doctoral thesis. The second work is 'Takmilat al-Quduri' by Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 AH), who is also the author of the well-known commentary 'Khulasat al-Dala'il'. The passage includes a quotation from the introduction of Takmilat al-Quduri, which praises the original Mukhtasar of Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, highlighting its excellence, conciseness, richness of meaning, and usefulness for both beginners and advanced scholars. This shows the high esteem in which al-Quduri's work was held in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
تهذيب الأسماء الواقعة في الهداية والخلاصة (Tahdhib al-Asma' al-Waqi'a fi al-Hidaya wa al-Khulasa): A biographical work by al-Qurashi that identifies and corrects the names of figures mentioned in al-Hidaya and Khulasat al-Dala'il.
تكملة القدوري (Takmilat al-Quduri): A completion or supplement to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar by Husam al-Din al-Razi, possibly adding missing issues or details.
خلاصة الدلائل في تنقيح المسائل (Khulasat al-Dala'il fi Tanqih al-Masa'il): A commentary by al-Razi on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, known for its thorough proofing of issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introducing the Takmilah al-Quduri: A Supplemental Hanafi Classic
Author's introduction to a supplementary fiqh work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and methodology of the Takmilah al-Quduri and identify its place in the Hanafi textual tradition.

Core Idea
The Takmilah is a companion to al-Quduri, not a replacement—it completes what is scattered without repeating what is settled.

This passage presents the author's own introduction to his Takmilah, a supplement to the renowned Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Husam al-Din al-Razi explains why such a work was needed: to gather additional rulings from other key Hanafi texts and organize them to align with al-Quduri's structure, thus providing a more complete picture of the madhhab without redundancy. Understanding this preface helps students appreciate how later Hanafi scholars built upon earlier authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
The author explicitly says he sought to collect scattered issues from other Hanafi works to complete al-Quduri's text.
The purpose is supplementary, not critical.
2
Recognize the sources he drew upon
He lists al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Irshad, and Mujaz al-Farghani as his source texts for additional rulings.
These are also foundational Hanafi texts.
3
Understand the organizational method
He arranged the collected material according to the same chapter order as al-Quduri, to maintain coherence.
The goal is seamless integration with the original.
4
Identify what is excluded and what is included
He avoids repetition except when necessary for context, and includes clarifications, expansions, and variant opinions.
The Takmilah is a supplement, not a commentary.
5
Appreciate the claimed benefit
Studying the Takmilah after al-Quduri is likened to reading five major Hanafi compendia at once.
This underscores the work's value.

24- Takmilah al-Quduri.
By Husam al-Din al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Makki, who died in 598 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He is the author of the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri called 'Khulasat al-Dala'il fi Tanqih al-Masa'il'.
It is mentioned in the author's introduction:
... To proceed: The highest rank of the follower, when unable to reach the level of the predecessor, is to follow in his footsteps or to look upon his traces with the eye. Shaykh Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him, authored a concise work that excelled in its composition, excellent in its arrangement and structure, and sufficed despite its brevity of expression and depth of meaning, with many issues and allusion to proofs.
The beginner cannot do without studying and reading it, nor can the advanced dispense with reviewing and perusing it. Whoever aspires to produce something like it would be more ambitious than
Ash'ab and more incapable than Tha'lab.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
So I intended to collect what scattered from the organization of his book of the issues published in the concise works of our companions, such as al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Irshad, and Mujaz al-Farghani.
I gathered them and arranged them according to the order of his book, and I chaptered them according to the similarity of its chapters,
without repeating a single issue or restating a difficult problem, except for what cannot be mentioned without repeating what he mentioned, or was a detail of what he summarized, or a comment on what he omitted, or there was in it an increase of clarification or relating a statement of someone... and what resembles that and runs in its course. So that it would be a completion (takmilah) of his work, and a supplement to his authorship, for it completes the benefits of al-Quduri. Whoever studies it and understands it after memorizing al-Quduri and knowing it, would be like one who has read the five concise works and combined the light of the planets and the sun." End quote.
There exist several excellent old manuscripts of this Takmilah; see al-Fihris al-Shamil. Among these is a precious copy of 169 folios, read to the author, and copied in 586 AH; another of 190 folios, written in 608 AH.
Imam 'Abd al-Qadir al-Qurashi mentioned this Takmilah in his book.
(1) This introduction was written to me, taken from a manuscript in the Sulaymaniyya Library in Istanbul, by the noble and virtuous brother, Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya, may Allah reward him well.
2 (0746/4)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage introduces the 'Takmilah al-Quduri', a supplementary work to Imam al-Quduri's famous Mukhtasar. The author, Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 AH), explains his motivation: recognizing the indispensability of al-Quduri's work for both beginners and advanced students, he sought to gather additional rulings found in other foundational Hanafi texts (such as al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, etc.) and organize them according to al-Quduri's arrangement. His goal was not to repeat al-Quduri, but to complete it by detailing what was summarized, clarifying what was omitted, and adding explanatory remarks or variant opinions. The Takmilah is thus a companion volume; studying it after mastering al-Quduri is likened to reading five major Hanafi compendia. The text also notes the existence of valuable manuscripts, including one read back to the author himself. This passage is a typical front matter where the author states his methodology and purpose.

Key Terms
تكملة (takmilah): A supplemental work that completes another text by adding missing rulings, clarifications, and expansions without repetition.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A concise collection of hadith and fiqh rulings by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) To critique and correct al-Quduri's Mukhtasar
D) To provide a concise summary of al-Quduri's work

Key Takeaway
The Takmilah al-Quduri is a carefully crafted supplement that enriches the study of al-Quduri by integrating additional rulings from other Hanafi classics without redundancy.

Two Early Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical listing of two commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two early Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and describe their key features and manuscript locations.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri attracted multiple early commentaries; al-Uzjandi and al-Khatli produced notable ones.

The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding its early commentaries helps you grasp how the matn was transmitted and expanded. This passage introduces two such commentaries from the 6th/12th century, providing details about their authors, methods, and extant manuscripts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Commentaries
Locate the two numbered entries (29 and 30) in the passage. Each describes a separate commentary by a different author.
The first is by Abu Ya'qub al-Uzjandi, the second by Nasr al-Khatli al-Samarqandi.
2
Note the Author's Full Name and Death Date
For each commentary, extract the commentator's full name (including nisba) and death date if given. This is crucial for historical classification.
Al-Uzjandi: 6th century AH (exact death not given). Al-Khatli: died 600 AH.
3
Extract the Features of Each Commentary
From the author's own introduction (for al-Uzjandi) and external praise (for al-Khatli), note the methodology and scope. Al-Uzjandi appended categories; al-Khatli produced a two-volume work praised as excellent.
Al-Uzjandi: concise expression, appended categories. Al-Khatli: two volumes, highly regarded.
4
Locate Manuscript Information
The passage provides library locations and copy dates for each commentary. Record these to understand the textual transmission.
Al-Uzjandi: Jarallah Library Istanbul, copied 603 AH. Al-Khatli: Vienna copy (375 ff.) and Esmihan Sultan copy (166 ff., up to Book of Wills).
5
Understand the Significance
Recognise that these commentaries are primary sources for studying the Mukhtasar. They show how later Hanafi scholars built on al-Quduri's work.
Knowing these commentaries helps in choosing reliable sharh when studying the matn.

الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
وقد نقلت منه في كتابي هذا ما قاله في الفرائض بحروفه، ولذا نبهت عليه أنه ليس من تأليفي بل تأليفه». اهـ من مقدمة المؤلف. ونسخة عارف حكمت هذه تقع في (١٨٤) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٩) سطراً، وتاريخ نسخها سنة ٩٠٤هـ.
۲۹- شرح مختصر القدوري.
لأبي يعقوب ظهير الدين يوسف بن عثمان بن الفضل الأوزجندي(۱)، من علماء القرن السادس الهجري، رحمه الله تعالى.
وتوجد نسخة منه في مكتبة جار الله باسطنبول، برقم (۷۳۱)، كتبت سنة ٦٠٣هـ ، ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل(٢).
وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف ما يلي قال الشيخ الإمام الأجل السيد شيخ الإسلام ظهير الدين أبـو يعقوب يوسف بن عثمان بن الفضل بن محمد الأوزجندي:
إنه سألني بعض إخواني شرح مختصر القدوري، ببيان المعاني، فضمنتُ أن أبين لكل رواية دراية على وجه له كفاية، بعبارة موجزة مؤثرة، وإشارة بليغة مقنعة، وألحق آخرَ كل فصل أو باب : الأجناس المختلفة في جميع الكتاب، وأفرزها عن مسائل التصنيف، كي لا يتهمني أحد بالتغيير والتحريف ...». اهـ
۳۰۔ شرح مختصر القدوري .
لنصر بن محمد الختلي السمرقندي الفقيه الحنفي، المتوفى سنة ٦٠٠هـ (۱)، رحمه الله تعالى.
وسمي المؤلف في المخطوطات بـ: محمد بن عبد الله الختلي. قال القرشي في ترجمته (۲) : رأيتُ له شرحاً لمختصر القدوري في مجلدين، أبدع فيه، كان في حدود الستمائة». اهـ
ومن الكتاب نسخة في (فينا)، في (٣٧٥) ورقة، ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل(۳).
كما يوجد للكتاب نسخة أخرى في اسميخان سلطان (١٤٧)، كتبت سنة ٨٥٠هـ ، في (١٦٦) ورقة، إلى آخر كتاب الوصايا. وفي أولها فهرست للكتب، وجاء في أسفل الصفحة بحرف كبير ما يلي: كتاب شرح القدوري رحمه الله ، المعروف بالختلي، شرحه
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
I have transmitted from it in this book what he said about the obligatory shares in his own words, and therefore I have pointed out that it is not from my authorship but rather his authorship. End quote from the author's introduction. This copy of 'Arif Hakmat consists of (184) folios, with (19) lines per page, and its copy date is 904 AH.
29- Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
By Abu Ya'qub Zahir al-Din Yusuf ibn 'Uthman ibn al-Fadl al-Uzjandi(1), from the scholars of the sixth century AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
A copy of it exists in the Jarallah Library in Istanbul, number (731), written in 603 AH, see al-Fihris al-Shamil(2).
The author's introduction states: The leading Imam, the master, the Shaykh al-Islam Zahir al-Din Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn 'Uthman ibn al-Fadl ibn Muhammad al-Uzjandi said:
One of my brothers asked me for a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining the meanings, so I undertook to explain for every narration a comprehension in a manner that suffices, with an effective concise expression, and a convincing eloquent indication, and I appended at the end of every chapter or section: the different categories in the entire book, and separated them from the issues of the classification, so that no one would accuse me of alteration or distortion... End quote.
30- Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
By Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Khatli al-Samarqandi, the Hanafi jurist, died 600 AH(1), may Allah have mercy on him.
The author is named in the manuscripts as: Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah al-Khatli. Al-Qurashi said in his biography (2): 'I saw for him a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri in two volumes, in which he excelled, composed around the year 600.' End quote.
A copy of the book exists in Vienna, in (375) folios, see al-Fihris al-Shamil(3).
Another copy of the book exists in Esmihan Sultan (147), written in 850 AH, in (166) folios, up to the end of the Book of Wills. At its beginning is an index of books, and at the bottom of the page in large letters is written: 'Kitab Sharh al-Quduri rahimahu Allah, known as al-Khatli, his commentary.'
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory chapter of Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, where the author discusses earlier commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He lists two notable Hanafi commentaries. The first is by Abu Ya'qub Zahir al-Din Yusuf al-Uzjandi (or al-Arzanjani as some manuscripts have it), a scholar of the 6th century AH. The author quotes from al-Uzjandi's introduction, explaining that he was asked to write a commentary that combines concise expressions with convincing indications, and he appended lists of categories at the end of each chapter to prevent accusations of alteration. The second commentary is by Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Khatli al-Samarqandi, also known as Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Khatli, who died around 600 AH. Al-Qurashi praised his two-volume commentary as excellent. Manuscript locations and details are provided for both works. This biographical information is important for students of the Hanafi school to understand the textual history and transmission of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise handbook of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied in the Hanafi madhhab.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary or exposition of a base text, explaining its meanings and providing evidence.
الأوزجندي (al-Uzjandi): A nisba referring to the town of Uzjand (or Arzanjān) in Central Asia; here it identifies the commentator Abu Ya'qub.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The early commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Uzjandi and al-Khatli are vital sources for understanding the transmission and development of Hanafi fiqh.

Al-Khatli and His Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical entry describing al-Khatli and his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Khatli's name and death date as recorded in manuscripts, describe the content and locations of his commentary, and explain the manuscript discrepancies.

Core Idea
Al-Khatli's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a two-volume work praised by al-Qurashi, but his identity varies between manuscripts.

This lesson examines a biographical entry on al-Khatli, a Hanafi scholar who authored a commentary on the foundational text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage highlights manuscript variations in his name and death year, as well as the locations where his work survives. Understanding these details is essential for accurately citing sources in Hanafi fiqh research.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Commentator
Read the first line: the author is Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Khatli, a Hanafi jurist who died in 600 AH. Note that a variant name is given later.
Manuscripts also name him Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Khatli.
2
Assess the Commentary's Reputation
Look at al-Qurashi's quote: he saw a two-volume commentary and judged it excellent. This establishes the work's scholarly value.
3
Examine Manuscript Evidence
Two manuscripts are described: one in 'Fayna' with 375 folios, another in Ismikhan Sultan with 166 folios (to the Book of Wills). The second states the work was written in 451 AH.
The difference in folio count may indicate the second is incomplete.
4
Note the Beginning of the Commentary
The commentary starts with a chapter on the virtues of Imam Abu Hanifa, then the Book of Purification. This reveals its structure.
5
Synthesize the Discrepancy
The author stresses that the commentator's name and death date need verification due to conflicting manuscript evidence. Consider why this matters for Hanafi textual history.
Cross-checking names prevents misattribution.

۳۰۔ شرح مختصر القدوري .
لنصر بن محمد الختلي السمرقندي الفقيه الحنفي، المتوفى سنة ٦٠٠هـ (1)، رحمه الله تعالى.
وسمي المؤلف في المخطوطات بـ: محمد بن عبد الله الختلي. قال القرشي في ترجمته (۲) : رأيتُ له شرحاً لمختصر القدوري في مجلدين، أبدع فيه، كان في حدود الستمائة». اهـ
ومن الكتاب نسخة في (فينا)، في (٣٧٥) ورقة، ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل(۳).
كما يوجد للكتاب نسخة أخرى في اسميخان سلطان (١٤٧)، كتبت سنة ٨٥٠هـ ، في (١٦٦) ورقة، إلى آخر كتاب الوصايا. وفي أولها فهرست للكتب، وجاء في أسفل الصفحة بحرف كبير ما يلي: كتاب شرح القدوري رحمه الله ، المعروف بالختلي، شرحه الإمام الأجل الكبير، العالم العابد الزاهد، الحبر المحقق المدقق المتقن محمد بن عبد الله بن حامد بن عبد الله بن محمد بن إبراهيم أبو سهل الختلي لسنة إحدى وخمسين وأربعمائة.
وكتب على طرة النسخة في الأعلى : (شرح القدوري، المسمى الخَتْلي).
وقد جاء في أول هذا الشرح فصل في مناقب الإمام أبي حنيفة، ثم بدأ بكتاب الطهارة (١).
وعلى هذا ، فليُحرَّر اسم الشارح الختلي، ولتحرر سنة وفاته.
30. Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Khatli al-Samarqandi, the Hanafi jurist, died in the year 600 AH (1), may God have mercy on him. The author is named in the manuscripts as: Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Khatli. Al-Qurashi said in his biography (2): 'I saw a commentary of his on Mukhtasar al-Quduri in two volumes, he excelled in it, it was around the year six hundred.' End quote. A copy of the book is in (Fayna?), in 375 folios, see al-Fihris al-Shamil (3). Another copy of the book exists in Ismikhan Sultan (147), written in the year 850 AH, in 166 folios, up to the end of the Book of Wills. At its beginning is an index of books, and at the bottom of the page in large letters is written: 'The book of Sharh al-Quduri, may God have mercy on him, known as al-Khatli, commentary by the great venerable Imam, the scholar, the worshiper, the ascetic, the perfected investigator, the precise, Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Hamid ibn Abd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim Abu Sahl al-Khatli, in the year one hundred and fifty-one and four hundred.' And on the top margin of the copy was written: 'Sharh al-Quduri, called al-Khatli.' At the beginning of this commentary there is a chapter on the virtues of Imam Abu Hanifa, then it begins with the Book of Purification (1). On this basis, the name of the commentator al-Khatli should be corrected, and his year of death should be corrected.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry listing a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Khatli. It begins by identifying the author as Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Khatli al-Samarqandi, a Hanafi jurist, who died in 600 AH. The text notes a discrepancy in the manuscripts: the author's name is sometimes given as Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Khatli. Al-Qurashi is quoted saying he saw a two-volume commentary that was excellent, composed around 600 AH. The passage then provides manuscript locations: one in Fayna (likely a library) with 375 folios, and another in Ismikhan Sultan written in 850 AH with 166 folios covering up to the Book of Wills. The second manuscript has a note stating the commentary was completed in 451 AH by Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Khatli. At the beginning of the commentary is a chapter on the virtues of Imam Abu Hanifa, then it starts with the Book of Purification. The author stresses the need to verify the commentator's name and death date.

Key Terms
الختلي (al-Khatli): A Hanafi jurist from Samarqand, author of a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri.

Identifying Two Key Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Listing two commentaries with biographical and manuscript details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authors and key features of the commentaries al-Nuri and al-Yanabi', and distinguish them from similar works like Khulasat al-Dala'il.

Core Idea
Two commentaries, two authors: al-Nuri (Abu Ja'far al-Razi) and al-Yanabi' (Rashid al-Din al-Shibli) – but beware of confusion with Khulasat al-Dala'il.

This passage lists two important Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational matn in the school. It provides their authors, death dates, and a crucial manuscript note: some copies cataloged as al-Nuri are actually Khulasat al-Dala'il by a different al-Razi. Knowing this helps avoid misattribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the works and authors
Read the text to note the full titles, authors' names, and death dates for al-Nuri and al-Yanabi'.
Al-Nuri is by Abu Ja'far al-Razi (d. 615 AH); al-Yanabi' by Rashid al-Din al-Shibli (d. 620 or 686 AH).
2
Understand the manuscript confusion
Note that three Turkish copies thought to be al-Nuri are actually Khulasat al-Dala'il by Husam al-Din al-Razi. Recognize the cause: both authors share the nisba 'al-Razi'.
This highlights the importance of verifying manuscripts beyond catalog entries.
3
Memorize the key details
Fix in memory: the author, death year, and a distinguishing feature (e.g., al-Yanabi' was completed in 616 AH, al-Nuri's confusion with Khulasat).
Use these details when referencing Hanafi commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣١ - النُّوري في شرح مختصر القدوري. لأبي جعفر محمد بن إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي الرازي، المتوفى في الموصل سنة ٦١٥ هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى. توجد منه عدة نُسَخ في تركيا، والقاهرة، ينظر لهـا الفهـرس الشامل، منها نسخة كتبت سنة ٦٩٥ هـ في مكتبة جار الله باسطنبول، ولم يُذكر عدد أوراق النسخة ، ليُعلم منها حجم الكتاب. لكن كتب إلى مشكوراً الأستاذ محمد فاتح قايا من اسطنبول أنــه اطلع على نُسَخ تركيا، وهي ثلاثة، التي ذكـر أرقامها أصحاب الفهرس الشامل، فوجدها نُسخاً من كتاب خلاصة الدلائل، لحسام الدين الرازي، وليست من كتاب (النوري)، يقول: وكأن الذي أوقع المفهرسين في هذا اللبس أن كلا منهما رازي، والله أعلم. وتبقى النسخة الرابعة للكتاب نسخة دار الكتب المصرية، التي ذكرها أصحاب الفهرس الشامل، فلتُحرَّر ليتأكد منها.
٣٢ الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع (شرح لمختصر القدوري). للإمام رشید الدین محمود بن رمضان الشبلي الرومي، المدرس بمدرسة الحلاوية بحلب، فرغ منه سنة ٦١٦هـ، رحمـه الله تعالى. قال العلامة قاسم : شَرَحَ القدوري شرحاً جامعاً لكثير من الفروع الفقهية. اهـ وقد اختلف في سنة وفاته، ففي كشف الظنون: أنه توفي سنة ٦٨٦ هـ وقيل: بل توفي سنة ٦٢٠ هـ .
31. Al-Nuri in the commentary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Razi, who died in Mosul in the year 615 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Several copies exist in Turkey and Cairo, referenced in the comprehensive catalog. Among them is a copy written in 695 AH in the Jarallah library in Istanbul, but the number of folios is not mentioned to know the size of the book. However, the esteemed Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya from Istanbul wrote to me that he examined the Turkish copies, three in number, whose numbers were mentioned by the compilers of the comprehensive catalog, and found them to be copies of the book Khulasat al-Dala'il by Husam al-Din al-Razi, not from the book (al-Nuri). He said: It seems that the cause of confusion for the catalogers is that both are al-Razi, and Allah knows best. The fourth copy of the book remains the copy of the Egyptian National Library, which the catalogers mentioned, so it should be verified. 32. Al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari' (a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri). By Imam Rashid al-Din Mahmud ibn Ramadan al-Shibli al-Rumi, teacher at the Halawiyya school in Aleppo, completed in 616 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. 'Allamah Qasim said: He wrote a comprehensive commentary on al-Quduri covering many fiqh branches. End quote. There is disagreement on his death year: in Kashf al-Zunun, it is said he died in 686 AH, and some say he died in 620 AH.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is biographical, listing two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The first is al-Nuri by Abu Ja'far al-Razi (d. 615 AH). The author notes a common confusion: many cataloged copies of al-Nuri are actually copies of Khulasat al-Dala'il by a different scholar (Husam al-Din al-Razi), warned by modern scholar Muhammad Fatih Qaya. The second is al-Yanabi' by Rashid al-Din al-Shibli (d. 620 or 686 AH), completed in 616 AH, praised by 'Allamah Qasim as comprehensive. These entries help students identify authentic Hanafi commentaries and avoid manuscript misattributions.

Key Terms
النوري (al-Nuri): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu Ja'far al-Razi (d. 615 AH).
الينابيع (al-Yanabi'): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Rashid al-Din al-Shibli (d. 620/686 AH), completed in 616 AH.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh work by Imam al-Quduri, widely commented upon.
خلاصة الدلائل (Khulasat al-Dala'il): A different Hanafi work by Husam al-Din al-Razi, sometimes confused with al-Nuri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both are commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
B) Both authors are named al-Razi
C) Both were written in the same year
D) Both are preserved in Turkish libraries

Key Takeaway
When studying Hanafi commentaries, always verify the author's full name and work title to avoid confusing al-Nuri with Khulasat al-Dala'il.

Identifying the Author of al-Yanabi': Rashid al-Din al-Shayblī
Biographical and bibliographic entry on a Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Rashid al-Din Mahmud al-Shayblī and distinguish him from other scholars with similar names.

Core Idea
Knowing the author and manuscript history safeguards against misattribution in Hanafi scholarship.

When studying a commentary on a foundational text like Mukhtasar al-Quduri, it is crucial to know the author's identity, his lifespan, and the manuscript tradition. This lesson examines a biographical entry for Rashid al-Din Mahmud al-Shayblī and his work al-Yanabi', clarifying common confusions in scholarly references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text and author
Read the passage to find the full name of the commentary and its author. Note the author's title (Rashid al-Din) and his affiliation (teacher at al-Halawiyya school).
2
Examine the completion and death dates
Extract the completion year (616 AH) of the commentary. Then compare the conflicting death dates mentioned (769 AH, 723 AH, blank). Consider why there is confusion.
The large gap between completion and proposed death dates suggests a possible error in later sources.
3
Distinguish from a namesake
Notice the explicit statement that this author is not Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Shayblī. Understand why such clarification is needed in biographical dictionaries.
Both authors have the same nisba 'al-Shayblī', leading to potential mix-ups.
4
Note the manuscript details
Identify the number of volumes, folios, lines per page, and the oldest known copy (Istanbul, 620 AH, during the author's lifetime). Recognize the value of early manuscripts.
The Istanbul copy being from the author's lifetime strengthens its authority.
5
Assess the passage's purpose
The passage is not a fiqh ruling but a bibliographic note. It aims to resolve confusion about manuscript identity and author biography, which is essential for proper citation in Hanafi studies.
Such entries are common in works that list commentaries, helping scholars trace textual transmission.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic entry within the third chapter listing commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author first clarifies a confusion about three manuscripts in Turkey: they were thought to be copies of a commentary called 'al-Nuri' but are actually copies of 'Khulasat al-Dala'il' by Husam al-Din al-Razi. He then highlights a fourth copy in Egypt that needs verification. The main subject is commentary number 32: 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'' by Rashid al-Din Mahmud ibn Ramadan al-Shayblī al-Rumi, a teacher at the Halawiyya school in Aleppo. The commentary was completed in 616 AH. The passage notes a discrepancy about the author's death year: Kashf al-Zunun says 769 AH, the comprehensive index says 723 AH, and Hadiyat al-'Arifin leaves it blank. It emphasizes that this al-Shayblī is not Muhammad al-Shayblī, author of 'Akam al-Marjan'. The passage concludes with details of the manuscript: one volume, 245 folios, 21 lines per page, based on a copy from 661 AH, and mentions an older Istanbul copy from 620 AH made during the author's lifetime.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied as an introductory legal manual.
الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع (al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Rashid al-Din Mahmud al-Shayblī, completed in 616 AH.
رشيد الدين محمود بن رمضان الشبلي الرومي (Rashid al-Din Mahmud ibn Ramadan al-Shayblī al-Rumi): The Hanafi scholar who authored al-Yanabi'. He taught at the Halawiyya school in Aleppo.

Identifying the Correct Author of al-Yanabi'
Biographical correction of al-Yanabi''s authorship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct author of al-Yanabi' and apply critical textual methods to resolve authorship confusions in Hanafi literature.

Core Idea
The author of al-Yanabi' is Rashid al-Din Mahmud ibn Ramadan, not al-Shibli — careful manuscript evidence corrects common scholarly errors.

This lesson examines a passage from al-Lubab clarifying the authorship of a key Hanafi work, al-Yanabi'. You will learn how the commentator uses manuscript evidence and critical reasoning to correct a widespread confusion between two Hanafi scholars. Applying this method will sharpen your ability to verify textual attributions in your own studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Confusion
Read the passage to find what mistaken belief is being corrected. Two authors are being confused: one is Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shibli (author of Akam al-Marjan), the other is the real author of al-Yanabi'.
2
Locate the Evidence
Find the evidence the commentator uses: the author's full name (Rashid al-Din Abu Abdullah Mahmud ibn Ramadan al-Rumi al-Hanafi), the date and place of composition (Aleppo, 616 AH), and the existence of a manuscript copied during the author's lifetime (620 AH).
Note the use of manuscript dates as primary evidence.
3
Assess the Criticism
The commentator criticizes Ahmad al-Naqib for hastily doubting the attribution. Identify the basis of this criticism: lack of knowledge and hasty judgment. Consider why careful scholarship is important in fiqh textual studies.
4
Apply the Method
Practice applying the same critical method to another Hanafi text. For any attributed work, ask: Is there a manuscript copy from the author's era? Does the author's name match across reliable sources? Are later scholars (like al-Baghdadi) unanimous?
This method protects against both false attribution and unjustified dismissal.

Perfection is Allah's alone. And I will quote below the introduction of the author of al-Yanabi' so that his work in it may be known...
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note from the commentary 'al-Lubab' on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. It discusses the author of a book called 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'' (The Springs on Knowledge of Principles and Branches). The text clarifies that the author is not the famous Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shibli (author of 'Akam al-Marjan'), but rather Rashid al-Din Abu Abdullah Mahmud ibn Ramadan al-Rumi al-Hanafi. It provides details about the book's size, manuscript copies, and corrects errors made by later scholars who confused the two. The passage also notes that the book was composed in Aleppo in 616 AH and that a copy exists in Istanbul from 620 AH, copied during the author's lifetime. The commentator warns against hasty judgments about the author's identity, emphasizing the need for careful scholarship.

Key Terms
الينابيع (al-Yanabi'): A book on usul al-fiqh and furu' by Rashid al-Din Mahmud ibn Ramadan al-Hanafi.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri.
أكام المرجان (Akam al-Marjan): A book by Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shibli, distinct from the author of al-Yanabi'.

Key Takeaway

Context and Purpose of Al-Mujtaba Commentary
Biographical introduction and author's preface

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical circumstances that prompted Imam al-Zahidi to write Al-Mujtaba and identify its role in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
The Mongol devastation spurred a Hanafi scholar to pen a commentary that revived fiqh scholarship.

This lesson introduces a biographical and prefatory passage from a work cataloging commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It focuses on Al-Mujtaba, a major Hanafi commentary written by Imam Najm al-Din al-Zahidi. The passage explains why the author wrote this commentary in the wake of the Mongol invasions, providing a window into the challenges faced by Muslim scholars and the motivations behind preserving the Hanafi legal tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and His Background
Who is Najm al-Din al-Zahidi? Note his full name, death year, travels, and his affiliation: Hanafi in fiqh but Mu'tazili in creed. This helps contextualize his scholarly outlook.
Al-Zahidi's Mu'tazili leanings are mentioned, but his Hanafi fiqh is emphasized.
2
Recognize the Historical Calamity Described
Read the author's preface and identify the 'general fitna' (الفتنة العامة) that overwhelmed Islamic lands. This refers to the Mongol/Tatar invasions, which destroyed cities, killed scholars, and disrupted learning.
The vivid language (طمت هذه الطامة) underscores the scale of destruction.
3
Understand the Demand from Students
Why did students request a new commentary? The preface states that the foundations of fiqh were neglected, and students wanted to ascend to the ranks of jurists. They needed a work that clarified difficulties and resolved ambiguities.
The students represent the next generation seeking to revive scholarship.
4
Identify the Gap in Existing Commentaries
Al-Zahidi notes that previous commentators assumed the text was clear and omitted detailed explanations. Thus, there was a need for a commentary that unpacks summaries, explains difficult points, and clarifies problems.
This gap motivated a more comprehensive work.
5
Explain the Author's Response
Al-Zahidi responded by writing Al-Mujtaba, a three-volume commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. His goal was to make the foundational text accessible and preserve Hanafi fiqh learning during a time of crisis.
The title 'Al-Mujtaba' means 'the chosen', reflecting its selective yet comprehensive nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
٣٤- المجتبى شرح مختصر القدوري.
للإمام نجم الدين مختار بن محمود الزاهدي الخوارزمي، المتوفى سنة ٦٥٨هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وكان قد رحل من خوارزم إلى بغداد وبلاد الروم، وهو حنفي الفروع، معتزلي الاعتقاد.
وشرحه من أكبر شروح مختصر القدوري، يقع في ثلاث مجلدات.
قال الإمام اللكنوي عنه: «وشَرْحُه نفيس نافع». اهـ
وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف: ... لما عمَّت الفتنة العامة ديار الإسلام، وطمت هذه الطامة ... شارع الشرائع والأحكام واستولت يد التدمير على طلبة العلم والعلماء، وأنشبت المنيَّةُ أظفارها في يواقيح الفضلاء، لم يبق في عالم الفضل منهم إلا شيخ تحرير قد بلغ ساحل الحياة، أو شاب عزيز شغلته شواغل العيش واللذات. فبقيت مباني الفقه سدىً هَمَلاً، وأهملت معانيه علماً وعملاً، فهزت بعض إخواني همة الارتقاء إلى مراقي الفقهاء، وبعضهم اللقا مواطن بعد الأدب، والإحاطة فيه لمسالك العرب والعجم، فطلبوا إلي شرح المختصر المنسوب إلى إمام الأئمة، وفقيه آخر هذه الأمة أبي الحسين أحمد بن محمد أحمد بن جعفر بن أحمد القدوري، طيب الله ثراه، وجعل حظيرة القدس مأواه. فإنه أعظم دواوين الفقه بركة وخطراً، وأرفعها شأناً وقدراً، وأدورها في أندية الفضلاء والمدارس، وأيمنها للمدرس والدارس. وقد ترك أعمُّ المُشَرِّحين له لغاية وضوحه عندهم تفصيل مجملاته، وتفسير مهماته، وكشف مشكلاته، فأجبتهم إلى ذلك.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
34. Al-Mujtaba, commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
By Imam Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi al-Khwarizmi, died 658 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
He traveled from Khwarazm to Baghdad and the lands of Rum; he was Hanafi in branches, Mu'tazili in creed.
His commentary is among the largest commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, in three volumes.
Imam al-Lakhnawi said about him: 'His commentary is excellent and beneficial.'
And it is stated in the author's introduction: ... When the general fitna (tribulation) overwhelmed the lands of Islam, and this calamity engulfed ... (the calamity) of the legislator of laws and rulings, and the hand of destruction seized students and scholars, and death extended its claws into the strong among the virtuous, there remained in the world of virtue among them only a master of refinement who had reached the shore of life, or a noble youth preoccupied with the concerns of livelihood and pleasures. So the foundations of fiqh remained neglected and abandoned, its meanings ignored in knowledge and practice. Then some of my brethren stirred with ambition to ascend to the ranks of the jurists, and some to meet after refinement, and to encompass the methods of Arabs and non-Arabs in it. So they asked me to comment on the Mukhtasar attributed to the Imam of Imams, the jurist of the end of this ummah, Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Ahmad al-Quduri, may Allah make his resting place pleasant and grant him the abode of Paradise. For it is the greatest book of jurisprudence in blessing and importance, the highest in status and rank, the most widespread in the circles of the virtuous and schools, and the most auspicious for teacher and student. Most of those who commented on it left out, due to its clarity for them, the detailing of its summaries, the explanation of its difficulties, and the clarification of its problems; so I responded to them in that.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and introductory section from the third chapter of a work listing commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It introduces one specific commentary: Al-Mujtaba by Imam Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi al-Khwarizmi. The author provides key biographical details: al-Zahidi was a Hanafi jurist with Mu'tazili theological leanings, who traveled extensively from Khwarazm to Baghdad and Anatolia. His commentary is noted as one of the largest, spanning three volumes, and is praised by later scholars like al-Lakhnawi for its excellence. The passage then quotes the author's own preface, which vividly describes the devastating impact of the Mongol invasions ('the general fitna') on Islamic scholarship. Faced with the destruction of centers of learning and the loss of scholars, students requested a clear, detailed commentary on al-Quduri's foundational text. Al-Zahidi responded by writing Al-Mujtaba, aiming to unpack the concise statements, explain difficult points, and resolve ambiguities that previous commentators had overlooked due to the text's apparent clarity. This preface emphasizes the urgency and practical need for the work in a time of scholarly decline.

Key Terms
المجتبى (al-Mujtaba): The title of this commentary, meaning 'the chosen' or 'the selected'.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Mujtaba was written to revive Hanafi fiqh study after the Mongol devastations, by clarifying a foundational text that prior commentators had not sufficiently explained.

Evaluating the Authority of Al-Zahidi’s Works in the Hanafi School
Discussion of credibility and criticism of al-Zahidi's commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria used to evaluate the reliability of a Hanafi jurist’s works and apply them to assess the status of al-Zahidi’s writings.

Core Idea
Al-Zahidi's works, despite their utility, are not fully reliable and cannot override the canonical Hanafi texts.

This lesson examines the scholarly debate around Najm al-Din al-Zahidi’s commentaries, particularly al-Mujtaba. While al-Zahidi claimed to have drawn from reliable sources, later authorities like al-Laknawi flagged his works as containing weak transmissions and Mu'tazili influences. Understanding why certain books are considered authoritative and others not is essential for proper Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his claims
Read al-Zahidi’s own statement from the conclusion of al-Mujtaba, where he asserts his effort to avoid alteration and his reliance on reliable books. Note his humility in requesting correction of errors.
This shows al-Zahidi’s self-perception as a careful compiler.
2
Analyze the criticism by al-Laknawi
Examine the two quotes from al-Laknawi: first, his initial praise that the works contain strange issues and benefits; second, his definitive classification as unreliable due to weak transmissions and Mu'tazili creed.
Al-Laknawi’s final judgment overrides his initial praise.
3
Understand the basis for rejection
Identify the specific reasons: al-Zahidi’s Mu'tazili belief (i.e., theological deviation) and the presence of weak riwayat in his books, as confirmed by Tanqih al-Fatawa and Umdat al-Ri'aya.
The Hanafi school evaluates works by both content (riwayat) and author’s creed.
4
Determine the operative rule
Learn the rule from Tanqih al-Fatawa: al-Zahidi’s transmission does not oppose the reliable Nu'maniyya books unless supported by another source. This places his works at a lower level of authority.
This is a key principle for dealing with later commentaries.

* مناقشة ما قيل من عدم اعتماد الزاهدي وكتبه عموماً : بعد أن رأيتُ هذا الجهد الكبير، والعمل العظيم الذي قام به الزاهدي في المجتبى، واعتماد علماء المذهب ممن جاء بعده عليه، وإكثار النقل عنه، حتى قالوا سارت به «الركبان»، بعد هذا كله نقف متأملين بما قاله الإمام محمد عبد الحي اللكنوي، (ت ١٣٠٤هـ)، وانتقاده لكتاب المجتبى، وكتب الزاهدي عموماً، فقد قال(۱): قد طالعتُ المجتبى شرح القدوري، والقُنية ـ لـه ـ ، فوجدتُهما على المسائل الغريبة حاويين، ولتفصيل الفوائد كافيين. اهـ ويقول أيضاً : ومن الكتب الغير المعتبرة: تصانيف نجم الدين مختار بن محمود الزاهدي معتزلي الاعتقاد حنفي الفروع، المتوفى سنة ٦٥٦هـ، كالقنية، والحاوي، والمجتبى شرح القدوري، وزاد الأئمة.

وفيه أيضاً في موضع آخر : الحاوي للزاهـــدي مشهور بنقــل الروايات الضعيفة». اهـ من عمدة الرعاية(٢).

In it, and it appears that its author owned a large, rare library, containing the primary books of the school, and the books of those who preceded him from the Hanafi imams.
6
For example, in the issue of the obligation of Hajj at the time of the Qarmatians' uprising, their turmoil, and their killing of pilgrims, he transmits many quotations from the imams of the school who lived through that turmoil or were close to its time, such as al-Karkhi, al-Jassas, Abu Abdullah al-Balkhi, Abu Qasim al-Saffar, Abu al-Layth, al-Wubari, Abu Bakr al-Warraq, and others. He transmits the opinion of each one of them, and that some of them made it obligatory and some of them dropped it, and the point of view of each of them, and so on...
* And al-Zahidi said in the conclusion of al-Mujtaba:
'I have exerted my effort and capacity, and employed my ability and capability in avoiding alteration and distortion, and in avoiding in transmitting the issues and causes (al-'ilal) from the reliable books any detrimental change and miswriting. But the heart is afflicted with the doubts of the world, and the mind, due to pride and much study, is weary and exhausted. Forgetfulness is a characteristic of humanity, and error and slip are the emblem of mankind. So, the hoped-for from whoever honors this commentary by looking into it, and comprehending the subtleties of its structures and the secrets of its meanings, is to rectify its slips and errors in it, after he perfects the necessity of rectifying them. For I have not composed any composition in it, nor preferred in the exposition of the issues and causes, their abbreviation and compilation, any arrangement, except after long reflection, numerous consultations and contemplation. And Allah is the granter of immunity, grace, and success...' End.
* Discussion of what was said about the non-reliance on al-Zahidi and his books in general: After I saw this great effort and immense work that al-Zahidi did in al-Mujtaba, and the reliance of the scholars of the school who came after him upon it, and their frequent transmission from it, until they said 'the travelers carried it', after all this we pause reflectively at what Imam Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) said, and his criticism of the book al-Mujtaba and al-Zahidi's books in general. For he said (1): I have perused al-Mujtaba, the commentary on al-Quduri, and al-Quniya — his — and found them encompassing strange issues, and sufficient for detailing benefits. End. And he also says: And among the books that are not considered reliable: the works of Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi — Mu'tazili in belief, Hanafi in furu' — who died in 656 AH, such as al-Quniya, al-Hawi, al-Mujtaba Sharh al-Quduri, and Zād al-A'immah.
For he said in Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya: The transmission of al-Zahidi does not oppose the transmission of the reliable Nu'maniyya (Hanafi) books, for Ibn Wahban mentioned that no attention is paid to what the author of al-Quniya transmitted in opposition to the rules, unless it is supported by a transmission from someone else. And similarly in al-Nahr. End.
And in it also in another place: Al-Hawi by al-Zahidi is notorious for transmitting weak narrations. End. From Umdat al-Ri'aya (2).
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage discusses the scholarly debate over the reliability of Najm al-Din al-Zahidi's works in the Hanafi school, specifically his commentary al-Mujtaba on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author first highlights al-Zahidi's extensive effort in compiling from earlier Hanafi authorities and includes al-Zahidi's own humble request for correction of errors. However, the passage then presents a critical evaluation by Imam Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, who initially praises the works but ultimately classifies them as unreliable due to al-Zahidi's Mu'tazili creed and the presence of weak transmissions. Citing Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya and Umdat al-Ri'aya, the passage concludes that al-Zahidi's transmissions are not to override the established Hanafi corpus (the Nu'maniyya books) unless supported by other sources. This serves as a cautionary note: al-Zahidi's writings, despite their utility, carry the authority weight of later fatawa works (mutakhkhirin) and not the primary Zahir al-Riwayah, and must be used with scholarly scrutiny.

Key Terms
الروايات الضعيفة (al-riwāyāt al-ḍaʿīfah): Weak or unreliable transmitted opinions (riwayat) that are not given evidentiary weight in the Hanafi school unless supported by stronger sources.
الكتب المعتبرة (al-kutub al-muʿtabarah): The reliable, authoritative books of the Hanafi school, typically the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah and others accepted by the later jurists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi scholar must evaluate later commentaries by both the author's creed and the strength of the transmitted evidence; al-Zahidi's works, though comprehensive, are not authoritative unless corroborated by the core texts.

Evaluating the Reliability of Al-Zahidi's Works in the Hanafi School
Assessing the reliability of al-Zahidi's works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criterion that later Hanafi authorities use to accept or reject rulings from al-Zahidi's works and apply it to a hypothetical scenario.

Core Idea
A ruling from al-Zahidi contrary to established Hanafi rules is rejected unless corroborated by another transmitted report.

Al-Zahidi was a great Hanafi scholar, but his works like al-Mujtaba and al-Qunyah contain both reliable and weak narrations. Later authorities such as Ibn Abidin established a clear criterion: any position from al-Zahidi that goes against the school's norms must be supported by an independent transmitted report (naql). This lesson unpacks the criticism, defense, and practical application of that principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Criticism
Al-Laknawi states that al-Zahidi was 'careless in narrations' and his works are not reliable unless they correspond to other sources. This sets up the problem.
This criticism is from a later authority.
2
Extract the Criterion
Ibn Abidin specifies that any ruling in al-Mujtaba (or other works by al-Zahidi) that contradicts the school's rules must be supported by a transmitted report (naql).
The key phrase: 'لا يُلتفت إلى ما قاله الزاهدي مخالفاً للقواعد ما لم يؤيَّد بنقل'.
3
Recognize the Defense
Despite the criticism, al-Zahidi's works were widely used by major Hanafi commentators like Ibn Nujaym, indicating general acceptance. Al-Zahidi himself claimed careful methodology.
This balances the earlier criticism.
4
Apply the Principle
In practice, a ruling from al-Mujtaba that seems unique is not automatically rejected but requires independent verification from another reliable source.
Example: if al-Mujtaba states a unique condition for wudu, it remains suspect unless backed elsewhere.
5
Conclude the Balance
The student should understand that al-Zahidi's works are credible but require caution with outlier positions. The criterion ensures reliability without wholesale rejection.
Al-Zahidi's works are later (mutakhkhirin) sources, not Zahir al-Riwayah.

وهكذا، فما نقله اللكنوي من نقول عن ابن وهبان في حق القنية، وفي مصنفات الزاهدي عموماً، نقلها الطحطاوي في حواشــي الــدر المختار (۳) ونقلها أيضاً ابن عابدين في حاشيته رد المحتار (4) وكذلك قال ابن عابدين (٥) عن المجتبى خاصة والزاهدي عموماً: وأما ما في المجتبى»، فلم يعزه إلى أحد، وهو وإن كان وجهه ظاهراً، إذ لا يظهر فرق بينه وبين ما إذا أوصى بمثل نصيب ابن ،، لكنه لا يعارِضُ ما هنا ما لم يؤيد بنقل؛ لأن «المجتبى» للزاهدي، وقد قالوا: لا يُلتفت إلى ما قاله الزاهدي مخالفاً للقواعد ما لم يؤيَّد بنقل. تأمل». اهـ من ابن عابدين.

And Allamah Laknawi also said: 'Al-Zahidi, despite his greatness, is careless in narrations.' He also said about al-Zahidi's works in general: 'They are not considered reliable unless they are found to correspond to other works, because they combine the ripe and the unripe.' End quote. Also, considering what al-Zahidi said in the introduction to his book al-Mujtaba, which I quoted earlier, and what he said in its conclusion: 'I exerted my effort in quoting from the trustworthy books, avoiding alteration and distortion, refraining from rashness in transmitting rulings and reasons, and I did not compose anything except after lengthy reflection, frequent consultations, and deep thought...' and so on. Ibn Nujaym in the introduction to al-Bahr, when listing his sources, mentioned al-Mujtaba by al-Zahidi. Thus, one may comment on the words of Imam al-Laknawi and those before and after him with what was also said about al-Haddad, author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, as will be mentioned: There is no harm if there are some weak narrations in al-Zahidi's books that contradict the established rules of the school; but this possibility does not undermine al-Mujtaba, this great and precious commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, nor does it invalidate reliance upon al-Zahidi and his works in general, based on such general statements as mentioned before. And the reader should remain vigilant and alert concerning such narrations and statements that...
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a biographical-critical discussion about the Hanafi scholar al-Zahidi (d. 589/1193) and the reliability of his works, especially his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri titled al-Mujtaba. The author begins by quoting al-Laknawi's criticism that al-Zahidi was 'careless in narrations' and that his works are not reliable unless corroborated, as they mix reliable and weak material. This criticism is then cited by later authorities like al-Tahtawi and Ibn Abidin. Ibn Abidin specifically states that any ruling in al-Mujtaba contrary to the school's norms must be supported by another transmitted report. However, the author then defends al-Zahidi, noting that al-Laknawi himself praised him as a great imam and expert. Al-Zahidi's own claims of careful methodology in his introduction are presented. Moreover, the widespread reliance of later Hanafi commentators—such as in Tabyin al-Haqaiq, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Bahr al-Raiq—on al-Mujtaba is cited as evidence of its acceptance. Ibn Nujaym listed it among his primary sources. The author concludes that while some weak narrations may exist, they do not undermine the overall value of al-Mujtaba or the credibility of al-Zahidi. The reader should remain cautious of such exceptional narrations.

Key Terms
المجتبى (al-Mujtaba): The commentary by al-Zahidi on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, considered a major Hanafi reference but with some caution regarding its narrations.
القنية (al-Qunyah): A famous Hanafi work by al-Zahidi covering various fiqh topics, known for its breadth but also for mixing reliable and weak material.
الزاهدي (al-Zahidi): Abu al-Raja' Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi (d. 589/1193), a prominent Hanafi jurist and author of al-Qunyah and al-Mujtaba.
نقل (naql): A transmitted report or narration from a reliable source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It must be supported by a transmitted report (naql).
B) It must be from al-Zahidi's own reasoning.
C) It must be agreed upon by all later scholars.
D) It must be from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Zahidi's works are valuable but any ruling contrary to the school's norms requires external support; they are not rejected outright.

Biography of Zahir al-Din al-Nujabadi and His Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biography of a Hanafi jurist and bibliographic clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct title of al-Nujabadi's work and state his role as a Hanafi jurist and imam of al-Mustansiriyya.

Core Idea
A summary (talkhis) is a distinct work, not the original Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

This lesson introduces you to a 7th-century Hanafi scholar, Zahir al-Din al-Nujabadi, whose summary of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is often misidentified. Understanding this distinction is important for accurate bibliographic references in Hanafi studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Locate the full name, place of origin, and position (imam of al-Mustansiriyya).
He is from Bukhara, a center of Hanafi learning.
2
Note his death date
Record the year 668 AH and verify with biographical sources.
This places him in the 13th century CE.
3
Recognize the work's title
The passage corrects a common error: the work is Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri, not Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Talkhis means summary; it is an abridgement of Quduri's matn.
4
Understand the significance of talkhis
Summaries like this aid memorization and are common in the Hanafi tradition.
They are not replacements but study aids.
5
Verify with sources
The passage cites multiple historical and bibliographic works for cross-referencing.
This shows the importance of manuscript verification.

۳۷- تلخیص مختصر القدوري . للإمام الفقيه ظهير الدين محمد بن عمر النوجاباذي (النوحابادي) البخاري الحنفي، إمام المستنصرية ببغداد ، المتوفى سنة ٦٦٨هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. *(0) ذكره القرشي في الجواهر المضية، وغيره. (۱) له ترجمة في تاج التراجم ص .٢١٥ (۲) ۲۷۱/۳ ، وتبعه سزكين في التراث العربي ١٢٠/٣. .۷۳۹/۷ (۳) (4) 90/Y (E) (5) ۲۹۱/۳ ، وكشف الظنون ١٦٣٤/٢ ، وينظر تاج التراجم ص ٥٧٢، وفيه وقع اسم الكتاب خطأ : له مختصر القدوري»، وسقطت كلمة: «تلخيص».
37. Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By the Imam jurist Zahir al-Din Muhammad ibn Umar al-Nujabadi (al-Nuhabadi) al-Bukhari al-Hanafi, the Imam of al-Mustansiriyya in Baghdad, died in the year 668 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. *(0) Al-Qurashi mentioned him in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, and others. (1) His biography is in Taj al-Tarajim p. 215. (2) 271/3, and followed by Sezgin in al-Turath al-Arabi 120/3. 739/7 (3) (4) 90/Y (E) (5) 291/3, and Kashf al-Zunun 1634/2, and see Taj al-Tarajim p. 572, and in it the book's name is mistakenly written: 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and the word 'Talkhis' is omitted.

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for the Hanafi jurist Zahir al-Din al-Nujabadi, author of Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He was a prominent scholar from Bukhara and served as the imam of al-Mustansiriyya in Baghdad. The text provides his death year as 668 AH and cites several biographical sources. It notes a common mistake in referencing his work, where the title is given as Mukhtasar al-Quduri instead of Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri. This careful bibliographic correction is important for identifying the correct work in manuscript catalogues.

Key Terms
تلخیص مختصر القدوري (Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A summary/abridgement of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Nujabadi.
ظهير الدين النوجاباذي (Zahir al-Din al-Nujabadi): Full name: Muhammad ibn Umar al-Nujabadi, Hanafi jurist and imam of al-Mustansiriyya.

Biographical Note: Taj al-Din al-Mawsili and His Jami' al-Kalim al-Sharifa
Biographical entry on a Shafi'i scholar's Hanafi fiqh summary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of a Shafi'i scholar writing a Hanafi fiqh text and identify the correct death year of Taj al-Din al-Mawsili based on source analysis.

Core Idea
A Shafi'i scholar's Hanafi fiqh summary highlights cross-madhhab scholarship.

This lesson introduces you to Taj al-Din al-Mawsili, a Shafi'i scholar who authored a concise summary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri on Hanafi fiqh. The passage also reveals a common challenge in biographical research: verifying death years when primary sources disagree. Understanding these details deepens your appreciation for how Hanafi texts were transmitted and authored by scholars from other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his madhhab
The author is Taj al-Din al-Mawsili. His full name is given as Abd al-Rahim ibn Muhammad ibn Yunus. He is explicitly identified as Shafi'i (الشافعي). Note this even though his work is on Hanafi fiqh.
This cross-madhhab activity was common.
2
Recognize the work and its commission
The work is a summary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri titled Jami' al-Kalim al-Sharifa. It was written at the suggestion of Ata Malik al-Juwayni, a vizier. The opening phrase is 'Praise be to Allah, the Eternal'.
3
Analyze the death year discrepancy
Kashf al-Zunun gives two different death years: 770s (771 AH) and 670s (670 AH). It also records 671 AH. The Comprehensive Index (الفهرس الشامل) gives 671 AH. The passage suggests the correct year is 671 AH.
Discrepancies in biographical sources require cross-referencing.
4
Conclude the most likely correct year
Based on the passage, the most reliable death year is 671 AH, supported by the Comprehensive Index and mentioned in Kashf al-Zunun.

۳۸۔ مختصر لمختصر القدوري المسمى: (جوامع الكلم الشريفة على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة . للإمام تاج الدين أبي نصر عبد الرحيم بن محمد بن يونس الموصلي الشافعي، المتوفى سنة ٦٧٠هـ ، أو ٦٧١هـ، رحمه الله. وذلك بإشارة عطا ملك الجويني، أوله: «الحمد لله الأزلي الخ». اهـ ذكره صاحب كشف الظنون في موضعين، الأول في ١٦٣٢/٢، وقال: «كان آية في القدرة على الاختصار»، وهنــا جـعـل ، وفاته سنة ٧٧١هـ، إحدى وسبعين وسبعمائة، هكذا رقماً وكتابة. والموضع الثاني في ١٦٣٤/٢ ، وجعل وفاته سنة ٦٧٠ هـ، سبعين وستمائة هكذا رقماً وكتابة ، ثم كتب سنة وفاته : (٦٧١هـ)، رقماً فقط. وذكر له أصحاب الفهرس الشامل (۱) نسخة في الأحمدية في تونس (۲۲۵۹) ، وذكروا وفاته سنة ٦٧١هـ.
38. Summary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri titled: Jami' al-Kalim al-Sharifa on the Madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. By Imam Taj al-Din Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Muhammad ibn Yunus al-Mawsili al-Shafi'i, died in the year 670 AH, or 671 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. This was upon the suggestion of Ata Malik al-Juwayni. Its opening: 'Praise be to Allah, the Eternal, etc.' End. The author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned it in two places: first in 1632/2, and said: 'He was a miracle in the ability to abridge,' and here he made his death year 771 AH, one hundred and seventy-one, both in numeral and writing. And the second place in 1634/2, and he made his death year 670 AH, seventy and six hundred, both in numeral and writing, then he wrote his death year: (671 AH), only in numeral. And the authors of the Comprehensive Index (1) mentioned a copy for him in al-Ahmadiyya in Tunis (2259), and they mentioned his death year as 671 AH.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This entry describes a summary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri titled Jami' al-Kalim al-Sharifa, written by Taj al-Din al-Mawsili, a Shafi'i scholar, at the request of the vizier Ata Malik al-Juwayni. Interestingly, a Shafi'i scholar authored a text on Hanafi fiqh. The passage notes a discrepancy in his death year: Kashf al-Zunun gives two different dates (771 AH and 670 AH) but also records 671 AH. The text clarifies that the correct death year is likely 671 AH based on the index. This highlights the importance of verifying death dates in biographical sources.

Key Terms
جوامع الكلم الشريفة (Jami' al-Kalim al-Sharifa): Title of a summary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Mawsili, lit. 'Comprehensive Noble Words'.
تاج الدين الموصلي (Taj al-Din al-Mawsili): Full name: Abd al-Rahim ibn Muhammad ibn Yunus, Shafi'i scholar who wrote a Hanafi work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biographical entry with death year and source references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi, state his death year, and explain the significance of his commentary in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Khabbazi's commentary is one of many explaining the foundational Hanafi matn.

This lesson introduces a key figure in the Hanafi scholarly tradition: Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi, author of a well-known commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding who wrote these commentaries and when helps us trace the development of Hanafi fiqh and the chain of transmission of its core texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Extract the name and title of the scholar from the text: Jalal al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad al-Khabbazi.
The nisba 'al-Khabbazi' may indicate a trade or origin.
2
Determine the death year
Note the death year given: 691 AH. This places him in the 7th century AH, after the founding generations of the Hanafi school.
The text includes (Y) and broken numbers, but the consensus in Kashf al-Zunun is 691 AH.
3
Identify his work
Recognize that his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the subject of this entry.
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi matn.
4
Locate biographical sources
The text references Taj al-Tarajim and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya as sources for his biography.
These are standard Hanafi biographical dictionaries.
5
Understand the significance
Al-Khabbazi's commentary is part of a rich tradition of sharh literature that clarifies and expands upon the core text.
Knowing the author and his context helps assess the authority and perspective of the commentary.

Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Al-Wafi and Al-Saruji
Listing and describing Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary sources compiled in al-Wafi and explain the significance of al-Saruji's Sharh al-Quduri in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Wafi is a comprehensive compilation of Hanafi furu' texts, not an original work.

In this passage, we learn about two important commentaries on the foundational Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The first, by Imam al-Saruji, is a massive fifty-part commentary. The second, al-Wafi by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, is a compilation that brings together multiple core Hanafi works into one volume. Understanding these commentaries helps you see how the Hanafi school preserved and transmitted its legal heritage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentaries
Locate the two commentaries mentioned: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Saruji and al-Wafi by al-Nasafi. Note their authors and death dates (both 710 AH).
Al-Saruji was chief judge in Egypt; al-Nasafi was a major Hanafi authority.
2
Analyze the composition of al-Wafi
Read the description of al-Wafi: it combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami'ayn (al-Kabir and al-Saghir), al-Ziyadat, and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat. Understand that 'al-Jami'ayn' are works by Muhammad al-Shaybani, and 'al-Ziyadat' supplements them. Nazm al-Khilafiyyat is a poem on legal differences.
This shows the Hanafi practice of integrating multiple authoritative texts into one commentary.
3
Estimate the size of al-Saruji's commentary
The passage states it's in fifty parts (juz'), each of 20 leaves, totaling about 1000 leaves. Consider what this indicates about the depth of Hanafi commentary.
This reflects the scholarly tradition of extensive elucidation.
4
Recognize the importance of the introduction
The passage quotes from the introduction of al-Wafi, where al-Nasafi states his purpose: to compile a comprehensive work covering the major Hanafi texts. This reveals the pedagogical aim.
Such introductions are valuable for understanding the author's methodology.
5
Relate to the Hanafi curriculum
Consider how these works fit into the study sequence: Mukhtasar al-Quduri as a matn, then commentaries like al-Wafi as intermediate texts, and larger ones like al-Saruji's for advanced study.
Knowing this hierarchy helps you navigate Hanafi sources.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Al-Quduri, and it was mentioned that he was translated by Imam al-‘Ayni in Tabaqat al-Hanafiyyah, and the teacher of our teachers. Like this.
Al-Khalikhali mentioned this without any information about him. Al-Qurashi in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah, and the scholar Qasim in Taj al-Tarajim.
43- Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri (2)
By Imam al-Saruji Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn ‘Abd al-Ghani, the chief judge in Egypt (3), died in 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
Al-Kafawi mentioned it in his Kata’ib A‘lam al-Akhyar (manuscript), as transmitted by the editor of al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah (4). Al-Kafawi said that he saw on the margin of a copy of al-Jawahir that it is in fifty parts. End.
I said: A part equals 20 leaves, so the size of this commentary is a thousand leaves, and Allah knows best.
