Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
425
It is a pleasant and well-esteemed text on Hanafi furu‘. Its author combined for it Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami‘ayn al-Kabir and al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, and added to them the versification of al-Nasafi “Nazm al-Khilafiyyat” by al-Nasafi Najm al-Din ‘Umar ibn Muhammad, died in 535 AH, author of Talbat al-Talabah and al-Tafsir. This poem has 2669 verses. He added to that other issues and occurrences.
The book has many copies; see al-Fihras al-Shamil (1).
(2) It was stated in the introduction of al-Wafi:
“Praise be to Allah who bestowed upon His servants and [??] by sending His messengers and guiding His ways. Blessings and peace upon the chief of creation, Muhammad, singled out with the best of manners.
The weak servant, needy of the Loving Allah, Abu al-Barakat ‘Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi, may Allah forgive him and his parents, and be good to them and him, said: I had been thinking at the time of my leisure to compose a book comprehensive for the issues of al-Jami‘ayn and al-Ziyadat, containing what is in al-Mukhtasar and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat.
(References to Kashf al-Zunun, etc.)
(1) Among its copies is a photographed one in the Islamic University of Madinah, number 2479, containing 179 leaves, photographed from a copy of the Azhar library, written in 731 AH. This introduction was transmitted from it.”
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical listing of commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It opens with a note on al-Quduri himself, mentioning his biographical entry by al-‘Ayni. Then it lists two specific commentaries: the commentary by al-Saruji (Sharh al-Quduri) and al-Wafi by al-Nasafi. The author describes the size of al-Saruji's commentary as fifty parts (juz'), each of 20 leaves, totaling about a thousand leaves. He then turns to al-Wafi, describing it as a concise but authoritative text covering Hanafi furu‘. The key feature of al-Wafi is that it compiles material from Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami‘ al-Kabir, al-Jami‘ al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. It also includes a poetic work on points of difference (khilafiyyat) by al-Nasafi Najm al-Din. The passage concludes with a quote from the introduction of al-Wafi, where the author states his purpose of compiling a comprehensive work covering these sources. This demonstrates the scholarly practice of integrating multiple authoritative texts into a single commentary for pedagogical benefit.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational summary of Hanafi fiqh by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
الوافي (al-Wafi): A commentary by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi that combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami'ayn, al-Ziyadat, and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat.
الجامعين (al-Jami'ayn): Refers to two works by Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir, both part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
الزيادات (al-Ziyadat): A work by Muhammad al-Shaybani containing additional rulings found in the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus.
نظم الخلافيات (Nazm al-Khilafiyyat): A poetic work on differences of legal opinion by Najm al-Din al-Nasafi (d. 535 AH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the commentary al-Wafi primarily compile?
A) Only Mukhtasar al-Quduri
B) Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami'ayn, al-Ziyadat, and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat
C) The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah
D) Only the works of al-Nasafi

Key Takeaway
Al-Wafi is a concise yet comprehensive compilation of core Hanafi furu' texts, serving as a bridge between the matn and the larger Zahir al-Riwayah corpus.

Major Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Al-Kafi, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Sharh al-Quduri
A textual note listing three Hanafi commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three major Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri mentioned in the text, and state their authors and key features.

Core Idea
Three key commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: al-Kafi (with proofs), Kanz al-Daqa'iq (40,000 mas'ala), and Sharh al-Quduri by Abu al-Fadl.

This passage introduces you to the rich commentarial tradition surrounding Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab. By understanding these commentaries, you gain insight into how later scholars engaged with and transmitted fiqh knowledge. The passage highlights al-Nasafi's two works—al-Kafi (a commentary on his own al-Wafi with proofs) and Kanz al-Daqa'iq (a concise summary of al-Wafi)—and a lesser-known commentary by Abu al-Fadl referenced by Ibn al-Humam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three commentaries
List the names: al-Kafi Sharh al-Wafi, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Sharh al-Quduri by Abu al-Fadl. Note that the first two are by al-Nasafi.
Al-Kafi is a commentary on al-Wafi; Kanz al-Daqa'iq is an abridgment of al-Wafi.
2
Analyze the relationship between al-Wafi, al-Kafi, and Kanz al-Daqa'iq
Al-Wafi is a compendium combining Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Nasafi's own versification. Al-Kafi is its commentary including proofs. Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a concise summary of al-Wafi without proofs.
Al-Kafi and Kanz serve different purposes: one for depth, one for quick reference.
3
Assess the authority and circulation of each work
Kanz al-Daqa'iq is described as a very solid matn with many commentaries, widely circulated. Al-Kafi is less commonly studied but important for proofs. Sharh al-Quduri is known mainly through citations in later works like Fath al-Qadir.
The passage notes that Kanz contains 40,000 mas'ala.

٤٥ـ الكافي شرح الوافي .
للنسفي أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد المتوفى سنة ٧١٠هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وهو شرح لمؤلف الوافي نفسه، فقد قال في مقدمة الوافي: «ولــو وفقت لشرحه لأوسمته بـ: الكافي. اهـ
وقد وفقه الله تعالى لما رجاه، وألف كتاب: «الكافي»، وفيه أدلة، بخلاف الوافي.
٤٦ - كنز الدقائق .
للإمام أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود النسفي، المتوفى سنة ٧١٠ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وقد اختصره النسفي من كتابه: «الوافي»، الذي جمع فيه بين مختصر القدوري، والجامعين الكبير والصغير والزيادات لمحمد بن الحسن، ومنظومة النسفي.
وكنز الدقائق متن متين معتبر جداً عند الحنفية، ومتداول بينهم، وعليه شروح عديدة.
وقد جاء في مقدمة مؤلفه :
... لما رأيتُ الهمم مائلة إلى المختصرات، والطباع راغبةً عن المطولات، أردت أن ألخص «الوافي»، بذكر مـا عـم وقوعــه، وكثر وجوده، لتكثر فائدته، وتتوفر عائدته، فشرعت فيه، وسميته بـ: «كنز الدقائق»، وهو وإن خلا عن العويصات والمعضلات، فقد تحلَّى بمسائل الفتاوى والواقعات ...». اهـ مــن مقدمة الكنز.
والكنز مطبوع لوحده مفرداً، ومطبوع مع شروحه العديدة، مثـل تبيين الحقائق للزيلعي، والبحر الرائق لابن نجيم، وغيرهما. وعدد مسائل الكنز أربعون ألف مسألة (٤٠٠٠٠)، كما رأيت هذه الفائدة على ظهـر نسخة مخطوطة من القدوري، في المكتبة المحمودية بالمدينة المنورة.

لأبي الفضل، المتوفى قبل سنة ٧١١هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. (1)

ومؤلف النهاية شرح الهداية هو الإمام السغناقي (الصغناقي) الحسين بن علي، المتوفى في مدينة حلب سنة ٧١١هـ، وقيل: ١٤هـ. (۲)
(1) في الفوائد البهية ص ٦٢: (الحسن بن علي) وفي تاج التراجم ص ١٦٠: (الحسين).
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Furthermore, al-Nasafi is from Nasaf, a great city in the land of Bukhara, and Ibn al-Sa'ati is Baghdadi then Ba'labakki.
45 - Al-Kafi Sharh al-Wafi.
By al-Nasafi, Abu al-Barakat 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad, died 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
It is a commentary on his own book al-Wafi, for he said in the introduction to al-Wafi: 'If I were granted success in commenting on it, I would name it al-Kafi.' So Allah granted him that which he hoped, and he authored the book 'al-Kafi', which contains proofs, unlike al-Wafi.
46 - Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
By Imam Abu al-Barakat 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi, died 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
He abridged it from his book 'al-Wafi', which combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and the versification of al-Nasafi.
Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a very solid and authoritative matn among the Hanafis, widely circulated, and has many commentaries.
And in the introduction of its author: '... When I saw that aspirations incline toward abridgments and natures dislike lengthy works, I wanted to summarize al-Wafi by mentioning what is commonly occurring and frequently present, so that its benefit may increase and its usefulness be abundant. So I began it and named it Kanz al-Daqa'iq. Although it is free of abstruse and difficult matters, it is adorned with issues of fatwas and real cases ...' End quote from the introduction of al-Kanz.
Al-Kanz is published alone, and also published with its many commentaries, such as Tabyin al-Haqa'iq of al-Zayla'i, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq of Ibn Nujaym, and others. The number of issues in al-Kanz is forty thousand (40,000), as I saw this benefit on the back of a manuscript copy of al-Quduri in the Mahmudiyya Library in Medina.
47 - Sharh al-Quduri.
By Abu al-Fadl, who died before 711 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. (1)
Thus Imam Ibn al-Humam mentioned it in Fath al-Qadir, where he said in the Book of 'Itaq: 'In al-Nihaya: I saw in the handwriting of my teacher: In Sharh al-Quduri of Abu al-Fadl ...' End quote.
The author of al-Nihaya Sharh al-Hidaya is Imam al-Sighnaqi (al-Saghnagi), al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, who died in the city of Aleppo in 711 AH, and it is said: 714 AH. (2)
(1) In al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 62: (al-Hasan ibn 'Ali) and in Taj al-Tarajim p. 160: (al-Husayn).
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage comes from the chapter on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It lists three important works: al-Kafi Sharh al-Wafi, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Sharh al-Quduri by Abu al-Fadl. The first two are by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, a major Hanafi scholar. Al-Kafi is a commentary on his own al-Wafi, distinguished by including proofs (adilla). Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a concise summary of al-Wafi, containing 40,000 mas'ala, and is highly regarded as a matn with numerous commentaries. The third work, Sharh al-Quduri by Abu al-Fadl, is mentioned by Ibn al-Humam but the author's full identity is ambiguous, with sources giving al-Hasan or al-Husayn. This passage illustrates the textual hierarchy and reliance on these works in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
الوافي (al-Wafi): A Hanafi fiqh compendium by al-Nasafi that combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat of Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with al-Nasafi's own versification.
كنز الدقائق (Kanz al-Daqa'iq): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by al-Nasafi, abridged from al-Wafi, containing 40,000 mas'ala. It is considered a reliable matn with many commentaries.
الجامع الكبير (al-Jami' al-Kabir): One of the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah compiled by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Knowing the commentarial hierarchy — al-Wafi, al-Kafi, Kanz al-Daqa'iq — equips you to navigate Hanafi legal literature with scholarly precision.

Kanz al-Daqaiq, an abridgement with 40,000 issues, became the focus of numerous commentaries and versifications.

This passage is a biographical list from a work on Hanafi jurisprudence. Introducing al-Manhaj: A Concise Compendium of Hanafi Fiqh
Biographical entry introducing a concise Hanafi fiqh work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three primary sources combined in al-Manhaj and explain the attribution discrepancy between Kashf al-Zunun and Hadiyat al-'Arifin.

Core Idea
Al-Manhaj combines al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Tahawi's works, and al-Quduri into one concise Hanafi manual.

This passage introduces a valuable Hanafi fiqh work, al-Manhaj 'ala Madhhab al-Hanafiyyah, authored by al-Qadi Najm al-Din. It is a concise compilation that brings together three foundational texts of the Hanafi school. Understanding this work helps us appreciate how later scholars synthesized earlier authoritative sources for easier memorization and study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its author
The passage introduces al-Manhaj 'ala Madhhab al-Hanafiyyah by al-Qadi Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-'Adim al-Halabi (d. 734 AH). Note the full name and death date.
Two different death dates are mentioned; we will compare them later.
2
List the three sources combined
The text states it combines al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, the works of al-Tahawi, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Identify each source's author and significance.
These are all major Hanafi texts from the early period.
3
Recognize the style and purpose
The work is described as having the most concise expression and clearest exposition. Understand that its purpose is to provide an accessible summary for students and practitioners.
Such compilations were common for memorization and quick reference.
4
Analyze the attribution discrepancy
Kashf al-Zunun attributes the work to Umar ibn Muhammad (d. 734 AH), while Hadiyat al-'Arifin attributes it to a different Ibn al-'Adim (d. 660 AH). Compare the two possibilities and note the need for verification.
The passage advises caution: 'let the author be verified between them.'
5
Assess the importance of this work
Al-Manhaj is a teaching tool that encapsulates essential rulings. Recognizing its sources helps you trace the genealogy of Hanafi texts.
This biographical note contextualizes later commentaries that reference al-Manhaj.

٥١ـ المنهاج على مذهب الحنفية . للقاضي نجم الدين عمر بن محمد بن العديم الحلبي، المتوفى سنة ٧٣٤ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. وهو مشتمل على أصول وفروع ، جمع فيـه بـيـن الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن، وبين تصنيف الطحاوي، والقدوري، بأوجز لفظ، وأوضح بيان كما وصفه بذلك صاحب كشف الظنون (۱). (۲) وأما صاحب هدية العارفين ، فسماه: «منهاج في الأصول والفروع على مذهب أبي حنيفة، ونسبه لابن العديم عمر بن القاضي مجد الدين أحمد بن هبة الله ، المولود سنة ٥٨٦هـ، والمتوفى سنة ٦٦٠ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى (۳) ، وعليه فليحرر المؤلف منهما.
51. Al-Manhaj 'ala Madhhab al-Hanafiyyah. By al-Qadi Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-'Adim al-Halabi, died 734 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It contains principles and branches, combining between al-Jami' al-Saghir of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and the work of al-Tahawi, and al-Quduri, with the most concise expression and clearest exposition, as described by the author of Kashf al-Zunun (1). (2) As for the author of Hadiyat al-'Arifin, he named it: 'Manhaj fi al-Usul wa al-Furu' 'ala Madhhab Abi Hanifah', and attributed it to Ibn al-'Adim Umar ibn al-Qadi Majd al-Din Ahmad ibn Hibat Allah, born 586 AH, died 660 AH, may Allah have mercy on him (3). Therefore, let the author be verified between them.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry introducing al-Manhaj 'ala Madhhab al-Hanafiyyah, a Hanafi fiqh work by al-Qadi Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-'Adim al-Halabi (d. 734 AH). The work is described as combining three major Hanafi texts: al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the works of al-Tahawi, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It is known for its concise expression and clarity. The passage also notes a discrepancy in attribution: while Kashf al-Zunun attributes it to Ibn al-'Adim (d. 734 AH), Hadiyat al-'Arifin names a different Ibn al-'Adim, Umar ibn al-Qadi Majd al-Din Ahmad ibn Hibat Allah (d. 660 AH). The text advises verifying the correct author.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A foundational Hanafi fiqh work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a key Hanafi matn.
المنهاج (al-Manhaj): The concise Hanafi fiqh work described, combining multiple earlier texts.
الطحاوي (al-Tahawi): Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Tahawi, a leading Hanafi scholar whose fiqh works are referenced.

Checkpoint
According to Kashf al-Zunun, what is the death year of the author of al-Manhaj?
A) 660 AH
B) 734 AH
C) 586 AH
D) 634 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Manhaj is a concise Hanafi fiqh manual synthesizing three major texts, serving as an efficient learning tool for students.
